gita_verse:1.1	<center><big>धृतराष्ट्र उवाच<br><br>धर्मक्षेत्रे कुरुक्षेत्रे समवेता युयुत्सवः।<br><br>मामकाः पाण्डवाश्चैव किमकुर्वत सञ्जय।।1.1।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dhṛitarāśhtra uvācha<br>dharma-kṣhetre kuru-kṣhetre samavetā yuyutsavaḥ<br>māmakāḥ pāṇḍavāśhchaiva kimakurvata sañjaya<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Dhṛtarāṣṭra said: O Sanjaya, what did my sons and the sons of Pandu do when they assembled on the sacred field of Kurukshetra, eager for battle?<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Dhritarashtra said, "What did my people and the sons of Pandu do when they had assembled together, eager for battle, on the holy plain of Kurukshetra, O Sanjaya?"<br><br>[sound:gita_1_1.mp3]
gita_verse:1.2	<center><big>सञ्जय उवाच<br><br>दृष्ट्वा तु पाण्डवानीकं व्यूढं दुर्योधनस्तदा।<br><br>आचार्यमुपसङ्गम्य राजा वचनमब्रवीत्।।1.2।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sañjaya uvācha<br>dṛiṣhṭvā tu pāṇḍavānīkaṁ vyūḍhaṁ duryodhanastadā<br>āchāryamupasaṅgamya rājā vachanamabravīt<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Sanjaya said: But then, seeing the army of the Pandavas in battle array, King Duryodhana approached the teacher, Drona, and spoke.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Sanjaya said: Having seen the army of the Pandavas drawn up in battle array, King Duryodhana approached his teacher, Drona, and spoke these words.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_2.mp3]
gita_verse:1.3	<center><big>पश्यैतां पाण्डुपुत्राणामाचार्य महतीं चमूम्।<br><br>व्यूढां द्रुपदपुत्रेण तव शिष्येण धीमता।।1.3।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>paśhyaitāṁ pāṇḍu-putrāṇām āchārya mahatīṁ chamūm<br>vyūḍhāṁ drupada-putreṇa tava śhiṣhyeṇa dhīmatā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O teacher, behold this vast army of the sons of Pandu, arrayed for battle by the intelligent disciple of Drupada.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Behold, O Teacher! This mighty army of the sons of Pandu, arrayed by the son of Drupada, thy wise disciple.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_3.mp3]
gita_verse:1.4-6	<center><big>अत्र शूरा महेष्वासा भीमार्जुनसमा युधि।<br><br>युयुधानो विराटश्च द्रुपदश्च महारथः।।1.4।।<br> <br><br>धृष्टकेतुश्चेकितानः काशिराजश्च वीर्यवान्।<br><br>पुरुजित्कुन्तिभोजश्च शैब्यश्च नरपुङ्गवः।।1.5।।<br> <br><br>युधामन्युश्च विक्रान्त उत्तमौजाश्च वीर्यवान्।<br><br>सौभद्रो द्रौपदेयाश्च सर्व एव महारथाः।।1.6।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>atra śhūrā maheṣhvāsā bhīmārjuna-samā yudhi<br>yuyudhāno virāṭaśhcha drupadaśhcha mahā-rathaḥ<br><br>dhṛiṣhṭaketuśhchekitānaḥ kāśhirājaśhcha vīryavān<br>purujit kuntibhojaśhcha śhaibyaśhcha nara-puṅgavaḥ<br>yudhāmanyuśhcha vikrānta uttamaujāśhcha vīryavān<br><br>saubhadro draupadeyāśhcha sarva eva mahā-rathāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Here are the heroes wielding great bows, who in battle are peers of Bhima and Arjuna: Yuyudhana (Satyaki) and Virata, and the maharatha (great chariot-rider) Drupada; Dhrstaketu, Cekitana, and the valiant king of Kasi (Varanasi); Purujit, Kuntibhoja, and Saibya, the choicest of men; And the valiant Yudhamanyu, and the chivalrous Uttamaujas; the son of Subhadra (Abhimanyu) and the sons of Draupadi—all of them are, indeed, maharathas.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Here are heroes, mighty archers, equal in battle to Bhima and Arjuna, Yuyudhana (Satyaki), Virata, and Drupada—all mighty warriors. Dhrishtaketu, Chekitana, the valiant king of Kasi, Purujit, Kuntibhoja, and Saibya—the best of men. The strong Yudhamanyu and the brave Uttamaujas, the son of Subhadra (Abhimanyu, the son of Subhadra and Arjuna), and the sons of Draupadi, all of them great charioteers (great heroes)."<br><br>[sound:gita_1_4-6.mp3]
gita_verse:1.7	<center><big>अस्माकं तु विशिष्टा ये तान्निबोध द्विजोत्तम।<br><br>नायका मम सैन्यस्य संज्ञार्थं तान्ब्रवीमि ते।।1.7।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>asmākaṁ tu viśhiṣhṭā ye tānnibodha dwijottama<br>nāyakā mama sainyasya sanjñārthaṁ tānbravīmi te<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But, O best among the Brahmanas, please be appraised of those who are foremost among us, the founders of my army. I speak of them to you by way of illustration.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Know also, O best among the twice-born! the names of those who are the most distinguished amongst ourselves, the leaders of my army; these I name to you for your information.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_7.mp3]
gita_verse:1.8	<center><big>भवान्भीष्मश्च कर्णश्च कृपश्च समितिञ्जयः।<br><br>अश्वत्थामा विकर्णश्च सौमदत्तिस्तथैव च।।1.8।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>bhavānbhīṣhmaśhcha karṇaśhcha kṛipaśhcha samitiñjayaḥ<br>aśhvatthāmā vikarṇaśhcha saumadattis tathaiva cha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>(They are): Your venerable self, Bhisma, Karna, and Krpa, who is ever victorious in battle; Asvatthama, Vikarna, Saumadatti, and Jayadratha.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>"Thou thyself, Bhishma, Karna, Kripa, the victorious in war, Asvatthama, Vikarna, and Bhurisrava, the son of Somadatta—all these are ready for battle."<br><br>[sound:gita_1_8.mp3]
gita_verse:1.9	<center><big>अन्ये च बहवः शूरा मदर्थे त्यक्तजीविताः।<br><br>नानाशस्त्रप्रहरणाः सर्वे युद्धविशारदाः।।1.9।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>anye cha bahavaḥ śhūrā madarthe tyaktajīvitāḥ<br>nānā-śhastra-praharaṇāḥ sarve yuddha-viśhāradāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>There are many heroes who have dedicated their lives to me, possessing various kinds of weapons and missiles, all of whom are skilled in battle.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>And also many other heroes, ready to give up their lives for my sake, armed with various weapons and missiles, all well-skilled in battle.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_9.mp3]
gita_verse:1.10	<center><big>अपर्याप्तं तदस्माकं बलं भीष्माभिरक्षितम्।<br><br>पर्याप्तं त्विदमेतेषां बलं भीमाभिरक्षितम्।।1.10।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>aparyāptaṁ tadasmākaṁ balaṁ bhīṣhmābhirakṣhitam<br>paryāptaṁ tvidameteṣhāṁ balaṁ bhīmābhirakṣhitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Therefore, our army, under the complete protection of Bhisma and others, is limitless. But this army of the enemies, under the protection of Bhima and others, is limited.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Our army, marshalled by Bhishma, is insufficient, whereas theirs, marshalled by Bhima, is sufficient.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_10.mp3]
gita_verse:1.11	<center><big>अयनेषु च सर्वेषु यथाभागमवस्थिताः।<br><br>भीष्ममेवाभिरक्षन्तु भवन्तः सर्व एव हि।।1.11।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ayaneṣhu cha sarveṣhu yathā-bhāgamavasthitāḥ<br>bhīṣhmamevābhirakṣhantu bhavantaḥ sarva eva hi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>However, venerable sirs, all of you without exception, while occupying all the positions in the different directions as allotted to you respectively, please protect Bhisma in particular.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Therefore, do all of you, stationed in your respective positions in the several divisions of the army, protect Bhishma alone.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_11.mp3]
gita_verse:1.12	<center><big>तस्य संजनयन्हर्षं कुरुवृद्धः पितामहः।<br><br>सिंहनादं विनद्योच्चैः शङ्खं दध्मौ प्रतापवान्।।1.12।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tasya sañjanayan harṣhaṁ kuru-vṛiddhaḥ pitāmahaḥ<br>siṁha-nādaṁ vinadyochchaiḥ śhaṅkhaṁ dadhmau pratāpavān<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The valiant grandfather, the eldest of the Kurus, loudly sounding a lion's roar, blew the conch to raise his (Duryodhana's) spirits.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>His glorious grandsire, the oldest of the Kauravas, roared like a lion to cheer Duryodhana and blew his conch.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_12.mp3]
gita_verse:1.13	<center><big>ततः शङ्खाश्च भेर्यश्च पणवानकगोमुखाः।<br><br>सहसैवाभ्यहन्यन्त स शब्दस्तुमुलोऽभवत्।।1.13।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tataḥ śhaṅkhāśhcha bheryaśhcha paṇavānaka-gomukhāḥ<br>sahasaivābhyahanyanta sa śhabdastumulo ’bhavat<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Just immediately afterward, conch shells, kettledrums, tabors, trumpets, and cow-horns blared forth, creating a tumultuous sound.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Then, suddenly, conches, kettledrums, tabors, drums, and cow horns blared forth from the Kaurava side, and the sound was tremendous.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_13.mp3]
gita_verse:1.14	<center><big>ततः श्वेतैर्हयैर्युक्ते महति स्यन्दने स्थितौ।<br><br>माधवः पाण्डवश्चैव दिव्यौ शङ्खौ प्रदध्मतुः।।1.14।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tataḥ śhvetairhayairyukte mahati syandane sthitau<br>mādhavaḥ pāṇḍavaśhchaiva divyau śhaṅkhau pradadhmatuḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Then Madhava (Krishna) and the son of Pandu (Arjuna), stationed in their magnificent chariot with white horses yoked to it, blew their divine conchs loudly.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Then, Madhava (Krishna) and the son of Pandu (Arjuna), seated in the magnificent chariot yoked with white horses, blew divine conches.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_14.mp3]
gita_verse:1.15	<center><big>पाञ्चजन्यं हृषीकेशो देवदत्तं धनंजयः।<br><br>पौण्ड्रं दध्मौ महाशङ्खं भीमकर्मा वृकोदरः।।1.15।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>pāñchajanyaṁ hṛiṣhīkeśho devadattaṁ dhanañjayaḥ<br>pauṇḍraṁ dadhmau mahā-śhaṅkhaṁ bhīma-karmā vṛikodaraḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Hrsikesa (Krsna) blew the conch Pancajanya; Dhananjaya (Arjuna) blew the conch Devadatta; and Vrkodara (Bhima) of terrible deeds blew the great conch Paundra.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Hrishikesha blew the Panchajanya, Arjuna blew the Devadatta, and Bhima, the wolf-bellied doer of terrible deeds, blew the great conch Paundra.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_15.mp3]
gita_verse:1.16-18	<center><big>अनन्तविजयं राजा कुन्तीपुत्रो युधिष्ठिरः।<br><br>नकुलः सहदेवश्च सुघोषमणिपुष्पकौ।।1.16।।<br> <br><br>काश्यश्च परमेष्वासः शिखण्डी च महारथः।<br><br>धृष्टद्युम्नो विराटश्च सात्यकिश्चापराजितः।।1.17।।<br> <br><br>द्रुपदो द्रौपदेयाश्च सर्वशः पृथिवीपते।<br><br>सौभद्रश्च महाबाहुः शङ्खान्दध्मुः पृथक्पृथक्।।1.18।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>anantavijayaṁ rājā kuntī-putro yudhiṣhṭhiraḥ<br>nakulaḥ sahadevaśhcha sughoṣha-maṇipuṣhpakau<br><br>kāśhyaśhcha parameṣhvāsaḥ śhikhaṇḍī cha mahā-rathaḥ<br>dhṛiṣhṭadyumno virāṭaśhcha sātyakiśh chāparājitaḥ<br><br>drupado draupadeyāśhcha sarvaśhaḥ pṛithivī-pate<br>saubhadraśhcha mahā-bāhuḥ śhaṅkhāndadhmuḥ pṛithak pṛithak<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>King Yudhisthira, son of Kunti, blew the Anantavijaya; Nakula and Sahadeva blew the Sughosa and the Manipuspaka, respectively. And the King of Kashi, wielding a great bow, and the great chariot-rider Sikhandin, Dhrstadyumna, Virata, and Satyaki the unconquered; Drupada and the sons of Draupadi, as well as the mighty-armed son of Subhadra, all of them together, O king, blew their respective conchs.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>King Yudhishthira, the son of Kunti, blew the Anantavijaya; Nakula and Sahadeva blew the Sughosha and the Manipushpaka. The king of Kasi, an excellent archer, Sikhandi, the mighty car-warrior, Dhrishtadyumna, Virata, and Satyaki, the unconquered. Drupada and the sons of Draupadi, O Lord of the Earth, and the son of Subhadra, the mighty-armed, blew their conches each separately.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_16-18.mp3]
gita_verse:1.19	<center><big>स घोषो धार्तराष्ट्राणां हृदयानि व्यदारयत्।<br><br>नभश्च पृथिवीं चैव तुमुलो व्यनुनादयन्।।1.19।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sa ghoṣho dhārtarāṣhṭrāṇāṁ hṛidayāni vyadārayat<br>nabhaśhcha pṛithivīṁ chaiva tumulo nunādayan<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That tremendous sound pierced the hearts of the sons of Dhrtarastra as it reverberated through the sky and the earth.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The tumultuous sound rent the hearts of Dhritarashtra's party, reverberating through both heaven and earth.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_19.mp3]
gita_verse:1.20	<center><big>अथ व्यवस्थितान् दृष्ट्वा धार्तराष्ट्रान्कपिध्वजः।<br><br>प्रवृत्ते शस्त्रसंपाते धनुरुद्यम्य पाण्डवः।।1.20।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>atha vyavasthitān dṛiṣhṭvā dhārtarāṣhṭrān kapi-dhwajaḥ<br>pravṛitte śhastra-sampāte dhanurudyamya pāṇḍavaḥ<br>hṛiṣhīkeśhaṁ tadā vākyam idam āha mahī-pate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O King, thereafter, seeing Dhrtarastra's men standing in their positions, with all the weapons ready for action, the son of Pandu, Arjuna, who had the insignia of Hanuman on his chariot-flag, raised his bow and said the following to Hrsikesa.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Then, seeing the people of Dhritarashtra's party standing arrayed and the discharge of weapons about to begin, Arjuna, the son of Pandu whose ensign was a monkey, took up his bow and said the following to Krishna, O Lord of the Earth.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_20.mp3]
gita_verse:1.21-22	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाच<br><br>हृषीकेशं तदा वाक्यमिदमाह महीपते।<br><br>सेनयोरुभयोर्मध्ये रथं स्थापय मेऽच्युत।।1.21।।<br> <br><br>यावदेतान्निरीक्षेऽहं योद्धुकामानवस्थितान्।<br><br>कैर्मया सह योद्धव्यमस्मिन्रणसमुद्यमे।।1.22।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>senayor ubhayor madhye rathaṁ sthāpaya me ’chyuta<br><br>yāvadetān nirīkṣhe ’haṁ yoddhu-kāmān avasthitān<br>kairmayā saha yoddhavyam asmin raṇa-samudyame<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O Acyuta, please place my chariot between both the armies." Until I survey those who stand intent on fighting and those who are about to engage in battle with me in this impending war.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O Krishna, place my chariot in the middle between the two armies, so that I may behold those who stand here, desirous to fight, and know with whom I must fight when the battle is about to commence." Arjuna said, "O Krishna, place my chariot in the middle between the two armies, so that I may behold those who stand here, desirous to fight, and know with whom I must fight when the battle is about to commence."<br><br>[sound:gita_1_21-22.mp3]
gita_verse:1.23	<center><big>योत्स्यमानानवेक्षेऽहं य एतेऽत्र समागताः।<br><br>धार्तराष्ट्रस्य दुर्बुद्धेर्युद्धे प्रियचिकीर्षवः।।1.23।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yotsyamānān avekṣhe ’haṁ ya ete ’tra samāgatāḥ<br>dhārtarāṣhṭrasya durbuddher yuddhe priya-chikīrṣhavaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>These who have assembled here and want to accomplish in the war what is dear to the perverted son of Dhrtarastra, I find them to be intent on fighting.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>For I desire to observe those who are assembled here to fight, wishing to please in battle the evil-minded Duryodhana—the son of Dhritarashtra.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_23.mp3]
gita_verse:1.24	<center><big>संजय उवाच<br><br>एवमुक्तो हृषीकेशो गुडाकेशेन भारत।<br><br>सेनयोरुभयोर्मध्ये स्थापयित्वा रथोत्तमम्।।1.24।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sañjaya uvācha<br>evam ukto hṛiṣhīkeśho guḍākeśhena bhārata<br>senayor ubhayor madhye sthāpayitvā rathottamam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Sanjaya said, "O scion of the line of Bharata, Hrishikesa, being told so by Gudakesa (Arjuna), placed the excellent chariot between the two armies, in front of Bhishma and Drona as well as all the rulers of the earth, and said, 'O Partha, behold these assembled Kurus!'"<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Sanjaya said, Thus addressed by Arjuna, Krishna stationed the best of chariots, O Dhritarashtra, in the midst of the two armies.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_24.mp3]
gita_verse:1.25	<center><big>भीष्मद्रोणप्रमुखतः सर्वेषां च महीक्षिताम्।<br><br>उवाच पार्थ पश्यैतान्समवेतान्कुरूनिति।।1.25।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>bhīṣhma-droṇa-pramukhataḥ sarveṣhāṁ cha mahī-kṣhitām<br>uvācha pārtha paśhyaitān samavetān kurūn iti<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Sanjaya said, "O scion of the line of Bharata (Dhrtarashtra), Hrsikesa, being told so by Gudakesa (Arjuna), placed the excellent chariot between the two armies, in front of Bhisma and Drona as well as all the rulers of the earth, and said, 'O Partha (Arjuna), behold these assembled people of the Kuru dynasty.'"<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>In front of Bhishma and Drona, and all the rulers of the earth, he said: "O Arjuna, son of Pritha, behold these Kurus gathered together."<br><br>[sound:gita_1_25.mp3]
gita_verse:1.26	<center><big>तत्रापश्यत्स्थितान्पार्थः पितृ़नथ पितामहान्।<br><br>आचार्यान्मातुलान्भ्रातृ़न्पुत्रान्पौत्रान्सखींस्तथा।।1.26।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tatrāpaśhyat sthitān pārthaḥ pitṝīn atha pitāmahān<br>āchāryān mātulān bhrātṝīn putrān pautrān sakhīṁs tathā<br>śhvaśhurān suhṛidaśh chaiva senayor ubhayor api<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Then Arjuna saw, marshalled among both the armies, his uncles, grandfathers, teachers, maternal uncles, brothers, cousins, sons, grandsons, comrades, fathers-in-law, and friends.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Then, Arjuna (son of Pritha) saw there (in the armies) stationed fathers, grandfathers, teachers, maternal uncles, brothers, sons, grandsons, and friends.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_26.mp3]
gita_verse:1.27	<center><big>श्वशुरान्सुहृदश्चैव सेनयोरुभयोरपि।<br><br>तान्समीक्ष्य स कौन्तेयः सर्वान्बन्धूनवस्थितान्।।1.27।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tān samīkṣhya sa kaunteyaḥ sarvān bandhūn avasthitān<br>kṛipayā parayāviṣhṭo viṣhīdann idam abravīt<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The son of Kunti, Arjuna, seeing all those relatives arrayed there, became overwhelmed by supreme compassion and sorrowfully said this:<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He saw fathers-in-law and friends in both the armies. The son of Kunti, Arjuna, seeing all those kinsmen thus standing arrayed, spoke sorrowfully, deeply filled with pity.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_27.mp3]
gita_verse:1.28	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाच<br><br>कृपया परयाऽऽविष्टो विषीदन्निदमब्रवीत्।<br><br>दृष्ट्वेमं स्वजनं कृष्ण युयुत्सुं समुपस्थितम्।।1.28।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>dṛiṣhṭvemaṁ sva-janaṁ kṛiṣhṇa yuyutsuṁ samupasthitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O Krsna, seeing these relatives and friends who have assembled here with the intention of fighting, my limbs become languid and my mouth becomes completely dry."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O Krishna, seeing my kinsmen arrayed here, eager to fight,<br><br>[sound:gita_1_28.mp3]
gita_verse:1.29-31	<center><big>सीदन्ति मम गात्राणि मुखं च परिशुष्यति।<br><br>वेपथुश्च शरीरे मे रोमहर्षश्च जायते।।1.29।।<br> <br><br>गाण्डीवं स्रंसते हस्तात्त्वक्चैव परिदह्यते।<br><br>न च शक्नोम्यवस्थातुं भ्रमतीव च मे मनः।।1.30।।<br> <br><br>निमित्तानि च पश्यामि विपरीतानि केशव।<br><br>न च श्रेयोऽनुपश्यामि हत्वा स्वजनमाहवे।।1.31।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sīdanti mama gātrāṇi mukhaṁ cha pariśhuṣhyati<br>vepathuśh cha śharīre me roma-harṣhaśh cha jāyate<br><br>gāṇḍīvaṁ sraṁsate hastāt tvak chaiva paridahyate<br>na cha śhaknomy avasthātuṁ bhramatīva cha me manaḥ<br><br>nimittāni cha paśhyāmi viparītāni keśhava<br>na cha śhreyo ’nupaśhyāmi hatvā sva-janam āhave<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>And there is trembling in my body, and my hair stands on end; the Gandiva (bow) slips from my hand and my skin burns intensely. Moreover, O Kesava (Krishna), I am not able to stand firmly, and my mind seems to be whirling. And I observe the omens to be adverse. Besides, I do not see any good to be derived from killing my own people in battle. O Krsna, I do not hanker after victory, nor even a kingdom, nor pleasures.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>My limbs fail, my mouth is parched, my body quivers, and my hair stands on end. The Gandiva slips from my hand, and my skin burns all over; I am unable to stand, and my mind is reeling, as it were. And I see ill omens, O Kesava. I do not see any good in slaying my kinsmen in battle.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_29-31.mp3]
gita_verse:1.32-33	<center><big>न काङ्क्षे विजयं कृष्ण न च राज्यं सुखानि च।<br><br>किं नो राज्येन गोविन्द किं भोगैर्जीवितेन वा।।1.32।।<br> <br><br>येषामर्थे काङ्क्षितं नो राज्यं भोगाः सुखानि च।<br><br>त इमेऽवस्थिता युद्धे प्राणांस्त्यक्त्वा धनानि च।।1.33।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na kāṅkṣhe vijayaṁ kṛiṣhṇa na cha rājyaṁ sukhāni cha<br>kiṁ no rājyena govinda kiṁ bhogair jīvitena vā<br><br>yeṣhām arthe kāṅkṣhitaṁ no rājyaṁ bhogāḥ sukhāni cha<br>ta ime ’vasthitā yuddhe prāṇāṁs tyaktvā dhanāni cha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Govinda! What need do we have of a kingdom, or what need of enjoyments and livelihood? Those for whom kingdom, enjoyments, and pleasures are desired by us—such as teachers, uncles, fathers-in-law, grandsons, brothers-in-law, as well as relatives—those very ones stand arrayed for battle, risking their lives and wealth. - O Govinda! What need do we have of a kingdom, or what need of enjoyments and livelihood? Those for whom kingdom, enjoyments, and pleasures are desired by us—such as teachers, uncles, fathers-in-law, grandsons, brothers-in-law, as well as relatives—those very ones stand arrayed for battle, risking their lives and wealth.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>I desire not victory, O Krishna, nor kingdom, nor pleasures.<br>What use is dominion to us, O Krishna, or pleasures or even life? gita_verse:1.34-35	<center><big>आचार्याः पितरः पुत्रास्तथैव च पितामहाः।<br><br>मातुलाः श्चशुराः पौत्राः श्यालाः सम्बन्धिनस्तथा।।1.34।।<br> <br><br>एतान्न हन्तुमिच्छामि घ्नतोऽपि मधुसूदन।<br><br>अपि त्रैलोक्यराज्यस्य हेतोः किं नु महीकृते।।1.35।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>āchāryāḥ pitaraḥ putrās tathaiva cha pitāmahāḥ<br>mātulāḥ śhvaśhurāḥ pautrāḥ śhyālāḥ sambandhinas tathā<br><br>etān na hantum ichchhāmi ghnato ’pi madhusūdana<br>api trailokya-rājyasya hetoḥ kiṁ nu mahī-kṛite<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>- O Govinda! What need do we have of a kingdom, or what need of enjoyments and livelihood? Those for whom kingdom, enjoyments, and pleasures are desired by us—such as teachers, uncles, fathers-in-law, grandsons, brothers-in-law, as well as relatives—those very ones stand arrayed for battle, risking their lives and wealth. O Madhusudana, even if I am killed, I do not want to kill these even for the sake of a kingdom extending across the three worlds; let alone doing so for the earth!<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Teachers, fathers, sons, and grandfathers, maternal uncles, fathers-in-law, grandsons, brothers-in-law, and other relatives— These I do not wish to kill, O Krishna, even though they kill me, for the sake of dominion over the three worlds; leave alone killing them for the sake of the earth."<br><br>[sound:gita_1_34-35.mp3]
gita_verse:1.36-37	<center><big>निहत्य धार्तराष्ट्रान्नः का प्रीतिः स्याज्जनार्दन।<br><br>पापमेवाश्रयेदस्मान्हत्वैतानाततायिनः।।1.36।।<br> <br><br>तस्मान्नार्हा वयं हन्तुं धार्तराष्ट्रान्स्वबान्धवान्।<br><br>स्वजनं हि कथं हत्वा सुखिनः स्याम माधव।।1.37।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>nihatya dhārtarāṣhṭrān naḥ kā prītiḥ syāj janārdana<br>pāpam evāśhrayed asmān hatvaitān ātatāyinaḥ<br><br>tasmān nārhā vayaṁ hantuṁ dhārtarāṣhṭrān sa-bāndhavān <br>sva-janaṁ hi kathaṁ hatvā sukhinaḥ syāma mādhava<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Janardana, what happiness will we gain by killing the sons of Dhrtarastra? We will only incur sin by killing these wrongdoers. Therefore, it is not proper for us to kill the sons of Dhrtarastra, who are our own relatives. For, O Madhava, how can we be happy by killing our kinsmen?<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>By killing these sons of Dhritarashtra, what pleasure could be ours, O Janardana? Only sin would accrue to us from killing these felons. Therefore, we should not kill the sons of Dhritarashtra, our relatives; for how can we be happy by killing our own kin, O Madhava (Krishna)?<br><br>[sound:gita_1_36-37.mp3]
gita_verse:1.38-39	<center><big>यद्यप्येते न पश्यन्ति लोभोपहतचेतसः।<br><br>कुलक्षयकृतं दोषं मित्रद्रोहे च पातकम्।।1.38।।<br> <br><br>कथं न ज्ञेयमस्माभिः पापादस्मान्निवर्तितुम्।<br><br>कुलक्षयकृतं दोषं प्रपश्यद्भिर्जनार्दन।।1.39।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yady apy ete na paśhyanti lobhopahata-chetasaḥ<br>kula-kṣhaya-kṛitaṁ doṣhaṁ mitra-drohe cha pātakam<br><br>kathaṁ na jñeyam asmābhiḥ pāpād asmān nivartitum<br>kula-kṣhaya-kṛitaṁ doṣhaṁ prapaśhyadbhir janārdana<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>- O Janardana, although these people, whose hearts have become perverted by greed, do not see the evil arising from destroying the family and sinning in hostility towards friends, yet how can we, who clearly see the evil arising from destroying the family, remain unaware of the need to abstain from this sin? - O Janardana, although these people, whose hearts have become perverted by greed, do not see the evil arising from destroying the family and sinning in hostility towards friends, yet how can we, who clearly see the evil arising from destroying the family, remain unaware of the need to abstain from this sin?<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Though they, with intelligence overpowered by greed, see no evil in the destruction of families and no sin in hostility to friends, Why should we not, who clearly see the evil in the destruction of families, learn to turn away from this sin, O Janardana (Krishna)?<br><br>[sound:gita_1_38-39.mp3]
gita_verse:1.40	<center><big>कुलक्षये प्रणश्यन्ति कुलधर्माः सनातनाः।<br><br>धर्मे नष्टे कुलं कृत्स्नमधर्मोऽभिभवत्युत।।1.40।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kula-kṣhaye praṇaśhyanti kula-dharmāḥ sanātanāḥ<br>dharme naṣhṭe kulaṁ kṛitsnam adharmo ’bhibhavaty uta<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>From the ruin of the family, the traditional rites and duties are totally destroyed. When rites and duties are destroyed, vice overwhelms the entire family.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>In the destruction of a family, the immemorial religious rites of that family perish; on the destruction of spirituality, impiety indeed, overwhelms the whole family.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_40.mp3]
gita_verse:1.41	<center><big>अधर्माभिभवात्कृष्ण प्रदुष्यन्ति कुलस्त्रियः।<br><br>स्त्रीषु दुष्टासु वार्ष्णेय जायते वर्णसङ्करः।।1.41।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>adharmābhibhavāt kṛiṣhṇa praduṣhyanti kula-striyaḥ<br>strīṣhu duṣhṭāsu vārṣhṇeya jāyate varṇa-saṅkaraḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Krishna, when vice predominates, the women of the family become corrupt. O descendant of the Vrsnis, when women become corrupted, it results in the intermingling of castes.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>O Krishna, by the prevalence of impiety, the women of the family become corrupt; and, when women are corrupted, O Varshenya (descendant of Vrishni), intermingling of castes arises.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_41.mp3]
gita_verse:1.42	<center><big>सङ्करो नरकायैव कुलघ्नानां कुलस्य च।<br><br>पतन्ति पितरो ह्येषां लुप्तपिण्डोदकक्रियाः।।1.42।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>saṅkaro narakāyaiva kula-ghnānāṁ kulasya cha<br>patanti pitaro hy eṣhāṁ lupta-piṇḍodaka-kriyāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>And the intermingling in the family leads the ruiners of the family verily into hell. gita_verse:1.43	<center><big>दोषैरेतैः कुलघ्नानां वर्णसङ्करकारकैः।<br><br>उत्साद्यन्ते जातिधर्माः कुलधर्माश्च शाश्वताः।।1.43।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>doṣhair etaiḥ kula-ghnānāṁ varṇa-saṅkara-kārakaiḥ<br>utsādyante jāti-dharmāḥ kula-dharmāśh cha śhāśhvatāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Due to the misdeeds of the ruiners of the family, which cause intermingling of castes, the traditional rites and duties of the castes and families are destroyed.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>By these evil deeds of the destroyers of the family, which cause confusion of castes, the eternal religious rites of the caste and the family are destroyed.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_43.mp3]
gita_verse:1.44	<center><big>उत्सन्नकुलधर्माणां मनुष्याणां जनार्दन।<br><br>नरकेऽनियतं वासो भवतीत्यनुशुश्रुम।।1.44।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>utsanna-kula-dharmāṇāṁ manuṣhyāṇāṁ janārdana<br>narake ‘niyataṁ vāso bhavatītyanuśhuśhruma<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Janardana, we have heard that living in hell is inevitable for those whose family duties are destroyed.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>We have heard, O Janardana, that those men in whose families the religious practices have been destroyed are inevitably destined to dwell in hell for an unknown period.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_44.mp3]
gita_verse:1.45-46	<center><big>अहो बत महत्पापं कर्तुं व्यवसिता वयम्।<br><br>यद्राज्यसुखलोभेन हन्तुं स्वजनमुद्यताः।।1.45।।<br> <br><br>यदि मामप्रतीकारमशस्त्रं शस्त्रपाणयः।<br><br>धार्तराष्ट्रा रणे हन्युस्तन्मे क्षेमतरं भवेत्।।1.46।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>aho bata mahat pāpaṁ kartuṁ vyavasitā vayam<br>yad rājya-sukha-lobhena hantuṁ sva-janam udyatāḥ<br><br>yadi mām apratīkāram aśhastraṁ śhastra-pāṇayaḥ<br>dhārtarāṣhṭrā raṇe hanyus tan me kṣhemataraṁ bhavet<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>What a pity that we have resolved to commit a great sin, eager to kill our own kith and kin out of greed for the pleasures of a kingdom! If, in this battle, the sons of Dhrtarastra, armed with weapons, kill me, who am non-resistant and unarmed, that will be more beneficial for me.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Alas! We are involved in a great sin, for we are prepared to kill our kinsmen, out of greed for the pleasures of a kingdom. If the sons of Dhritarashtra, with weapons in hand, should slay me in battle, unresisting and unarmed, that would be better for me.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_45-46.mp3]
gita_verse:1.47	<center><big>सञ्जय उवाच<br><br>एवमुक्त्वाऽर्जुनः संख्ये रथोपस्थ उपाविशत्।<br><br>विसृज्य सशरं चापं शोकसंविग्नमानसः।।1.47।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sañjaya uvācha<br>evam uktvārjunaḥ saṅkhye rathopastha upāviśhat<br>visṛijya sa-śharaṁ chāpaṁ śhoka-saṁvigna-mānasaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Sanjaya narrated: Having said so, Arjuna, with a mind afflicted by sorrow, sat down on the chariot in the midst of the battle, casting aside his bow along with the arrows.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Sanjaya said, Having thus spoken in the midst of the battlefield, Arjuna cast away his bow and arrow and, his mind overwhelmed with sorrow, sat down on the seat of the chariot.<br><br>[sound:gita_1_47.mp3]
gita_verse:2.1	<center><big>सञ्जय उवाच<br><br>तं तथा कृपयाऽविष्टमश्रुपूर्णाकुलेक्षणम्।<br><br>विषीदन्तमिदं वाक्यमुवाच मधुसूदनः।।2.1।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sañjaya uvācha<br>taṁ tathā kṛipayāviṣhṭamaśhru pūrṇākulekṣhaṇam<br>viṣhīdantamidaṁ vākyam uvācha madhusūdanaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Sanjaya said: To him who had been filled with pity, whose eyes were filled with tears and showed distress, and who was sorrowing, Madhusudana uttered these words.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Sanjaya said: To him, who was thus overcome with pity, despondent, with eyes full of tears and agitated, Madhusudana (the destroyer of Madhu) or Krishna spoke these words.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_1.mp3]
gita_verse:2.2	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाच<br><br>कुतस्त्वा कश्मलमिदं विषमे समुपस्थितम्।<br><br>अनार्यजुष्टमस्वर्ग्यमकीर्तिकरमर्जुन।।2.2।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī bhagavān uvācha<br>kutastvā kaśhmalamidaṁ viṣhame samupasthitam<br>anārya-juṣhṭamaswargyam akīrti-karam arjuna<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "O Arjuna, in this perilous place, whence has this impurity come to you, entertained by unenlightened persons, which does not lead to heaven and brings infamy?"<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "From whence has this perilous strait come upon you, this dejection which is unworthy of you, disgraceful, and which will close the gates of heaven upon you, O Arjuna?"<br><br>[sound:gita_2_2.mp3]
gita_verse:2.3	<center><big>क्लैब्यं मा स्म गमः पार्थ नैतत्त्वय्युपपद्यते।<br><br>क्षुद्रं हृदयदौर्बल्यं त्यक्त्वोत्तिष्ठ परन्तप।।2.3।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>klaibyaṁ mā sma gamaḥ pārtha naitat tvayyupapadyate<br>kṣhudraṁ hṛidaya-daurbalyaṁ tyaktvottiṣhṭha parantapa<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Partha, do not yield to unmanliness. gita_verse:2.4	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाच<br><br>कथं भीष्ममहं संख्ये द्रोणं च मधुसूदन।<br><br>इषुभिः प्रतियोत्स्यामि पूजार्हावरिसूदन।।2.4।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>kathaṁ bhīṣhmam ahaṁ sankhye droṇaṁ cha madhusūdana<br>iṣhubhiḥ pratiyotsyāmi pūjārhāvari-sūdana<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O Madhusudana, O destroyer of enemies, how can I fight with arrows in battle against Bhisma and Drona, who are worthy of adoration?"<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O Madhusudana, how can I fight in battle with arrows against Bhishma and Drona, who are worthy of being worshipped, O destroyer of enemies?"<br><br>[sound:gita_2_4.mp3]
gita_verse:2.5	<center><big>गुरूनहत्वा हि महानुभावान्<br><br>श्रेयो भोक्तुं भैक्ष्यमपीह लोके।<br><br>हत्वार्थकामांस्तु गुरूनिहैव<br><br>भुञ्जीय भोगान् रुधिरप्रदिग्धान्।।2.5।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>gurūnahatvā hi mahānubhāvān<br>śhreyo bhoktuṁ bhaikṣhyamapīha loke<br>hatvārtha-kāmāṁstu gurūnihaiva<br>bhuñjīya bhogān rudhira-pradigdhān<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Rather than killing the noble-minded elders, it is better in this world to live even on alms. gita_verse:2.6	<center><big>न चैतद्विद्मः कतरन्नो गरीयो<br><br>यद्वा जयेम यदि वा नो जयेयुः।<br><br>यानेव हत्वा न जिजीविषाम<br><br>स्तेऽवस्थिताः प्रमुखे धार्तराष्ट्राः।।2.6।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na chaitadvidmaḥ kataranno garīyo<br>yadvā jayema yadi vā no jayeyuḥ<br>yāneva hatvā na jijīviṣhāmas<br>te ’vasthitāḥ pramukhe dhārtarāṣhṭrāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>We do not know which is better for us, whether we shall win or they shall conquer us. gita_verse:2.7	<center><big>कार्पण्यदोषोपहतस्वभावः<br><br>पृच्छामि त्वां धर्मसंमूढचेताः।<br><br>यच्छ्रेयः स्यान्निश्िचतं ब्रूहि तन्मे<br><br>शिष्यस्तेऽहं शाधि मां त्वां प्रपन्नम्।।2.7।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kārpaṇya-doṣhopahata-svabhāvaḥ<br>pṛichchhāmi tvāṁ dharma-sammūḍha-chetāḥ<br>yach-chhreyaḥ syānniśhchitaṁ brūhi tanme<br>śhiṣhyaste ’haṁ śhādhi māṁ tvāṁ prapannam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>With my nature overpowered by weak commiseration, my mind bewildered about duty, I supplicate You. gita_verse:2.12	<center><big>न त्वेवाहं जातु नासं न त्वं नेमे जनाधिपाः।<br><br>न चैव न भविष्यामः सर्वे वयमतः परम्।।2.12।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na tvevāhaṁ jātu nāsaṁ na tvaṁ neme janādhipāḥ<br>na chaiva na bhaviṣhyāmaḥ sarve vayamataḥ param<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But certainly it is not a fact that I did not exist at any time; nor you, nor these rulers of men. gita_verse:2.13	<center><big>देहिनोऽस्मिन्यथा देहे कौमारं यौवनं जरा।<br><br>तथा देहान्तरप्राप्तिर्धीरस्तत्र न मुह्यति।।2.13।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dehino ’smin yathā dehe kaumāraṁ yauvanaṁ jarā<br>tathā dehāntara-prāptir dhīras tatra na muhyati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>As boyhood, youth, and decrepitude are to an embodied being in this present body, so is the acquisition of another body. gita_verse:2.14	<center><big>मात्रास्पर्शास्तु कौन्तेय शीतोष्णसुखदुःखदाः।<br><br>आगमापायिनोऽनित्यास्तांस्तितिक्षस्व भारत।।2.14।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>mātrā-sparśhās tu kaunteya śhītoṣhṇa-sukha-duḥkha-dāḥ<br>āgamāpāyino ’nityās tans-titikṣhasva bhārata<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But the contacts of the organs with the objects are the producers of cold and heat, happiness, and sorrow. gita_verse:2.15	<center><big>यं हि न व्यथयन्त्येते पुरुषं पुरुषर्षभ।<br><br>समदुःखसुखं धीरं सोऽमृतत्वाय कल्पते।।2.15।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yaṁ hi na vyathayantyete puruṣhaṁ puruṣharṣhabha<br>sama-duḥkha-sukhaṁ dhīraṁ so ’mṛitatvāya kalpate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Arjuna, who is foremost among men, verily, the person whom these do not torment, the wise man to whom sorrow and happiness are the same—he is fit for immortality.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That firm man, whom surely these afflictions do not, O chief among men, to whom pleasure and pain are the same, is fit for attaining immortality.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_15.mp3]
gita_verse:2.16	<center><big>नासतो विद्यते भावो नाभावो विद्यते सतः।<br><br>उभयोरपि दृष्टोऽन्तस्त्वनयोस्तत्त्वदर्शिभिः।।2.16।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>nāsato vidyate bhāvo nābhāvo vidyate sataḥ<br>ubhayorapi dṛiṣhṭo ’nta stvanayos tattva-darśhibhiḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>There is no being of the unreal; the real has no non-existence. Yet, the nature of both has been realized by the seers of Truth.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The unreal has no being; there is no non-being of the real; the truth about both has been seen by the knowers of the truth (or the seers of the essence).<br><br>[sound:gita_2_16.mp3]
gita_verse:2.17	<center><big>अविनाशि तु तद्विद्धि येन सर्वमिदं ततम्।<br><br>विनाशमव्ययस्यास्य न कश्चित् कर्तुमर्हति।।2.17।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>avināśhi tu tadviddhi yena sarvam idaṁ tatam<br>vināśham avyayasyāsya na kaśhchit kartum arhati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But know that to be indestructible by which all this is pervaded. No one can cause the destruction of that, the Imperishable.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_17.mp3]
gita_verse:2.18	<center><big>अन्तवन्त इमे देहा नित्यस्योक्ताः शरीरिणः।<br><br>अनाशिनोऽप्रमेयस्य तस्माद्युध्यस्व भारत।।2.18।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>antavanta ime dehā nityasyoktāḥ śharīriṇaḥ<br>anāśhino ’prameyasya tasmād yudhyasva bhārata<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>These destructible bodies are said to belong to the everlasting, indestructible, and indeterminable embodied One. Therefore, fight, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_18.mp3]
gita_verse:2.19	<center><big>य एनं वेत्ति हन्तारं यश्चैनं मन्यते हतम्।<br><br>उभौ तौ न विजानीतो नायं हन्ति न हन्यते।।2.19।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ya enaṁ vetti hantāraṁ yaśh chainaṁ manyate hatam<br>ubhau tau na vijānīto nāyaṁ hanti na hanyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who thinks of this One as the killer, and he who thinks of this One as the one being killed, both of them do not know. This One neither kills nor is It killed.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who takes the Self to be the slayer and he who thinks it is slain, neither of them knows. It does not slay, nor is it slain.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_19.mp3]
gita_verse:2.20	<center><big>न जायते म्रियते वा कदाचि<br><br>न्नायं भूत्वा भविता वा न भूयः।<br><br>अजो नित्यः शाश्वतोऽयं पुराणो<br><br>न हन्यते हन्यमाने शरीरे।।2.20।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na jāyate mriyate vā kadāchin<br>nāyaṁ bhūtvā bhavitā vā na bhūyaḥ<br>ajo nityaḥ śhāśhvato ’yaṁ purāṇo<br>na hanyate hanyamāne śharīre<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Never is this One born, nor does It ever die; nor, having come into existence, does It cease to be. This One is birthless, eternal, undecaying, and ancient; It is not killed when the body is killed.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>It is not born, nor does it ever die; after having been, it again does not cease to be; unborn, eternal, changeless, and ancient, it is not killed when the body is killed.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_20.mp3]
gita_verse:2.21	<center><big>वेदाविनाशिनं नित्यं य एनमजमव्ययम्।<br><br>कथं स पुरुषः पार्थ कं घातयति हन्ति कम्।।2.21।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>vedāvināśhinaṁ nityaṁ ya enam ajam avyayam<br>kathaṁ sa puruṣhaḥ pārtha kaṁ ghātayati hanti kam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Partha, he who knows this One as indestructible, eternal, birthless, and undecaying—how can that person kill, or cause to be killed, whom?<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Whoever knows it to be indestructible, eternal, unborn, and inexhaustible, how can that person slay, O Arjuna, or cause to be slain?<br><br>[sound:gita_2_21.mp3]
gita_verse:2.22	<center><big>वासांसि जीर्णानि यथा विहाय<br><br>नवानि गृह्णाति नरोऽपराणि।<br><br>तथा शरीराणि विहाय जीर्णा<br><br>न्यन्यानि संयाति नवानि देही।।2.22।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>vāsānsi jīrṇāni yathā vihāya<br>navāni gṛihṇāti naro ’parāṇi<br>tathā śharīrāṇi vihāya jīrṇānya<br>nyāni sanyāti navāni dehī<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>As after rejecting worn-out clothes, a man takes up other new ones, likewise, after rejecting worn-out bodies, the embodied one unites with other new ones.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Just as a man casts off worn-out clothes and puts on new ones, so too the embodied Self casts off worn-out bodies and enters others that are new.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_22.mp3]
gita_verse:2.23	<center><big>नैनं छिन्दन्ति शस्त्राणि नैनं दहति पावकः।<br><br>न चैनं क्लेदयन्त्यापो न शोषयति मारुतः।।2.23।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>nainaṁ chhindanti śhastrāṇi nainaṁ dahati pāvakaḥ<br>na chainaṁ kledayantyāpo na śhoṣhayati mārutaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Weapons cannot cut It, fire cannot burn It, water cannot moisten It, and air cannot dry It.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Weapons cannot cut it, fire cannot burn it, water cannot wet it, wind cannot dry it.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_23.mp3]
gita_verse:2.24	<center><big>अच्छेद्योऽयमदाह्योऽयमक्लेद्योऽशोष्य एव च।<br><br>नित्यः सर्वगतः स्थाणुरचलोऽयं सनातनः।।2.24।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>achchhedyo ’yam adāhyo ’yam akledyo ’śhoṣhya eva cha<br>nityaḥ sarva-gataḥ sthāṇur achalo ’yaṁ sanātanaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>It cannot be cut, burned, moistened, or dried up; it is eternal, omnipresent, stationary, unmoving, and unchanging.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>This Self cannot be cut, burned, wetted, nor dried up; it is eternal, all-pervasive, stable, immovable, and ancient.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_24.mp3]
gita_verse:2.25	<center><big>अव्यक्तोऽयमचिन्त्योऽयमविकार्योऽयमुच्यते।<br><br>तस्मादेवं विदित्वैनं नानुशोचितुमर्हसि।।2.25।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>avyakto ’yam achintyo ’yam avikāryo ’yam uchyate<br>tasmādevaṁ viditvainaṁ nānuśhochitum arhasi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>It is said that This is unmanifest; This is inconceivable; This is unchangeable. Therefore, having known This thus, you ought not to grieve.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>This Self is said to be unmanifested, unthinkable, and unchangeable. Therefore, knowing this to be so, you should not grieve.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_25.mp3]
gita_verse:2.26	<center><big>अथ चैनं नित्यजातं नित्यं वा मन्यसे मृतम्।<br><br>तथापि त्वं महाबाहो नैवं शोचितुमर्हसि।।2.26।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>atha chainaṁ nitya-jātaṁ nityaṁ vā manyase mṛitam<br>tathāpi tvaṁ mahā-bāho naivaṁ śhochitum arhasi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>On the other hand, if you think this One is born continually or constantly dies, even then, O mighty-armed one, you should not grieve.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But even if thou thinkest of It as constantly being born and constantly dying, even then, O mighty-armed one, thou shouldst not grieve.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_26.mp3]
gita_verse:2.27	<center><big>जातस्य हि ध्रुवो मृत्युर्ध्रुवं जन्म मृतस्य च।<br><br>तस्मादपरिहार्येऽर्थे न त्वं शोचितुमर्हसि।।2.27।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>jātasya hi dhruvo mṛityur dhruvaṁ janma mṛitasya cha<br>tasmād aparihārye ’rthe na tvaṁ śhochitum arhasi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For the death of anyone born is certain, and the rebirth of the dead is certain. Therefore, you should not grieve over an inevitable fact.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>For the born, death is certain, and for the dead, birth is certain; therefore, you should not grieve over the inevitable.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_27.mp3]
gita_verse:2.28	<center><big>अव्यक्तादीनि भूतानि व्यक्तमध्यानि भारत।<br><br>अव्यक्तनिधनान्येव तत्र का परिदेवना।।2.28।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>avyaktādīni bhūtāni vyakta-madhyāni bhārata<br>avyakta-nidhanānyeva tatra kā paridevanā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O descendant of Bharata, all beings remain unmanifested in the beginning; they become manifested in the middle. After death, they certainly become unmanifested. What lamentation can there be for them?<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Beings are unmanifest in their beginning, manifest in their middle state, O Arjuna, and unmanifest again in their end. What is there to grieve about?<br><br>[sound:gita_2_28.mp3]
gita_verse:2.29	<center><big>आश्चर्यवत्पश्यति कश्चिदेन<br><br>माश्चर्यवद्वदति तथैव चान्यः।<br><br>आश्चर्यवच्चैनमन्यः श्रृणोति<br><br>श्रुत्वाप्येनं वेद न चैव कश्चित्।।2.29।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>āśhcharya-vat paśhyati kaśhchid enan<br>āśhcharya-vad vadati tathaiva chānyaḥ<br>āśhcharya-vach chainam anyaḥ śhṛiṇoti<br>śhrutvāpyenaṁ veda na chaiva kaśhchit<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Someone visualizes it as a wonder; someone else talks of it as a wonder; someone else hears of it as a wonder; and yet someone else does not even realize it after hearing about it.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>One sees this (the Self) as a wonder; another speaks of it as a wonder; another hears of it as a wonder; yet, having heard, none understands it at all.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_29.mp3]
gita_verse:2.30	<center><big>देही नित्यमवध्योऽयं देहे सर्वस्य भारत।<br><br>तस्मात्सर्वाणि भूतानि न त्वं शोचितुमर्हसि।।2.30।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dehī nityam avadhyo ’yaṁ dehe sarvasya bhārata<br>tasmāt sarvāṇi bhūtāni na tvaṁ śhochitum arhasi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O descendant of Bharata, this embodied Self existing in everyone's body can never be killed; therefore, you ought not to grieve for all these beings.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>This indweller in the body of everyone is ever indestructible, O Arjuna; therefore, you should not grieve for any creature.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_30.mp3]
gita_verse:2.31	<center><big>स्वधर्ममपि चावेक्ष्य न विकम्पितुमर्हसि।<br><br>धर्म्याद्धि युद्धाछ्रेयोऽन्यत्क्षत्रियस्य न विद्यते।।2.31।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>swa-dharmam api chāvekṣhya na vikampitum arhasi<br>dharmyāddhi yuddhāch chhreyo ’nyat kṣhatriyasya na vidyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Even considering your own duty, you should not waver, since there is nothing better for a Ksatriya than a righteous battle.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Further, having regard to your duty, you should not waver, for there is nothing higher for a Kshatriya than a righteous war.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_31.mp3]
gita_verse:2.32	<center><big>यदृच्छया चोपपन्नं स्वर्गद्वारमपावृतम्।<br><br>सुखिनः क्षत्रियाः पार्थ लभन्ते युद्धमीदृशम्।।2.32।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yadṛichchhayā chopapannaṁ swarga-dvāram apāvṛitam<br>sukhinaḥ kṣhatriyāḥ pārtha labhante yuddham īdṛiśham<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O son of Partha, happy are the Kshatriyas who come across such a battle, which presents itself unsought and is an open gate to heaven.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Happy are the Kshatriyas, O Arjuna! who are called to fight in such a battle that comes of its own accord as an open door to heaven.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_32.mp3]
gita_verse:2.33	<center><big>अथ चैत्त्वमिमं धर्म्यं संग्रामं न करिष्यसि।<br><br>ततः स्वधर्मं कीर्तिं च हित्वा पापमवाप्स्यसि।।2.33।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>atha chet tvam imaṁ dharmyaṁ saṅgrāmaṁ na kariṣhyasi<br>tataḥ sva-dharmaṁ kīrtiṁ cha hitvā pāpam avāpsyasi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>On the other hand, if you do not fight this righteous battle, then you will incur sin, forsaking your own duty and fame.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But if you will not fight this righteous war, then having abandoned your own duty and reputation, you will incur sin.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_33.mp3]
gita_verse:2.34	<center><big>अकीर्तिं चापि भूतानि कथयिष्यन्ति तेऽव्ययाम्।<br><br>संभावितस्य चाकीर्तिर्मरणादतिरिच्यते।।2.34।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>akīrtiṁ chāpi bhūtāni<br>kathayiṣhyanti te ’vyayām<br>sambhāvitasya chākīrtir<br>maraṇād atirichyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>People also will speak of your unending infamy, and to an honored person, infamy is worse than death.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>People will also recount your everlasting dishonor; and for one who has been honored, dishonor is worse than death.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_34.mp3]

gita_verse:2.36	<center><big>अवाच्यवादांश्च बहून् वदिष्यन्ति तवाहिताः।<br><br>निन्दन्तस्तव सामर्थ्यं ततो दुःखतरं नु किम्।।2.36।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>avāchya-vādānśh cha bahūn vadiṣhyanti tavāhitāḥ<br>nindantastava sāmarthyaṁ tato duḥkhataraṁ nu kim<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>And your enemies will speak many indecent words while denigrating your power. gita_verse:2.37	<center><big>हतो वा प्राप्स्यसि स्वर्गं जित्वा वा भोक्ष्यसे महीम्।<br><br>तस्मादुत्तिष्ठ कौन्तेय युद्धाय कृतनिश्चयः।।2.37।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>hato vā prāpsyasi swargaṁ jitvā vā bhokṣhyase mahīm<br>tasmād uttiṣhṭha kaunteya yuddhāya kṛita-niśhchayaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Either by being killed, you will attain heaven, or by winning, you will enjoy the earth. Therefore, O Arjuna, rise up with determination to fight.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Slain, you will obtain heaven; victorious, you will enjoy the earth; therefore, stand up, O son of Kunti, resolved to fight.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_37.mp3]
gita_verse:2.38	<center><big>सुखदुःखे समे कृत्वा लाभालाभौ जयाजयौ।<br><br>ततो युद्धाय युज्यस्व नैवं पापमवाप्स्यसि।।2.38।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sukha-duḥkhe same kṛitvā lābhālābhau jayājayau<br>tato yuddhāya yujyasva naivaṁ pāpam avāpsyasi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Treating happiness and sorrow, gain and loss, and conquest and defeat with equanimity, then engage in battle. Thus, you will not incur sin.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Having made pleasure and pain, gain and loss, victory and defeat equal, engage in battle for the sake of battle; thus, you shall not incur sin.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_38.mp3]
gita_verse:2.39	<center><big>एषा तेऽभिहिता सांख्ये बुद्धिर्योगे त्विमां श्रृणु।<br><br>बुद्ध्यायुक्तो यया पार्थ कर्मबन्धं प्रहास्यसि।।2.39।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>eṣhā te ’bhihitā sānkhye<br>buddhir yoge tvimāṁ śhṛiṇu<br>buddhyā yukto yayā pārtha<br>karma-bandhaṁ prahāsyasi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Partha, this wisdom has been imparted to you from the standpoint of Self-realization. But listen to this wisdom from the standpoint of Yoga, endowed with which, you will get rid of the bondage of action.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>This, which has been taught to you, is wisdom concerning Sankhya. Now listen to wisdom concerning Yoga, endowed with which, O Arjuna, you shall cast off the bonds of action.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_39.mp3]
gita_verse:2.40	<center><big>नेहाभिक्रमनाशोऽस्ति प्रत्यवायो न विद्यते।<br><br>स्वल्पमप्यस्य धर्मस्य त्रायते महतो भयात्।।2.40।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>nehābhikrama-nāśho ’sti pratyavāyo na vidyate<br>svalpam apyasya dharmasya trāyate mahato bhayāt<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Here, there is no waste of effort; nor is there any harm. Even a little of this righteousness saves one from great fear.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>In this, there is no loss of effort, nor is there any harm produced, nor any transgression. Even a little of this knowledge protects one from great fear.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_40.mp3]
gita_verse:2.41	<center><big>व्यवसायात्मिका बुद्धिरेकेह कुरुनन्दन।<br><br>बहुशाखा ह्यनन्ताश्च बुद्धयोऽव्यवसायिनाम्।।2.41।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>vyavasāyātmikā buddhir ekeha kuru-nandana<br>bahu-śhākhā hyanantāśh cha buddhayo ’vyavasāyinām<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O scion of the Kuru dynasty, in this there is a single, one-pointed conviction. gita_verse:2.42-43	<center><big>यामिमां पुष्पितां वाचं प्रवदन्त्यविपश्चितः।<br><br>वेदवादरताः पार्थ नान्यदस्तीति वादिनः।।2.42।।<br> <br><br>कामात्मानः स्वर्गपरा जन्मकर्मफलप्रदाम्।<br><br>क्रियाविशेषबहुलां भोगैश्वर्यगतिं प्रति।।2.43।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yāmimāṁ puṣhpitāṁ vāchaṁ pravadanty-avipaśhchitaḥ<br>veda-vāda-ratāḥ pārtha nānyad astīti vādinaḥ<br> kāmātmānaḥ swarga-parā janma-karma-phala-pradām<br>kriyā-viśheṣha-bahulāṁ bhogaiśhwarya-gatiṁ prati<br><br>kāmātmānaḥ svarga-parā <br><br> janma-karma-phala-pradām<br><br> kriyā-viśeṣa-bahulāṁ<br><br> bhogaiśvarya-gatiṁ prati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O son of Prtha, those undiscerning people who utter this flowery talk, which promises birth as a result of rites and duties, and is full of various special rites meant for the attainment of enjoyment and affluence, remain engrossed in the utterances of the Vedas and declare that nothing else exists; their minds are full of desires and they have heaven as their goal. O son of Prtha, those undiscerning people who utter this flowery talk, which promises birth as a result of rites and duties, and is full of various special rites meant for the attainment of enjoyment and affluence, remain engrossed in the utterances of the Vedas and declare that nothing else exists; their minds are full of desires and they have heaven as their goal.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The unwise, taking pleasure in the eulogizing words of the Vedas, utter flowery speech, saying, "There is nothing else," O Arjuna. Full of desires, with heaven as their goal, (they speak words that are directed to ends) leading to new births as the result of their works, and prescribe various methods abounding in specific actions, for the attainment of pleasure and power.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_42-43.mp3]
gita_verse:2.44	<center><big>भोगैश्वर्यप्रसक्तानां तयापहृतचेतसाम्।<br><br>व्यवसायात्मिका बुद्धिः समाधौ न विधीयते।।2.44।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>bhogaiśwvarya-prasaktānāṁ tayāpahṛita-chetasām<br>vyavasāyātmikā buddhiḥ samādhau na vidhīyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One-pointed conviction does not become established in the minds of those who delight in enjoyment and affluence, and whose intellects are carried away by it.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>For those who are attached to pleasure and power, whose minds are drawn away by such teachings, their determinate reason is not formed which is steadily bent on meditation and Samadhi (superconscious state).<br><br>[sound:gita_2_44.mp3]
gita_verse:2.45	<center><big>त्रैगुण्यविषया वेदा निस्त्रैगुण्यो भवार्जुन।<br><br>निर्द्वन्द्वो नित्यसत्त्वस्थो निर्योगक्षेम आत्मवान्।।2.45।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>trai-guṇya-viṣhayā vedā nistrai-guṇyo bhavārjuna<br>nirdvandvo nitya-sattva-stho niryoga-kṣhema ātmavān<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Arjuna, the Vedas [Meaning only the portion dealing with rites and duties (karma-kanda).] have the three qualities as their object. You become free from worldliness, free from the pairs of duality, ever-poised in the quality of sattva, without (desire for) acquisition and protection, and self-collected.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Vedas deal with the three attributes; be thou above these three attributes. O Arjuna, free yourself from the pairs of opposites and ever remain in the quality of Sattva, freed from acquisition and preservation, and be established in the Self.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_45.mp3]
gita_verse:2.46	<center><big>यावानर्थ उदपाने सर्वतः संप्लुतोदके।<br><br>तावान्सर्वेषु वेदेषु ब्राह्मणस्य विजानतः।।2.46।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yāvān artha udapāne sarvataḥ samplutodake<br>tāvānsarveṣhu vedeṣhu brāhmaṇasya vijānataḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>A Brahmana with realization has that much utility in all the Vedas as a person has in a well when there is a flood all around.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>To the Brahmana who has known the Self, all the Vedas are of as much use as a reservoir of water would be in a place where there is a flood.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_46.mp3]
gita_verse:2.47	<center><big>कर्मण्येवाधिकारस्ते मा फलेषु कदाचन।<br><br>मा कर्मफलहेतुर्भूर्मा ते सङ्गोऽस्त्वकर्मणि।।2.47।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>karmaṇy-evādhikāras te mā phaleṣhu kadāchana<br>mā karma-phala-hetur bhūr mā te saṅgo ’stvakarmaṇi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Your right is only to act, not to the results. Do not be the cause of the results of action. Do not have any inclination towards inaction.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Your right is only to work, but not to its results; do not let the results of action be your motive, nor let your attachment be to inaction.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_47.mp3]
gita_verse:2.48	<center><big>योगस्थः कुरु कर्माणि सङ्गं त्यक्त्वा धनञ्जय।<br><br>सिद्ध्यसिद्ध्योः समो भूत्वा समत्वं योग उच्यते।।2.48।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yoga-sthaḥ kuru karmāṇi saṅgaṁ tyaktvā dhanañjaya<br>siddhy-asiddhyoḥ samo bhūtvā samatvaṁ yoga uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>By being established in Yoga, O Dhananjaya (Arjuna), undertake actions, casting off attachment and remaining equanimous in success and failure. Equanimity is called Yoga.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Perform action, O Arjuna, being steadfast in Yoga, abandoning attachment and balanced in success and failure; evenness of mind is called Yoga.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_48.mp3]
gita_verse:2.49	<center><big>दूरेण ह्यवरं कर्म बुद्धियोगाद्धनञ्जय।<br><br>बुद्धौ शरणमन्विच्छ कृपणाः फलहेतवः।।2.49।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dūreṇa hy-avaraṁ karma buddhi-yogād dhanañjaya<br>buddhau śharaṇam anvichchha kṛipaṇāḥ phala-hetavaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Dhananjaya, indeed, action is inferior to the yoga of wisdom. Take refuge in wisdom. Those who thirst for rewards are pitiable.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Far lower than the Yoga of wisdom is action, O Arjuna. Seek thou refuge in wisdom; wretched are those whose motive is the fruit.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_49.mp3]
gita_verse:2.50	<center><big>बुद्धियुक्तो जहातीह उभे सुकृतदुष्कृते।<br><br>तस्माद्योगाय युज्यस्व योगः कर्मसु कौशलम्।।2.50।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>buddhi-yukto jahātīha ubhe sukṛita-duṣhkṛite<br>tasmād yogāya yujyasva yogaḥ karmasu kauśhalam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Possessed of wisdom, one rejects here both virtue and vice. Therefore, devote yourself to (Karma-) yoga; for yoga is skilfulness in action.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Endowed with wisdom and evenness of mind, one casts off in this life both good and evil deeds; therefore, devote yourself to Yoga; Yoga is skill in action.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_50.mp3]
gita_verse:2.51	<center><big>कर्मजं बुद्धियुक्ता हि फलं त्यक्त्वा मनीषिणः।<br><br>जन्मबन्धविनिर्मुक्ताः पदं गच्छन्त्यनामयम्।।2.51।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>karma-jaṁ buddhi-yuktā hi phalaṁ tyaktvā manīṣhiṇaḥ<br>janma-bandha-vinirmuktāḥ padaṁ gachchhanty-anāmayam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For those devoted to wisdom, they become enlightened men by giving up the fruits of their actions, and thus they reach a state beyond evil, having been freed from the bondage of birth.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The wise, possessing knowledge, having abandoned the fruits of their actions, and being freed from the bonds of birth, go to the place which is beyond all evil.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_51.mp3]
gita_verse:2.52	<center><big>यदा ते मोहकलिलं बुद्धिर्व्यतितरिष्यति।<br><br>तदा गन्तासि निर्वेदं श्रोतव्यस्य श्रुतस्य च।।2.52।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yadā te moha-kalilaṁ buddhir vyatitariṣhyati<br>tadā gantāsi nirvedaṁ śhrotavyasya śhrutasya cha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>When your mind goes beyond the turbidity of delusion, then you will acquire dispassion for what has to be heard and what has already been heard.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>When your intellect passes beyond the mire of delusion, then you will attain indifference to what has been heard and what has yet to be heard.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_52.mp3]
gita_verse:2.53	<center><big>श्रुतिविप्रतिपन्ना ते यदा स्थास्यति निश्चला।<br><br>समाधावचला बुद्धिस्तदा योगमवाप्स्यसि।।2.53।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhruti-vipratipannā te yadā sthāsyati niśhchalā<br>samādhāv-achalā buddhis tadā yogam avāpsyasi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>When your mind, which has become bewildered by hearing, becomes unshakable and steadfast in the Self, then you will attain Yoga that arises from discrimination.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>When your intellect, which is perplexed by the Vedic texts you have read, stands immovable and steady in the Self, then you will attain Self-realization.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_53.mp3]
gita_verse:2.54	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाच<br><br>स्थितप्रज्ञस्य का भाषा समाधिस्थस्य केशव।<br><br>स्थितधीः किं प्रभाषेत किमासीत व्रजेत किम्।।2.54।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>sthita-prajñasya kā bhāṣhā samādhi-sthasya keśhava<br>sthita-dhīḥ kiṁ prabhāṣheta kim āsīta vrajeta kim<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O Kesava, what is the description of a man of steady wisdom who is self-absorbed? How does one of steady wisdom speak, how do they sit, and how do they walk?"<br><br>[sound:gita_2_54.mp3]
gita_verse:2.55	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाच<br><br>प्रजहाति यदा कामान् सर्वान् पार्थ मनोगतान्।<br><br>आत्मन्येवात्मना तुष्टः स्थितप्रज्ञस्तदोच्यते।।2.55।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī bhagavān uvācha<br>prajahāti yadā kāmān sarvān pārtha mano-gatān<br>ātmany-evātmanā tuṣhṭaḥ sthita-prajñas tadochyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed One said, "O Partha, when one fully renounces all the desires that have entered the mind and remains satisfied in the Self alone, then he is called a man of steady wisdom."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "When a man completely casts off, O Arjuna, all the desires of the mind and is satisfied in the Self by the Self, then he is said to be one of steady wisdom."<br><br>[sound:gita_2_55.mp3]
gita_verse:2.56	<center><big>दुःखेष्वनुद्विग्नमनाः सुखेषु विगतस्पृहः।<br><br>वीतरागभयक्रोधः स्थितधीर्मुनिरुच्यते।।2.56।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>duḥkheṣhv-anudvigna-manāḥ sukheṣhu vigata-spṛihaḥ<br>vīta-rāga-bhaya-krodhaḥ sthita-dhīr munir uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That monk is called a man of steady wisdom when his mind is unperturbed even in sorrow, he is free from longing for delights, and has gone beyond attachment, fear, and anger.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He whose mind is not shaken by adversity, who does not long for pleasures, and is free from attachment, fear, and anger, is called a sage of steady wisdom.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_56.mp3]
gita_verse:2.57	<center><big>यः सर्वत्रानभिस्नेहस्तत्तत्प्राप्य शुभाशुभम्।<br><br>नाभिनन्दति न द्वेष्टि तस्य प्रज्ञा प्रतिष्ठिता।।2.57।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yaḥ sarvatrānabhisnehas tat tat prāpya śhubhāśhubham<br>nābhinandati na dveṣhṭi tasya prajñā pratiṣhṭhitā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The wisdom of that person remains established who has no attachment to anything anywhere, who neither welcomes nor rejects anything, whatever good or bad, when they come across it.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who is everywhere without attachment, upon encountering anything good or bad, neither rejoices nor hastens; his wisdom is firm.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_57.mp3]
gita_verse:2.58	<center><big>यदा संहरते चायं कूर्मोऽङ्गानीव सर्वशः।<br><br>इन्द्रियाणीन्द्रियार्थेभ्यस्तस्य प्रज्ञा प्रतिष्ठिता।।2.58।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yadā sanharate chāyaṁ kūrmo ’ṅgānīva sarvaśhaḥ<br>indriyāṇīndriyārthebhyas tasya prajñā pratiṣhṭhitā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>And when one fully withdraws their senses from the objects of the senses, just as a tortoise withdraws its limbs, then their wisdom remains established.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>When, like the tortoise which withdraws all its limbs on all sides, he withdraws his senses from the sense-objects, then his wisdom becomes steady.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_58.mp3]
gita_verse:2.59	<center><big>विषया विनिवर्तन्ते निराहारस्य देहिनः।<br><br>रसवर्जं रसोऽप्यस्य परं दृष्ट्वा निवर्तते।।2.59।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>viṣhayā vinivartante nirāhārasya dehinaḥ<br>rasa-varjaṁ raso ’pyasya paraṁ dṛiṣhṭvā nivartate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The objects recede from an abstinent person, except for the taste for them. Even this taste falls away after realization of the Absolute.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The objects of the senses turn away from the abstinent man, leaving the longing behind; but his longing also turns away upon seeing the Supreme.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_59.mp3]
gita_verse:2.60	<center><big>यततो ह्यपि कौन्तेय पुरुषस्य विपश्चितः।<br><br>इन्द्रियाणि प्रमाथीनि हरन्ति प्रसभं मनः।।2.60।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yatato hyapi kaunteya puruṣhasya vipaśhchitaḥ<br>indriyāṇi pramāthīni haranti prasabhaṁ manaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For, O son of Kunti, the turbulent senses can violently snatch away the mind of an intelligent person, even while they are striving diligently.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The turbulent senses, O Arjuna, can violently carry away the mind of a wise person, even though they are striving to control them.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_60.mp3]
gita_verse:2.61	<center><big>तानि सर्वाणि संयम्य युक्त आसीत मत्परः।<br><br>वशे हि यस्येन्द्रियाणि तस्य प्रज्ञा प्रतिष्ठिता।।2.61।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tāni sarvāṇi sanyamya yukta āsīta mat-paraḥ<br>vaśhe hi yasyendriyāṇi tasya prajñā pratiṣhṭhitā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Controlling all of them, one should remain focused on Me as the supreme. For, the wisdom of one whose senses are under control becomes steadfast.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Having restrained them all, he should sit steadfast, intent on Me; his wisdom is steady whose senses are under control.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_61.mp3]
gita_verse:2.62	<center><big>ध्यायतो विषयान्पुंसः सङ्गस्तेषूपजायते।<br><br>सङ्गात् संजायते कामः कामात्क्रोधोऽभिजायते।।2.62।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dhyāyato viṣhayān puṁsaḥ saṅgas teṣhūpajāyate<br>saṅgāt sañjāyate kāmaḥ kāmāt krodho ’bhijāyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>- In the case of a person who dwells on objects, there arises attachment to them. From attachment grows hankering, and from hankering springs anger.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>When one thinks of objects, attachment to them arises; from attachment, desire is born; from desire, anger arises.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_62.mp3]
gita_verse:2.63	<center><big>क्रोधाद्भवति संमोहः संमोहात्स्मृतिविभ्रमः।<br><br>स्मृतिभ्रंशाद् बुद्धिनाशो बुद्धिनाशात्प्रणश्यति।।2.63।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>krodhād bhavati sammohaḥ sammohāt smṛiti-vibhramaḥ<br>smṛiti-bhranśhād buddhi-nāśho buddhi-nāśhāt praṇaśhyati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>From anger follows delusion; from delusion, a failure of memory; from the failure of memory, the loss of understanding; and from the loss of understanding, one perishes.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Anger leads to delusion, which causes loss of memory; this, in turn, leads to the destruction of discrimination, resulting in destruction.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_63.mp3]
gita_verse:2.64	<center><big>रागद्वेषवियुक्तैस्तु विषयानिन्द्रियैश्चरन्।<br><br>आत्मवश्यैर्विधेयात्मा प्रसादमधिगच्छति।।2.64।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>rāga-dveṣha-viyuktais tu viṣhayān indriyaiśh charan<br>ātma-vaśhyair-vidheyātmā prasādam adhigachchhati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But by perceiving objects with the organs that are free from attraction and repulsion, and are under his own control, the self-controlled person attains serenity.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But the self-controlled man, moving among objects with the senses restrained and free from attraction and repulsion, attains peace.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_64.mp3]
gita_verse:2.65	<center><big>प्रसादे सर्वदुःखानां हानिरस्योपजायते।<br><br>प्रसन्नचेतसो ह्याशु बुद्धिः पर्यवतिष्ठते।।2.65।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>prasāde sarva-duḥkhānāṁ hānir asyopajāyate<br>prasanna-chetaso hyāśhu buddhiḥ paryavatiṣhṭhate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>When there is serenity, all his sorrows are eradicated, for the wisdom of one with a serene mind soon becomes firmly established.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>In that peace, all pains are destroyed; for the intellect of the tranquil-minded soon becomes steady.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_65.mp3]
gita_verse:2.66	<center><big>नास्ति बुद्धिरयुक्तस्य न चायुक्तस्य भावना।<br><br>न चाभावयतः शान्तिरशान्तस्य कुतः सुखम्।।2.66।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>nāsti buddhir-ayuktasya na chāyuktasya bhāvanā<br>na chābhāvayataḥ śhāntir aśhāntasya kutaḥ sukham<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For the unsteady there is no wisdom, and there is no meditation for the unsteady person. And for an unmeditative person there is no peace. How can there be happiness for one without peace?<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>There is no knowledge of the Self for the unsteady, and no meditation is possible for the unsteady, and no peace for the unmeditative, and how can there be happiness for one who has no peace?<br><br>[sound:gita_2_66.mp3]
gita_verse:2.67	<center><big>इन्द्रियाणां हि चरतां यन्मनोऽनुविधीयते।<br><br>तदस्य हरति प्रज्ञां वायुर्नावमिवाम्भसि।।2.67।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>indriyāṇāṁ hi charatāṁ yan mano ’nuvidhīyate<br>tadasya harati prajñāṁ vāyur nāvam ivāmbhasi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For, the mind which follows in the wake of the wandering senses carries away his wisdom like a boat on the waters.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>For the mind, which follows in the wake of the wandering senses, carries away his discrimination, as the wind carries away a boat on the waters.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_67.mp3]
gita_verse:2.68	<center><big>तस्माद्यस्य महाबाहो निगृहीतानि सर्वशः।<br><br>इन्द्रियाणीन्द्रियार्थेभ्यस्तस्य प्रज्ञा प्रतिष्ठिता।।2.68।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tasmād yasya mahā-bāho nigṛihītāni sarvaśhaḥ<br>indriyāṇīndriyārthebhyas tasya prajñā pratiṣhṭhitā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Therefore, O mighty-armed one, this wisdom becomes established when all its senses are withdrawn from their objects.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Therefore, O mighty-armed Arjuna, his knowledge is steady whose senses are completely restrained from sense objects.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_68.mp3]
gita_verse:2.69	<center><big>या निशा सर्वभूतानां तस्यां जागर्ति संयमी।<br><br>यस्यां जाग्रति भूतानि सा निशा पश्यतो मुनेः।।2.69।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yā niśhā sarva-bhūtānāṁ tasyāṁ jāgarti sanyamī<br>yasyāṁ jāgrati bhūtāni sā niśhā paśhyato muneḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The self-restrained man stays awake during what is night for all creatures. That which creatures stay awake for, it is night to the discerning sage.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That which is night to all beings, in that the self-controlled man is awake; when all beings are awake, that is night for the sage who sees.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_69.mp3]
gita_verse:2.70	<center><big>आपूर्यमाणमचलप्रतिष्ठं<br><br>समुद्रमापः प्रविशन्ति यद्वत्।<br><br>तद्वत्कामा यं प्रविशन्ति सर्वे<br><br>स शान्तिमाप्नोति न कामकामी।।2.70।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>āpūryamāṇam achala-pratiṣhṭhaṁ<br>samudram āpaḥ praviśhanti yadvat<br>tadvat kāmā yaṁ praviśhanti sarve<br>sa śhāntim āpnoti na kāma-kāmī<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That man attains peace into whom all desires enter, just as waters flow into the sea that remains unchanged even when filled from all sides. Not so one who is desirous of objects.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He attains peace into whom all desires enter, just as waters enter the ocean which, filled from all sides, remains unmoved; but not the man who is full of desires.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_70.mp3]
gita_verse:2.71	<center><big>विहाय कामान्यः सर्वान्पुमांश्चरति निःस्पृहः।<br><br>निर्ममो निरहंकारः स शांतिमधिगच्छति।।2.71।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>vihāya kāmān yaḥ sarvān pumānśh charati niḥspṛihaḥ<br>nirmamo nirahankāraḥ sa śhāntim adhigachchhati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That man attains peace who, after rejecting all desires, moves about free from hankering, without the idea of 'me' and 'mine', and devoid of pride.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That person attains peace who, abandoning all desires, moves about without longing, without the sense of ownership, and without egoism.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_71.mp3]
gita_verse:2.72	<center><big>एषा ब्राह्मी स्थितिः पार्थ नैनां प्राप्य विमुह्यति।<br><br>स्थित्वाऽस्यामन्तकालेऽपि ब्रह्मनिर्वाणमृच्छति।।2.72।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>eṣhā brāhmī sthitiḥ pārtha naināṁ prāpya vimuhyati<br>sthitvāsyām anta-kāle ’pi brahma-nirvāṇam ṛichchhati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Partha, this is the state of being established in Brahman. One does not become deluded after attaining this; one attains identification with Brahman by being established in this state even in the closing years of one's life.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>O son of Pritha, this is the eternal state, the Brahmic seat. Attaining this, one is not deluded. Being established in it, one attains oneness with Brahman even at the end of life.<br><br>[sound:gita_2_72.mp3]
gita_verse:3.1-2	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाच<br><br>ज्यायसी चेत्कर्मणस्ते मता बुद्धिर्जनार्दन।<br><br>तत्किं कर्मणि घोरे मां नियोजयसि केशव।।3.1।।<br> <br><br>व्यामिश्रेणेव वाक्येन बुद्धिं मोहयसीव मे।<br><br>तदेकं वद निश्िचत्य येन श्रेयोऽहमाप्नुयाम्।।3.2।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>jyāyasī chet karmaṇas te matā buddhir janārdana<br>tat kiṁ karmaṇi ghore māṁ niyojayasi keśhava<br><br>vyāmiśhreṇeva vākyena buddhiṁ mohayasīva me<br>tad ekaṁ vada niśhchitya yena śhreyo ’ham āpnuyām<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O Janardana (Krishna), if it is Your opinion that wisdom is superior to action, why do You urge me to take such horrible action, O Kesava?" You bewilder my understanding, as it were, with a seemingly conflicting statement! Tell me for certain which one of these I may use to attain the highest Good.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Arjuna said: If Thou thinkest that knowledge is superior to action, O Krishna, why then, O Kesava, doest Thou ask me to engage in this terrible action? With this seemingly perplexing speech, you seem to be confusing my understanding; therefore, tell me one certain way by which I may attain bliss.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_1-2.mp3]
gita_verse:3.3	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाच<br><br>लोकेऽस्मिन्द्विविधा निष्ठा पुरा प्रोक्ता मयानघ।<br><br>ज्ञानयोगेन सांख्यानां कर्मयोगेन योगिनाम्।।3.3।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī bhagavān uvācha<br>loke’smin dvi-vidhā niṣhṭhā purā proktā mayānagha<br>jñāna-yogena sāṅkhyānāṁ karma-yogena yoginām<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, O unblemished one, two kinds of steadfastness in this world were spoken of by Me in days gone by—through the Yoga of Knowledge for the men of realization; through the Yoga of Action for the yogis.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "In this world, there is a twofold path, as I said before, O sinless one: the path of knowledge of the Sankhyas and the path of action of the Yogins."<br><br>[sound:gita_3_3.mp3]
gita_verse:3.4	<center><big>न कर्मणामनारम्भान्नैष्कर्म्यं पुरुषोऽश्नुते।<br><br>न च संन्यसनादेव सिद्धिं समधिगच्छति।।3.4।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na karmaṇām anārambhān naiṣhkarmyaṁ puruṣho ’śhnute<br>na cha sannyasanād eva siddhiṁ samadhigachchhati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>A person does not attain freedom from action by abstaining from action; nor does he attain fulfillment merely through renunciation.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Man does not reach actionlessness by not performing actions; nor does he attain perfection by mere renunciation.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_4.mp3]
gita_verse:3.5	<center><big>न हि कश्िचत्क्षणमपि जातु तिष्ठत्यकर्मकृत्।<br><br>कार्यते ह्यवशः कर्म सर्वः प्रकृतिजैर्गुणैः।।3.5।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na hi kaśhchit kṣhaṇam api jātu tiṣhṭhatyakarma-kṛit<br>kāryate hyavaśhaḥ karma sarvaḥ prakṛiti-jair guṇaiḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For no one ever remains even for a moment without doing work, for all are made to work under compulsion by the gunas born of Nature.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Verily, no one can remain for even a moment without performing action; for everyone is made to act helplessly, indeed, by the qualities born of Nature.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_5.mp3]
gita_verse:3.6	<center><big>कर्मेन्द्रियाणि संयम्य य आस्ते मनसा स्मरन्।<br><br>इन्द्रियार्थान्विमूढात्मा मिथ्याचारः स उच्यते।।3.6।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>karmendriyāṇi sanyamya ya āste manasā smaran<br>indriyārthān vimūḍhātmā mithyāchāraḥ sa uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One who, after withdrawing the organs of action, sits mentally recollecting the objects of the senses, is called a hypocrite, for they have a deluded mind.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who, restraining the organs of action, sits thinking of the sense-objects in his mind, he of deluded understanding is called a hypocrite.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_6.mp3]
gita_verse:3.7	<center><big>यस्त्विन्द्रियाणि मनसा नियम्यारभतेऽर्जुन।<br><br>कर्मेन्द्रियैः कर्मयोगमसक्तः स विशिष्यते।।3.7।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yas tvindriyāṇi manasā niyamyārabhate ’rjuna<br>karmendriyaiḥ karma-yogam asaktaḥ sa viśhiṣhyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But, O Arjuna, one who engages in Karma-yoga, controlling the organs of action with the mind and becoming unattached, excels.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But whoever, controlling the senses by the mind, O Arjuna, engages himself in Karma Yoga with the organs of action, without attachment, he excels.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_7.mp3]
gita_verse:3.8	<center><big>नियतं कुरु कर्म त्वं कर्म ज्यायो ह्यकर्मणः।<br><br>शरीरयात्रापि च ते न प्रसिद्ध्येदकर्मणः।।3.8।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>niyataṁ kuru karma tvaṁ karma jyāyo hyakarmaṇaḥ<br>śharīra-yātrāpi cha te na prasiddhyed akarmaṇaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>You should perform your obligatory duties, for action is superior to inaction. Moreover, even the maintenance of your body will not be possible without action.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Perform your bounden duty, for action is superior to inaction, and even the maintenance of the body would not be possible for you through inaction.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_8.mp3]
gita_verse:3.9	<center><big>यज्ञार्थात्कर्मणोऽन्यत्र लोकोऽयं कर्मबन्धनः।<br><br>तदर्थं कर्म कौन्तेय मुक्तसंगः समाचर।।3.9।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yajñārthāt karmaṇo ’nyatra loko ’yaṁ karma-bandhanaḥ<br>tad-arthaṁ karma kaunteya mukta-saṅgaḥ samāchara<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>This man becomes bound by actions other than those intended for God. Without being attached, O son of Kunti, perform actions for Him.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The world is bound by actions other than those performed for the sake of sacrifice; do thou, therefore, O son of Kunti (Arjuna), perform actions for that sake alone, free from attachment.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_9.mp3]
