gita_verse:3.10	<center><big>सहयज्ञाः प्रजाः सृष्ट्वा पुरोवाच प्रजापतिः।<br><br>अनेन प्रसविष्यध्वमेष वोऽस्त्विष्टकामधुक्।।3.10।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>saha-yajñāḥ prajāḥ sṛiṣhṭvā purovācha prajāpatiḥ<br>anena prasaviṣhyadhvam eṣha vo ’stviṣhṭa-kāma-dhuk<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>In days of yore, having created the beings together with the sacrifices, Prajapati said, "By this, you shall multiply. Let this be your yielder of coveted objects of desire."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Creator, having in the beginning created mankind together with sacrifice, said, "By this shall you propagate; let this be the milch cow of your desires—the cow that yields all the desired objects."<br><br>[sound:gita_3_10.mp3]
gita_verse:3.11	<center><big>देवान्भावयतानेन ते देवा भावयन्तु वः।<br><br>परस्परं भावयन्तः श्रेयः परमवाप्स्यथ।।3.11।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>devān bhāvayatānena te devā bhāvayantu vaḥ<br>parasparaṁ bhāvayantaḥ śhreyaḥ param avāpsyatha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>'You nourish the gods with this. Let those gods nourish you in return. By mutually nourishing each other, you shall attain the supreme Good.'<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>With this, nourish the gods, and may the gods nourish you; thus, nourishing each other, you shall attain the highest good.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_11.mp3]
gita_verse:3.12	<center><big>इष्टान्भोगान्हि वो देवा दास्यन्ते यज्ञभाविताः।<br><br>तैर्दत्तानप्रदायैभ्यो यो भुङ्क्ते स्तेन एव सः।।3.12।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>iṣhṭān bhogān hi vo devā dāsyante yajña-bhāvitāḥ<br>tair dattān apradāyaibhyo yo bhuṅkte stena eva saḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>'Being nourished by sacrifices, the gods will indeed give you the coveted enjoyments. He is certainly a thief who enjoys what has been given by them without offering it to them.'<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The gods, nourished by the sacrifice, will give you the desired objects. So, he who enjoys the objects given by the gods without offering anything in return is indeed a thief.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_12.mp3]
gita_verse:3.13	<center><big>यज्ञशिष्टाशिनः सन्तो मुच्यन्ते सर्वकिल्बिषैः।<br><br>भुञ्जते ते त्वघं पापा ये पचन्त्यात्मकारणात्।।3.13।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yajña-śhiṣhṭāśhinaḥ santo muchyante sarva-kilbiṣhaiḥ<br>bhuñjate te tvaghaṁ pāpā ye pachantyātma-kāraṇāt<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>By partaking in the remnants of sacrifices, they become freed from all sins. But those who are unholy and cook for themselves incur sin.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The righteous who eat the remnants of the sacrifice are freed from all sins; but those sinful ones who cook food solely for their own sake indeed consume sin.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_13.mp3]
gita_verse:3.14	<center><big>अन्नाद्भवन्ति भूतानि पर्जन्यादन्नसम्भवः।<br><br>यज्ञाद्भवति पर्जन्यो यज्ञः कर्मसमुद्भवः।।3.14।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>annād bhavanti bhūtāni parjanyād anna-sambhavaḥ<br>yajñād bhavati parjanyo yajñaḥ karma-samudbhavaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>From food are born the creatures; the origin of food is from rain; rain originates from sacrifice; sacrifice has action as its source.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>From food come forth beings; from rain, food is produced; from sacrifice arises rain, and sacrifice is born of action.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_14.mp3]
gita_verse:3.15	<center><big>कर्म ब्रह्मोद्भवं विद्धि ब्रह्माक्षरसमुद्भवम्।<br><br>तस्मात्सर्वगतं ब्रह्म नित्यं यज्ञे प्रतिष्ठितम्।।3.15।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>karma brahmodbhavaṁ viddhi brahmākṣhara-samudbhavam<br>tasmāt sarva-gataṁ brahma nityaṁ yajñe pratiṣhṭhitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Know that action has the Vedas as its origin; the Vedas have the Immutable as their source. Hence, the all-pervading Vedas are forever based on sacrifice.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Know that action comes from Brahma, and Brahma comes from the Imperishable. Therefore, the all-pervasive Brahma ever rests in sacrifice.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_15.mp3]
gita_verse:3.16	<center><big>एवं प्रवर्तितं चक्रं नानुवर्तयतीह यः।<br><br>अघायुरिन्द्रियारामो मोघं पार्थ स जीवति।।3.16।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>evaṁ pravartitaṁ chakraṁ nānuvartayatīha yaḥ<br>aghāyur indriyārāmo moghaṁ pārtha sa jīvati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Partha, he who does not follow the wheel thus set in motion lives in vain, their life is sinful, and they indulge in the senses.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who does not follow the wheel thus set in motion, who is of sinful life, rejoicing in the senses, lives in vain, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_16.mp3]
gita_verse:3.17	<center><big>यस्त्वात्मरतिरेव स्यादात्मतृप्तश्च मानवः।<br><br>आत्मन्येव च सन्तुष्टस्तस्य कार्यं न विद्यते।।3.17।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yas tvātma-ratir eva syād ātma-tṛiptaśh cha mānavaḥ<br>ātmanyeva cha santuṣhṭas tasya kāryaṁ na vidyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But that man who rejoices only in the Self, is satisfied with the Self, and is content only in the Self—for him there is no duty to perform.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But for that man who rejoices only in the Self, who is satisfied with the Self and is content in the Self alone, indeed there is nothing to do.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_17.mp3]
gita_verse:3.18	<center><big>नैव तस्य कृतेनार्थो नाकृतेनेह कश्चन।<br><br>न चास्य सर्वभूतेषु कश्िचदर्थव्यपाश्रयः।।3.18।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>naiva tasya kṛitenārtho nākṛiteneha kaśhchana<br>na chāsya sarva-bhūteṣhu kaśhchid artha-vyapāśhrayaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For him, there is no concern here at all with performing action, nor any with non-performance. Moreover, he has no dependence on any object to serve any purpose.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>For him, there is no interest whatsoever in what is done or not done; nor does he depend on any being for any purpose.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_18.mp3]
gita_verse:3.19	<center><big>तस्मादसक्तः सततं कार्यं कर्म समाचर।<br><br>असक्तो ह्याचरन्कर्म परमाप्नोति पूरुषः।।3.19।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tasmād asaktaḥ satataṁ kāryaṁ karma samāchara<br>asakto hyācharan karma param āpnoti pūruṣhaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Therefore, remaining unattached, always perform the obligatory duty; for, by performing one's duty without attachment, a person attains the highest.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Therefore, without attachment, always perform the actions that should be done; for by performing actions without attachment, one reaches the Supreme.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_19.mp3]
gita_verse:3.20-21	<center><big>कर्मणैव हि संसिद्धिमास्थिता जनकादयः।<br><br>लोकसंग्रहमेवापि संपश्यन्कर्तुमर्हसि।।3.20।।<br> <br><br>यद्यदाचरति श्रेष्ठस्तत्तदेवेतरो जनः।<br><br>स यत्प्रमाणं कुरुते लोकस्तदनुवर्तते।।3.21।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>karmaṇaiva hi sansiddhim āsthitā janakādayaḥ<br>loka-saṅgraham evāpi sampaśhyan kartum arhasi<br><br>yad yad ācharati śhreṣhṭhas tat tad evetaro janaḥ<br>sa yat pramāṇaṁ kurute lokas tad anuvartate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For Janaka and others strove to attain liberation through action itself. You should perform your duties, keeping in view the prevention of mankind from going astray. Whatever a superior person does, another person does the same! Whatever they uphold as authority, an ordinary person follows that.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Janaka and others attained perfection indeed through action alone; even with the intention of protecting the masses, you should perform action. Whatever a great man does, others also do; whatever he establishes as the standard, the world follows.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_20-21.mp3]
gita_verse:3.22	<center><big>न मे पार्थास्ति कर्तव्यं त्रिषु लोकेषु किञ्चन।<br><br>नानवाप्तमवाप्तव्यं वर्त एव च कर्मणि।।3.22।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na me pārthāsti kartavyaṁ triṣhu lokeṣhu kiñchana<br>nānavāptam avāptavyaṁ varta eva cha karmaṇi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>In all the three worlds, O Partha, there is no duty for Me to fulfill; nothing remains unachieved or to be achieved. (Still,) I continue in action.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>There is nothing in the three worlds, O Arjuna, that needs to be done by Me, nor is there anything unattained that needs to be attained; yet I engage Myself in action.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_22.mp3]
gita_verse:3.23	<center><big>यदि ह्यहं न वर्तेयं जातु कर्मण्यतन्द्रितः।<br><br>मम वर्त्मानुवर्तन्ते मनुष्याः पार्थ सर्वशः।।3.23।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yadi hyahaṁ na varteyaṁ jātu karmaṇyatandritaḥ<br>mama vartmānuvartante manuṣhyāḥ pārtha sarvaśhaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For, O Partha, if at any time I do not continue vigilantly in action, people will follow My path in every way.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>For, should I not ever engage myself in action, unwearied, people would in every way follow my path, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_23.mp3]
gita_verse:3.24	<center><big>उत्सीदेयुरिमे लोका न कुर्यां कर्म चेदहम्।<br><br>सङ्करस्य च कर्ता स्यामुपहन्यामिमाः प्रजाः।।3.24।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>utsīdeyur ime lokā na kuryāṁ karma ched aham<br>sankarasya cha kartā syām upahanyām imāḥ prajāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>These worlds would be ruined if I did not perform action. And I shall become the agent of intermingling (of castes), and shall be destroying these beings.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>These worlds would perish if I did not perform action; I would be the author of confusion of castes and destruction of these beings.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_24.mp3]
gita_verse:3.25	<center><big>सक्ताः कर्मण्यविद्वांसो यथा कुर्वन्ति भारत।<br><br>कुर्याद्विद्वांस्तथासक्तश्िचकीर्षुर्लोकसंग्रहम्।।3.25।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>saktāḥ karmaṇyavidvānso yathā kurvanti bhārata<br>kuryād vidvāns tathāsaktaśh chikīrṣhur loka-saṅgraham<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O scion of the Bharata dynasty, as the unenlightened people act with attachment to work, so should the enlightened person act, without attachment, desiring to prevent people from going astray.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>As the ignorant act out of attachment to action, O Bharata, so should the wise act without attachment, wishing for the welfare of the world.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_25.mp3]
gita_verse:3.26	<center><big>न बुद्धिभेदं जनयेदज्ञानां कर्मसङ्गिनाम्।<br><br>जोषयेत्सर्वकर्माणि विद्वान् युक्तः समाचरन्।।3.26।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na buddhi-bhedaṁ janayed ajñānāṁ karma-saṅginām<br>joṣhayet sarva-karmāṇi vidvān yuktaḥ samācharan<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The enlightened man should not disturb the beliefs of the ignorant, who are attached to work. He should remain diligent himself and make them perform all their duties.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Let no wise man unsettle the minds of ignorant people who are attached to action; he should engage them in all actions, himself fulfilling them with devotion.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_26.mp3]
gita_verse:3.27	<center><big>प्रकृतेः क्रियमाणानि गुणैः कर्माणि सर्वशः।<br><br>अहङ्कारविमूढात्मा कर्ताऽहमिति मन्यते।।3.27।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>prakṛiteḥ kriyamāṇāni guṇaiḥ karmāṇi sarvaśhaḥ<br>ahankāra-vimūḍhātmā kartāham iti manyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>While actions are being done in every way by the gunas (qualities) of Nature, one who is deluded by egoism thinks, "I am the doer."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>All actions are wrought in all cases by the qualities of Nature alone. He whose mind is deluded by egoism thinks, "I am the doer."<br><br>[sound:gita_3_27.mp3]
gita_verse:3.28	<center><big>तत्त्ववित्तु महाबाहो गुणकर्मविभागयोः।<br><br>गुणा गुणेषु वर्तन्त इति मत्वा न सज्जते।।3.28।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tattva-vit tu mahā-bāho guṇa-karma-vibhāgayoḥ<br>guṇā guṇeṣhu vartanta iti matvā na sajjate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But, O mighty-armed one, the one who is a knower of the facts about the varieties of the gunas and actions does not become attached, thinking thus: 'The organs act on the objects of the organs.'<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But he who knows the Truth, O mighty-armed Arjuna, about the divisions of the qualities and their functions, knowing that the Gunas, as senses, move amidst the Gunas, as the sense-objects, is not attached.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_28.mp3]
gita_verse:3.29	<center><big>प्रकृतेर्गुणसम्मूढाः सज्जन्ते गुणकर्मसु।<br><br>तानकृत्स्नविदो मन्दान्कृत्स्नविन्न विचालयेत्।।3.29।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>prakṛiter guṇa-sammūḍhāḥ sajjante guṇa-karmasu<br>tān akṛitsna-vido mandān kṛitsna-vin na vichālayet<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Those who are completely deluded by the gunas of Nature become attached to the activities of the gunas. The one who knows the All should not disturb those of dull intellect, who do not know the All.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Those deluded by the qualities of Nature are attached to the functions of the qualities. The man of perfect knowledge should not unsettle the foolish one who is of imperfect knowledge.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_29.mp3]
gita_verse:3.30	<center><big>मयि सर्वाणि कर्माणि संन्यस्याध्यात्मचेतसा।<br><br>निराशीर्निर्ममो भूत्वा युध्यस्व विगतज्वरः।।3.30।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>mayi sarvāṇi karmāṇi sannyasyādhyātma-chetasā<br>nirāśhīr nirmamo bhūtvā yudhyasva vigata-jvaraḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Free from the fever of the soul, dedicate all actions to Me, with your mind intent on the Self, and become free from expectations and egoism, and engage in battle.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Renouncing all actions in Me, with the mind centered on the Self, free from hope and egoism, and from mental fever, fight thou.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_30.mp3]
gita_verse:3.31	<center><big>ये मे मतमिदं नित्यमनुतिष्ठन्ति मानवाः।<br><br>श्रद्धावन्तोऽनसूयन्तो मुच्यन्ते तेऽपि कर्मभिः।।3.31।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ye me matam idaṁ nityam anutiṣhṭhanti mānavāḥ<br>śhraddhāvanto ’nasūyanto muchyante te ’pi karmabhiḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Those who faithfully follow this teaching of Mine without cavil, they too become freed from their actions.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Those who constantly practice this teaching of Mine with faith and without caviling, they too are freed from actions.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_31.mp3]
gita_verse:3.32	<center><big>ये त्वेतदभ्यसूयन्तो नानुतिष्ठन्ति मे मतम्।<br><br>सर्वज्ञानविमूढांस्तान्विद्धि नष्टानचेतसः।।3.32।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ye tvetad abhyasūyanto nānutiṣhṭhanti me matam<br>sarva-jñāna-vimūḍhāns tān viddhi naṣhṭān achetasaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But those who, finding fault where there is none, do not follow My teaching, know them—who are deluded about all knowledge concerning the qualified and the unqualified Brahman and who are devoid of discrimination—to have gone to ruin.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But those who criticize My teaching and do not practice it, deprived of all knowledge and lacking discernment, know them to be doomed to destruction.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_32.mp3]
gita_verse:3.33	<center><big>सदृशं चेष्टते स्वस्याः प्रकृतेर्ज्ञानवानपि।<br><br>प्रकृतिं यान्ति भूतानि निग्रहः किं करिष्यति।।3.33।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sadṛiśhaṁ cheṣhṭate svasyāḥ prakṛiter jñānavān api<br>prakṛitiṁ yānti bhūtāni nigrahaḥ kiṁ kariṣhyati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Even a man of wisdom behaves according to his own nature. They follow their nature. What can restraint do?<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Even a wise man acts in accordance with his own nature; beings will follow their nature; what can restraint do?<br><br>[sound:gita_3_33.mp3]
gita_verse:3.34	<center><big>इन्द्रियस्येन्द्रियस्यार्थे रागद्वेषौ व्यवस्थितौ।<br><br>तयोर्न वशमागच्छेत्तौ ह्यस्य परिपन्थिनौ।।3.34।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>indriyasyendriyasyārthe rāga-dveṣhau vyavasthitau<br>tayor na vaśham āgachchhet tau hyasya paripanthinau<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Attraction and repulsion are ordained with respect to the objects of all the organs. One should not be swayed by these two, as they are adversaries.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Attachment and aversion for the objects of the senses abide in the senses; let no one come under their sway; for, they are his enemies.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_34.mp3]
gita_verse:3.35	<center><big>श्रेयान्स्वधर्मो विगुणः परधर्मात्स्वनुष्ठितात्।<br><br>स्वधर्मे निधनं श्रेयः परधर्मो भयावहः।।3.35।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhreyān swa-dharmo viguṇaḥ para-dharmāt sv-anuṣhṭhitāt<br>swa-dharme nidhanaṁ śhreyaḥ para-dharmo bhayāvahaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One's own duty, though defective, is superior to another's duty well-performed. Death is better while engaged in one's own duty; another's duty is full of fear.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Better is one's own duty, though devoid of merit, than the duty of another well discharged. Better is death in one's own duty; the duty of another is fraught with fear.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_35.mp3]
gita_verse:3.36	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाच<br><br>अथ केन प्रयुक्तोऽयं पापं चरति पूरुषः।<br><br>अनिच्छन्नपि वार्ष्णेय बलादिव नियोजितः।।3.36।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>atha kena prayukto ’yaṁ pāpaṁ charati pūruṣhaḥ<br>anichchhann api vārṣhṇeya balād iva niyojitaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "Now then, O scion of the Vrsni dynasty (Krsna), what compels this man to commit sin even against his will, as if he were constrained by force?"<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "But what compels man to commit sin, even against his wishes, O Varshneya (Krishna), as if constrained by force?"<br><br>[sound:gita_3_36.mp3]
gita_verse:3.37	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाच<br><br>काम एष क्रोध एष रजोगुणसमुद्भवः।<br><br>महाशनो महापाप्मा विद्ध्येनमिह वैरिणम्।।3.37।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī bhagavān uvācha<br>kāma eṣha krodha eṣha rajo-guṇa-samudbhavaḥ<br>mahāśhano mahā-pāpmā viddhyenam iha vairiṇam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "This desire, this anger, born of the quality of rajas, is a great devourer, a great source of sin. Know this to be the enemy here."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "It is desire and it is anger, both of the quality of Rajas, all-devouring and all-sinful; know this as the foe here in this world."<br><br>[sound:gita_3_37.mp3]
gita_verse:3.38	<center><big>धूमेनाव्रियते वह्निर्यथाऽऽदर्शो मलेन च।<br><br>यथोल्बेनावृतो गर्भस्तथा तेनेदमावृतम्।।3.38।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dhūmenāvriyate vahnir yathādarśho malena cha<br>yatholbenāvṛito garbhas tathā tenedam āvṛitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>As fire is enveloped by smoke, as a mirror is obscured by dirt, and as a fetus remains enclosed in the womb, so is this shrouded by that.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>As fire is enveloped by smoke, as a mirror is covered by dust, and as an embryo is surrounded by the amniotic sac, so is this enveloped by that.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_38.mp3]
gita_verse:3.39	<center><big>आवृतं ज्ञानमेतेन ज्ञानिनो नित्यवैरिणा।<br><br>कामरूपेण कौन्तेय दुष्पूरेणानलेन च।।3.39।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>āvṛitaṁ jñānam etena jñānino nitya-vairiṇā<br>kāma-rūpeṇa kaunteya duṣhpūreṇānalena cha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O son of Kunti, knowledge is covered by this constant enemy of the wise, in the form of desire, which is an insatiable fire.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>O Arjuna, wisdom is enveloped by this constant enemy of the wise, in the form of desire, which is insatiable like fire.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_39.mp3]
gita_verse:3.40	<center><big>इन्द्रियाणि मनो बुद्धिरस्याधिष्ठानमुच्यते।<br><br>एतैर्विमोहयत्येष ज्ञानमावृत्य देहिनम्।।3.40।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>indriyāṇi mano buddhir asyādhiṣhṭhānam uchyate<br>etair vimohayatyeṣha jñānam āvṛitya dehinam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The organs, mind, and intellect are said to be its abode. This one diversely deludes the embodied being, veiling Knowledge with the help of these.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The senses, the mind, and the intellect are said to be its seat; through these, it deludes the embodied one, veiling their wisdom.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_40.mp3]
gita_verse:3.41	<center><big>तस्मात्त्वमिन्द्रियाण्यादौ नियम्य भरतर्षभ।<br><br>पाप्मानं प्रजहि ह्येनं ज्ञानविज्ञाननाशनम्।।3.41।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tasmāt tvam indriyāṇyādau niyamya bharatarṣhabha<br>pāpmānaṁ prajahi hyenaṁ jñāna-vijñāna-nāśhanam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Therefore, O scion of the Bharata dynasty, after first controlling the organs, completely renounce this one which is sinful and a destroyer of learning and wisdom.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Therefore, O best of the Bharatas, control your senses first and then kill this sinful thing, which destroys knowledge and realization.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_41.mp3]
gita_verse:3.42	<center><big>इन्द्रियाणि पराण्याहुरिन्द्रियेभ्यः परं मनः।<br><br>मनसस्तु परा बुद्धिर्यो बुद्धेः परतस्तु सः।।3.42।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>indriyāṇi parāṇyāhur indriyebhyaḥ paraṁ manaḥ<br>manasas tu parā buddhir yo buddheḥ paratas tu saḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>They say that the organs are superior to the gross body; the mind is superior to the organs; and the intellect is superior to the mind. However, He is superior to the intellect.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>They say that the senses are superior to the body; the mind is superior to the senses; the intellect is superior to the mind; and He (the Self) is superior even to the intellect.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_42.mp3]
gita_verse:3.43	<center><big>एवं बुद्धेः परं बुद्ध्वा संस्तभ्यात्मानमात्मना।<br><br>जहि शत्रुं महाबाहो कामरूपं दुरासदम्।।3.43।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>evaṁ buddheḥ paraṁ buddhvā sanstabhyātmānam ātmanā<br>jahi śhatruṁ mahā-bāho kāma-rūpaṁ durāsadam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>[The Ast, introduces this verse with, 'Tatah kim, what follows from that?'-Tr.] Understanding the Self thus as superior to the intellect, and completely establishing (the Self) through spiritual absorption with the (help of) the mind, O mighty-armed one, the enemy in the form of desire, which is difficult to subdue, vanishes.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Thus, knowing Him who is superior to the intellect and restraining the self by the Self, slay thou, O mighty-armed Arjuna, the enemy in the form of desire, hard to conquer.<br><br>[sound:gita_3_43.mp3]
gita_verse:4.1	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाच<br><br>इमं विवस्वते योगं प्रोक्तवानहमव्ययम्।<br><br>विवस्वान् मनवे प्राह मनुरिक्ष्वाकवेऽब्रवीत्।।4.1।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī bhagavān uvācha<br>imaṁ vivasvate yogaṁ proktavān aham avyayam<br>vivasvān manave prāha manur ikṣhvākave ’bravīt<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "I imparted this imperishable Yoga to Vivasvan, who then taught it to Manu, who in turn transmitted it to Iksavaku.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "I taught this imperishable Yoga to Vivasvan; he then told it to Manu; Manu proclaimed it to Ikshvaku.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_1.mp3]
gita_verse:4.2	<center><big>एवं परम्पराप्राप्तमिमं राजर्षयो विदुः।<br><br>स कालेनेह महता योगो नष्टः परन्तप।।4.2।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>evaṁ paramparā-prāptam imaṁ rājarṣhayo viduḥ<br>sa kāleneha mahatā yogo naṣhṭaḥ parantapa<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The king-sages knew this yoga, which was received in regular succession. That yoga, O destroyer of foes, is now lost due to a long lapse of time.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>This, handed down in regular succession by the royal sages, was known. This Yoga, however, has been lost here over time, O Parantapa (burner of the foes).<br><br>[sound:gita_4_2.mp3]
gita_verse:4.3	<center><big>स एवायं मया तेऽद्य योगः प्रोक्तः पुरातनः।<br><br>भक्तोऽसि मे सखा चेति रहस्यं ह्येतदुत्तमम्।।4.3।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sa evāyaṁ mayā te ’dya yogaḥ proktaḥ purātanaḥ<br>bhakto ’si me sakhā cheti rahasyaṁ hyetad uttamam<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That ancient Yoga itself, which is this, has been taught to you by Me today, considering you to be My devotee and friend, for this Yoga is a profound secret.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That same ancient yoga has been today taught to you by me, for you are my devotee and my friend; it is the supreme secret.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_3.mp3]
gita_verse:4.4	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाच<br><br>अपरं भवतो जन्म परं जन्म विवस्वतः।<br><br>कथमेतद्विजानीयां त्वमादौ प्रोक्तवानिति।।4.4।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>aparaṁ bhavato janma paraṁ janma vivasvataḥ<br>katham etad vijānīyāṁ tvam ādau proktavān iti<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "Your birth was later, whereas Vivasvan's birth was earlier. How am I to understand that You instructed him in the beginning?"<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "Later was Thy birth, and prior to it was the birth of Vivasvan (the Sun); how am I to understand that Thou hast taught this Yoga from the beginning?"<br><br>[sound:gita_4_4.mp3]
gita_verse:4.5	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाच<br><br>बहूनि मे व्यतीतानि जन्मानि तव चार्जुन।<br><br>तान्यहं वेद सर्वाणि न त्वं वेत्थ परन्तप।।4.5।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī bhagavān uvācha<br>bahūni me vyatītāni janmāni tava chārjuna<br>tānyahaṁ veda sarvāṇi na tvaṁ vettha parantapa<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "O Arjuna, many lives of Mine have passed, and so have yours. I know them all, but you do not know, O scorcher of enemies!"<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "Many births of Mine have passed, as well as of thine, O Arjuna; I know them all, but thou knowest not, O Parantapa (scorcher of foes)."<br><br>[sound:gita_4_5.mp3]
gita_verse:4.6	<center><big>अजोऽपि सन्नव्ययात्मा भूतानामीश्वरोऽपि सन्।<br><br>प्रकृतिं स्वामधिष्ठाय संभवाम्यात्ममायया।।4.6।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ajo ’pi sannavyayātmā bhūtānām īśhvaro ’pi san<br>prakṛitiṁ svām adhiṣhṭhāya sambhavāmyātma-māyayā<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Though I am birthless and undecaying by nature, and the Lord of beings, yet by subjugating My Prakriti, I take birth through My own Maya.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Though I am unborn and of imperishable nature, and though I am the Lord of all beings, yet, governing my own nature, I am born by my own Maya.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_6.mp3]
gita_verse:4.7	<center><big>यदा यदा हि धर्मस्य ग्लानिर्भवति भारत।<br><br>अभ्युत्थानमधर्मस्य तदाऽऽत्मानं सृजाम्यहम्।।4.7।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yadā yadā hi dharmasya glānir bhavati bhārata<br>abhyutthānam adharmasya tadātmānaṁ sṛijāmyaham<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O scion of the Bharata dynasty, whenever there is a decline in virtue and an increase in vice, then I manifest Myself.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Whenever there is a decline of righteousness and an increase of unrighteousness, O Arjuna, then I manifest Myself.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_7.mp3]
gita_verse:4.8	<center><big>परित्राणाय साधूनां विनाशाय च दुष्कृताम्।<br><br>धर्मसंस्थापनार्थाय संभवामि युगे युगे।।4.8।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>paritrāṇāya sādhūnāṁ vināśhāya cha duṣhkṛitām<br>dharma-sansthāpanārthāya sambhavāmi yuge yuge<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For the protection of the pious, the destruction of the evil-doers, and the establishment of virtue, I manifest myself in every age.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>For the protection of the good, for the destruction of the wicked, and for the establishment of righteousness, I am born in every age.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_8.mp3]
gita_verse:4.9	<center><big>जन्म कर्म च मे दिव्यमेवं यो वेत्ति तत्त्वतः।<br><br>त्यक्त्वा देहं पुनर्जन्म नैति मामेति सोऽर्जुन।।4.9।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>janma karma cha me divyam evaṁ yo vetti tattvataḥ<br>tyaktvā dehaṁ punar janma naiti mām eti so ’rjuna<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who thus knows truly the divine birth and actions of Mine does not get rebirth after casting off the body. He attains Me, O Arjuna.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who thus knows, in their true light, My divine birth and actions, having abandoned the body, is not born again; he comes to Me, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_9.mp3]
gita_verse:4.10	<center><big>वीतरागभयक्रोधा मन्मया मामुपाश्रिताः।<br><br>बहवो ज्ञानतपसा पूता मद्भावमागताः।।4.10।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>vīta-rāga-bhaya-krodhā man-mayā mām upāśhritāḥ<br>bahavo jñāna-tapasā pūtā mad-bhāvam āgatāḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Many who were devoid of attachment, fear, and anger, who were absorbed in Me, who had taken refuge in Me, and were purified by the austerity of knowledge, have attained My state.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Freed from attachment, fear, and anger, absorbed in Me, taking refuge in Me, purified by the fire of knowledge, many have attained My Being.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_10.mp3]
gita_verse:4.11	<center><big>ये यथा मां प्रपद्यन्ते तांस्तथैव भजाम्यहम्।<br><br>मम वर्त्मानुवर्तन्ते मनुष्याः पार्थ सर्वशः।।4.11।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ye yathā māṁ prapadyante tāns tathaiva bhajāmyaham<br>mama vartmānuvartante manuṣhyāḥ pārtha sarvaśhaḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>According to the manner in which they approach Me, I favor them in that same manner. O son of Partha, humans follow My path in every way.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>In whatever way men approach Me, even so do I reward them; My path do men tread in all ways, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_11.mp3]
gita_verse:4.12	<center><big>काङ्क्षन्तः कर्मणां सिद्धिं यजन्त इह देवताः।<br><br>क्षिप्रं हि मानुषे लोके सिद्धिर्भवति कर्मजा।।4.12।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kāṅkṣhantaḥ karmaṇāṁ siddhiṁ yajanta iha devatāḥ<br>kṣhipraṁ hi mānuṣhe loke siddhir bhavati karmajā<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Longing for the fruition of their actions (of their rites and duties), they worship the gods here. For, in the human world, success from action comes quickly.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Those who long for success in action in this world sacrifice to the gods; for success is quickly attained by men through action.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_12.mp3]
gita_verse:4.13	<center><big>चातुर्वर्ण्यं मया सृष्टं गुणकर्मविभागशः।<br><br>तस्य कर्तारमपि मां विद्ध्यकर्तारमव्ययम्।।4.13।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>chātur-varṇyaṁ mayā sṛiṣhṭaṁ guṇa-karma-vibhāgaśhaḥ<br>tasya kartāram api māṁ viddhyakartāram avyayam<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The four castes have been created by Me through a classification of the gunas and duties. Even though I am the agent of that (act of classification), still know Me to be non-agentive and changeless.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The fourfold caste has been created by Me according to the differentiation of Guna and Karma; though I am the author of it, know Me as non-doer and immutable.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_13.mp3]
gita_verse:4.14	<center><big>न मां कर्माणि लिम्पन्ति न मे कर्मफले स्पृहा।<br><br>इति मां योऽभिजानाति कर्मभिर्न स बध्यते।।4.14।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na māṁ karmāṇi limpanti na me karma-phale spṛihā<br>iti māṁ yo ’bhijānāti karmabhir na sa badhyate<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Actions do not taint Me; for I have no hankering for the results of actions. One who knows Me thus, does not become bound by their actions.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Actions do not taint Me, nor do I have a desire for the fruit of actions. He who knows Me thus is not bound by actions.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_14.mp3]
gita_verse:4.15	<center><big>एवं ज्ञात्वा कृतं कर्म पूर्वैरपि मुमुक्षुभिः।<br><br>कुरु कर्मैव तस्मात्त्वं पूर्वैः पूर्वतरं कृतम्।।4.15।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>evaṁ jñātvā kṛitaṁ karma pūrvair api mumukṣhubhiḥ<br>kuru karmaiva tasmāttvaṁ pūrvaiḥ pūrvataraṁ kṛitam<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Thus having known, even the ancient seekers of liberation performed their duties. Therefore, you should undertake action as was performed earlier by the ancients.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Having known this, the ancient seekers of freedom also performed action; therefore, do thou also perform action, as the ancients did in days of yore.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_15.mp3]
gita_verse:4.16	<center><big>किं कर्म किमकर्मेति कवयोऽप्यत्र मोहिताः।<br><br>तत्ते कर्म प्रवक्ष्यामि यज्ज्ञात्वा मोक्ष्यसेऽशुभात्।।4.16।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kiṁ karma kim akarmeti kavayo ’pyatra mohitāḥ<br>tat te karma pravakṣhyāmi yaj jñātvā mokṣhyase ’śhubhāt<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Even the intelligent are confounded as to what is action and what is inaction. I shall tell you of that action, knowing which you will become free from evil.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>What is action? What is inaction? Even the wise are confused about this. Therefore, I shall teach you the nature of action and inaction, by knowing which you will be liberated from the evil of Samsara, the wheel of birth and death.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_16.mp3]
gita_verse:4.17	<center><big>कर्मणो ह्यपि बोद्धव्यं बोद्धव्यं च विकर्मणः।<br><br>अकर्मणश्च बोद्धव्यं गहना कर्मणो गतिः।।4.17।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>karmaṇo hyapi boddhavyaṁ boddhavyaṁ cha vikarmaṇaḥ<br>akarmaṇaśh cha boddhavyaṁ gahanā karmaṇo gatiḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For there is something to be known even about action, and something to be known about prohibited action; and something needs to be known about inaction. The true nature of action is inscrutable.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>For verily, the true nature of action enjoined by the scriptures should be known, as well as that of forbidden or unlawful action, and of inaction; the nature of action is hard to understand.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_17.mp3]
gita_verse:4.18	<center><big>कर्मण्यकर्म यः पश्येदकर्मणि च कर्म यः।<br><br>स बुद्धिमान् मनुष्येषु स युक्तः कृत्स्नकर्मकृत्।।4.18।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>karmaṇyakarma yaḥ paśhyed akarmaṇi cha karma yaḥ<br>sa buddhimān manuṣhyeṣhu sa yuktaḥ kṛitsna-karma-kṛit<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who finds inaction in action, and action in inaction, is the wise one [possessed of the knowledge of Brahman] among men; they are engaged in yoga and are performers of all actions!<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who sees inaction in action and action in inaction, he is wise among men; he is a yogi and performer of all actions.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_18.mp3]
gita_verse:4.19	<center><big>यस्य सर्वे समारम्भाः कामसङ्कल्पवर्जिताः।<br><br>ज्ञानाग्निदग्धकर्माणं तमाहुः पण्डितं बुधाः।।4.19।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yasya sarve samārambhāḥ kāma-saṅkalpa-varjitāḥ<br>jñānāgni-dagdha-karmāṇaṁ tam āhuḥ paṇḍitaṁ budhāḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The wise call him learned whose actions are all devoid of desires and their thoughts, and whose actions have been burned away by the fire of wisdom.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He whose undertakings are all devoid of desires and selfish purposes, and whose actions have been burned by the fire of knowledge, the wise call him a sage.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_19.mp3]
gita_verse:4.20	<center><big>त्यक्त्वा कर्मफलासङ्गं नित्यतृप्तो निराश्रयः।<br><br>कर्मण्यभिप्रवृत्तोऽपि नैव किञ्चित्करोति सः।।4.20।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tyaktvā karma-phalāsaṅgaṁ nitya-tṛipto nirāśhrayaḥ<br>karmaṇyabhipravṛitto ’pi naiva kiñchit karoti saḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Having given up attachment to the results of action, he who is ever-content, dependent on nothing, does not really do anything even though he is engaged in action.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Having abandoned attachment to the fruits of the action, ever content, depending on nothing, he does not do anything even while being engaged in activity.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_20.mp3]
gita_verse:4.21	<center><big>निराशीर्यतचित्तात्मा त्यक्तसर्वपरिग्रहः।<br><br>शारीरं केवलं कर्म कुर्वन्नाप्नोति किल्बिषम्।।4.21।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>nirāśhīr yata-chittātmā tyakta-sarva-parigrahaḥ<br>śhārīraṁ kevalaṁ karma kurvan nāpnoti kilbiṣham<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One who is without solicitation, who has the mind and senses under control, and is totally without possessions, incurs no sin by performing actions merely for the maintenance of the body.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Without hope, controlling the mind and the self, having abandoned all covetousness, and performing only bodily actions, one incurs no sin.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_21.mp3]
gita_verse:4.22	<center><big>यदृच्छालाभसन्तुष्टो द्वन्द्वातीतो विमत्सरः।<br><br>समः सिद्धावसिद्धौ च कृत्वापि न निबध्यते।।4.22।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yadṛichchhā-lābha-santuṣhṭo dvandvātīto vimatsaraḥ<br>samaḥ siddhāvasiddhau cha kṛitvāpi na nibadhyate<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Remaining satisfied with what comes unasked for, having transcended the dualities, being free from spite, and balanced under success and failure, he is not bound even by performing actions.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Content with what comes to him without effort, free from the pairs of opposites and envy, even-minded in success and failure, he acts yet is not bound.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_22.mp3]
gita_verse:4.23	<center><big>गतसङ्गस्य मुक्तस्य ज्ञानावस्थितचेतसः।<br><br>यज्ञायाचरतः कर्म समग्रं प्रविलीयते।।4.23।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>gata-saṅgasya muktasya jñānāvasthita-chetasaḥ<br>yajñāyācharataḥ karma samagraṁ pravilīyate<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The liberated person, who has rid themselves of attachment and whose mind is fixed in knowledge, has their actions undertaken for a sacrifice completely destroyed.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>To one who is devoid of attachment, who is liberated, whose mind is established in knowledge, and who works for the sake of sacrifice (for the sake of God), the whole action is dissolved.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_23.mp3]
gita_verse:4.24	<center><big>ब्रह्मार्पणं ब्रह्महविर्ब्रह्माग्नौ ब्रह्मणा हुतम्।<br><br>ब्रह्मैव तेन गन्तव्यं ब्रह्मकर्मसमाधिना।।4.24।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>brahmārpaṇaṁ brahma havir brahmāgnau brahmaṇā hutam<br>brahmaiva tena gantavyaṁ brahma-karma-samādhinā<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The ladle is Brahman, the oblations are Brahman, and the offering is poured by Brahman into the fire of Brahman. He who has concentration on Brahman as the objective can only reach Brahman.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Brahman is the oblation; Brahman is the melted butter (ghee); by Brahman is the oblation poured into the fire of Brahman; Brahman indeed shall be attained by one who always sees Brahman in action.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_24.mp3]
gita_verse:4.25	<center><big>दैवमेवापरे यज्ञं योगिनः पर्युपासते।<br><br>ब्रह्माग्नावपरे यज्ञं यज्ञेनैवोपजुह्वति।।4.25।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>daivam evāpare yajñaṁ yoginaḥ paryupāsate<br>brahmāgnāvapare yajñaṁ yajñenaivopajuhvati<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Other yogis undertake sacrifice to gods alone, while others offer the Self as a sacrifice by themselves, in the fire of Brahman.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Some yogis perform sacrifice to the gods alone; while others, who have realized the Self, offer the Self as sacrifice in the fire of Brahman alone.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_25.mp3]
gita_verse:4.26	<center><big>श्रोत्रादीनीन्द्रियाण्यन्ये संयमाग्निषु जुह्वति।<br><br>शब्दादीन्विषयानन्य इन्द्रियाग्निषु जुह्वति।।4.26।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrotrādīnīndriyāṇyanye sanyamāgniṣhu juhvati<br>śhabdādīn viṣhayānanya indriyāgniṣhu juhvati<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Others offer their organs, such as their ears, etc., in the fires of self-control. Others offer the objects, such as sound, etc., in the fires of their organs.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Some again offer the organ of hearing and other senses as a sacrifice in the fire of restraint; others offer sound and other objects of the senses as a sacrifice in the fire of the senses.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_26.mp3]
gita_verse:4.27	<center><big>सर्वाणीन्द्रियकर्माणि प्राणकर्माणि चापरे।<br><br>आत्मसंयमयोगाग्नौ जुह्वति ज्ञानदीपिते।।4.27।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sarvāṇīndriya-karmāṇi prāṇa-karmāṇi chāpare<br>ātma-sanyama-yogāgnau juhvati jñāna-dīpite<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Others offer all the activities of the organs and the activities of the vital force into the fire of the yoga of self-control, lit by Knowledge.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Others again sacrifice all the functions of the senses and those of the breath (vital energy, or Prana) in the fire of the Yoga of self-restraint, kindled by knowledge.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_27.mp3]
gita_verse:4.28	<center><big>द्रव्ययज्ञास्तपोयज्ञा योगयज्ञास्तथापरे।<br><br>स्वाध्यायज्ञानयज्ञाश्च यतयः संशितव्रताः।।4.28।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dravya-yajñās tapo-yajñā yoga-yajñās tathāpare<br>swādhyāya-jñāna-yajñāśh cha yatayaḥ sanśhita-vratāḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Similarly, others are performers of sacrifices through wealth, through austerity, through yoga, and through study and knowledge; others are ascetics with severe vows.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Others again offer wealth, austerity, and Yoga as sacrifice, while ascetics of self-restraint and rigid vows offer the study of scriptures and knowledge as sacrifice.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_28.mp3]
gita_verse:4.29-30	<center><big>अपाने जुह्वति प्राण प्राणेऽपानं तथाऽपरे।<br><br>प्राणापानगती रुद्ध्वा प्राणायामपरायणाः।।4.29।।<br> <br><br>अपरे नियताहाराः प्राणान्प्राणेषु जुह्वति।<br><br>सर्वेऽप्येते यज्ञविदो यज्ञक्षपितकल्मषाः।।4.30।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>apāne juhvati prāṇaṁ prāṇe ’pānaṁ tathāpare<br>prāṇāpāna-gatī ruddhvā prāṇāyāma-parāyaṇāḥ<br> apare niyatāhārāḥ prāṇān prāṇeṣhu juhvati<br>sarve ’pyete yajña-vido yajña-kṣhapita-kalmaṣhāḥ<br><br>apare niyatāhārāḥ prāṇān  prāṇeṣu juhvati<br><br>sarve py 'ete yajña-vido yajña-kṣapita-kalmaṣāḥ <br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Constantly practicing control of the vital forces by stopping the movements of the outgoing and incoming breaths, some offer as a sacrifice the outgoing breath into the incoming breath; while still others, the incoming breath into the outgoing breath. Others, having their food regulated, offer the vital forces in the vital forces. All of them are knowers of the sacrifice and have their sins destroyed by the sacrifice.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Others offer as sacrifice the outgoing breath into the incoming, and the incoming into the outgoing, restraining the flow of the outgoing and the incoming breaths, solely absorbed in the restraint of the breath. Others who regulate their diet offer life-breaths in each life-breath. All these are knowers of sacrifice, whose sins are destroyed through sacrifice.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_29-30.mp3]
gita_verse:4.31	<center><big>यज्ञशिष्टामृतभुजो यान्ति ब्रह्म सनातनम्।<br><br>नायं लोकोऽस्त्ययज्ञस्य कुतो़ऽन्यः कुरुसत्तम।।4.31।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yajña-śhiṣhṭāmṛita-bhujo yānti brahma sanātanam<br>nāyaṁ loko ’styayajñasya kuto ’nyaḥ kuru-sattama<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Those who partake of the nectar left over after a sacrifice reach the eternal Brahman. This world ceases to exist for one who does not perform sacrifices; what, then, to speak of the other world, O best among the Kurus (Arjuna)!<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Those who eat the remnants of the sacrifice, which are like nectar, go to the eternal Brahman. This world is not for the one who does not perform sacrifice; how then can they have the other, O Arjuna?<br><br>[sound:gita_4_31.mp3]
gita_verse:4.32	<center><big>एवं बहुविधा यज्ञा वितता ब्रह्मणो मुखे।<br><br>कर्मजान्विद्धि तान्सर्वानेवं ज्ञात्वा विमोक्ष्यसे।।4.32।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>evaṁ bahu-vidhā yajñā vitatā brahmaṇo mukhe<br>karma-jān viddhi tān sarvān evaṁ jñātvā vimokṣhyase<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Thus, various kinds of sacrifices are spread at the mouth of the Vedas. Know them all to be born of action. Knowing this, you will become liberated.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Thus, manifold sacrifices are spread out before Brahman at the face of Brahman. Know them all to be born of action, and thus knowing, you shall be liberated.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_32.mp3]
gita_verse:4.33	<center><big>श्रेयान्द्रव्यमयाद्यज्ञाज्ज्ञानयज्ञः परन्तप।<br><br>सर्वं कर्माखिलं पार्थ ज्ञाने परिसमाप्यते।।4.33।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhreyān dravya-mayād yajñāj jñāna-yajñaḥ parantapa<br>sarvaṁ karmākhilaṁ pārtha jñāne parisamāpyate<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O destroyer of enemies, knowledge considered as a sacrifice is greater than sacrifices requiring materials. O son of Prtha, all actions in their totality culminate in knowledge.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Superior is wisdom-sacrifice to the sacrifice with objects, O Parantapa (scorcher of the foes). All actions in their entirety, O Arjuna, culminate in knowledge.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_33.mp3]
gita_verse:4.34	<center><big>तद्विद्धि प्रणिपातेन परिप्रश्नेन सेवया।<br><br>उपदेक्ष्यन्ति ते ज्ञानं ज्ञानिनस्तत्त्वदर्शिनः।।4.34।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tad viddhi praṇipātena paripraśhnena sevayā<br>upadekṣhyanti te jñānaṁ jñāninas tattva-darśhinaḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Know that the wise ones who have realized the Truth will impart the Knowledge to you through prostration, inquiry, and service.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Know that the wise who have realized the truth will instruct thee in that knowledge through long prostration, supplication, and service.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_34.mp3]
gita_verse:4.35	<center><big>यज्ज्ञात्वा न पुनर्मोहमेवं यास्यसि पाण्डव।<br><br>येन भूतान्यशेषेण द्रक्ष्यस्यात्मन्यथो मयि।।4.35।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yaj jñātvā na punar moham evaṁ yāsyasi pāṇḍava<br>yena bhūtānyaśheṣheṇa drakṣhyasyātmanyatho mayi<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Knowing this, O Pandava, you will not be deluded again in this way, and through it, you will see all beings, without exception, in the Self and also in Me.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Knowing that thou shalt not, O Arjuna, again be deluded like this; and by that thou shalt see all beings in thyself and also in me.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_35.mp3]
gita_verse:4.36	<center><big>अपि चेदसि पापेभ्यः सर्वेभ्यः पापकृत्तमः।<br><br>सर्वं ज्ञानप्लवेनैव वृजिनं सन्तरिष्यसि।।4.36।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>api ched asi pāpebhyaḥ sarvebhyaḥ pāpa-kṛit-tamaḥ<br>sarvaṁ jñāna-plavenaiva vṛijinaṁ santariṣhyasi<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Even if you are the worst sinner among all sinners, you can still cross over all wickedness with the raft of Knowledge alone.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Even if thou art the most sinful of all sinners, yet thou shalt surely cross over all sins by the raft of knowledge.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_36.mp3]
gita_verse:4.37	<center><big>यथैधांसि समिद्धोऽग्निर्भस्मसात्कुरुतेऽर्जुन।<br><br>ज्ञानाग्निः सर्वकर्माणि भस्मसात्कुरुते तथा।।4.37।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yathaidhānsi samiddho ’gnir bhasma-sāt kurute ’rjuna<br>jñānāgniḥ sarva-karmāṇi bhasma-sāt kurute tathā<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Arjuna, just as a blazing fire reduces wood to ashes, similarly the fire of Knowledge reduces all actions to ashes.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>As the blazing fire reduces fuel to ashes, O Arjuna, so does the fire of knowledge reduce all actions to ash.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_37.mp3]
gita_verse:4.38	<center><big>न हि ज्ञानेन सदृशं पवित्रमिह विद्यते।<br><br>तत्स्वयं योगसंसिद्धः कालेनात्मनि विन्दति।।4.38।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na hi jñānena sadṛiśhaṁ pavitramiha vidyate<br>tatsvayaṁ yogasansiddhaḥ kālenātmani vindati<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Indeed, there is nothing purifying here comparable to Knowledge. One who has become perfected over time through yoga, realizes That in their own heart.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Verily, there is no purifier in this world like knowledge. He who is perfected in Yoga finds it within the Self in due time.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_38.mp3]
gita_verse:4.39	<center><big>श्रद्धावाँल्लभते ज्ञानं तत्परः संयतेन्द्रियः।<br><br>ज्ञानं लब्ध्वा परां शान्तिमचिरेणाधिगच्छति।।4.39।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhraddhāvān labhate jñānaṁ tat-paraḥ sanyatendriyaḥ<br>jñānaṁ labdhvā parāṁ śhāntim achireṇādhigachchhati<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The one who has faith, is diligent, and has control over their organs, attains Knowledge. Achieving Knowledge, one soon attains supreme Peace.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The one who is full of faith, devoted to it, and has subdued their senses obtains this knowledge; and upon obtaining the knowledge, they attain the supreme peace immediately.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_39.mp3]
gita_verse:4.40	<center><big>अज्ञश्चाश्रद्दधानश्च संशयात्मा विनश्यति।<br><br>नायं लोकोऽस्ति न परो न सुखं संशयात्मनः।।4.40।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ajñaśh chāśhraddadhānaśh cha sanśhayātmā vinaśhyati<br>nāyaṁ loko ’sti na paro na sukhaṁ sanśhayātmanaḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One who is ignorant and faithless, and has a doubting mind, perishes. Neither this world nor the next, nor happiness, exists for one who has a doubting mind.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The ignorant, the faithless, and the doubting self go to destruction; there is neither this world nor the other, nor happiness for the doubting one.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_40.mp3]
gita_verse:4.41	<center><big>योगसंन्यस्तकर्माणं ज्ञानसंछिन्नसंशयम्।<br><br>आत्मवन्तं न कर्माणि निबध्नन्ति धनञ्जय।।4.41।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yoga-sannyasta-karmāṇaṁ jñāna-sañchhinna-sanśhayam<br>ātmavantaṁ na karmāṇi nibadhnanti dhanañjaya<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Dhananjaya (Arjuna), actions do not bind one who has renounced actions through yoga, whose doubts have been fully dispelled by Knowledge, and who is not inattentive.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who has renounced actions through Yoga, whose doubts have been dispelled by knowledge, and who is self-possessed—such a one is not bound by actions, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_4_41.mp3]
gita_verse:4.42	<center><big>तस्मादज्ञानसंभूतं हृत्स्थं ज्ञानासिनाऽऽत्मनः।<br><br>छित्त्वैनं संशयं योगमातिष्ठोत्तिष्ठ भारत।।4.42।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tasmād ajñāna-sambhūtaṁ hṛit-sthaṁ jñānāsinātmanaḥ<br>chhittvainaṁ sanśhayaṁ yogam ātiṣhṭhottiṣhṭha bhārata<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Therefore, O scion of the Bharata dynasty, take recourse to yoga and rise up, cutting asunder with the sword of knowledge this doubt in your heart, arising from ignorance.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Therefore, with the sword of knowledge (of the Self), cut asunder the doubt of the self, born of ignorance, residing in your heart, and take refuge in Yoga. Arise, O Arjuna!<br><br>[sound:gita_4_42.mp3]
gita_verse:5.1	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाच<br><br>संन्यासं कर्मणां कृष्ण पुनर्योगं च शंससि।<br><br>यच्छ्रेय एतयोरेकं तन्मे ब्रूहि सुनिश्िचतम्।।5.1।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>sannyāsaṁ karmaṇāṁ kṛiṣhṇa punar yogaṁ cha śhansasi<br>yach chhreya etayor ekaṁ tan me brūhi su-niśhchitam<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O Krsna, you praise renunciation of actions and, at the same time, Karma-yoga. Please tell me for certain which one is better between these two."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O Krishna, you praise renunciation of actions and also yoga. Please tell me conclusively which is better of the two."<br><br>[sound:gita_5_1.mp3]
gita_verse:5.2	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाच<br><br>संन्यासः कर्मयोगश्च निःश्रेयसकरावुभौ।<br><br>तयोस्तु कर्मसंन्यासात्कर्मयोगो विशिष्यते।।5.2।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī bhagavān uvācha<br>sannyāsaḥ karma-yogaśh cha niḥśhreyasa-karāvubhau<br>tayos tu karma-sannyāsāt karma-yogo viśhiṣhyate<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "Both renunciation of actions and Karma-yoga lead to liberation; however, Karma-yoga excels over renunciation of actions."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "Renunciation and the Yoga of action both lead to the highest bliss; but of the two, the Yoga of action is superior to the renunciation of action."<br><br>[sound:gita_5_2.mp3]
gita_verse:5.3	<center><big>ज्ञेयः स नित्यसंन्यासी यो न द्वेष्टि न काङ्क्षति।<br><br>निर्द्वन्द्वो हि महाबाहो सुखं बन्धात्प्रमुच्यते।।5.3।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>jñeyaḥ sa nitya-sannyāsī yo na dveṣhṭi na kāṅkṣhati<br>nirdvandvo hi mahā-bāho sukhaṁ bandhāt pramuchyate<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who neither hates nor craves should be known as a man of constant renunciation.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He should be known as a perpetual Sannyasi who neither hates nor desires; for, free from the pairs of opposites, O mighty-armed Arjuna, he is easily freed from bondage.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_3.mp3]
gita_verse:5.4	<center><big>सांख्ययोगौ पृथग्बालाः प्रवदन्ति न पण्डिताः।<br><br>एकमप्यास्थितः सम्यगुभयोर्विन्दते फलम्।।5.4।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sānkhya-yogau pṛithag bālāḥ pravadanti na paṇḍitāḥ<br>ekamapyāsthitaḥ samyag ubhayor vindate phalam<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The fools, not the learned ones, speak of Sankhya and (Karma-) yoga as being different. Anyone who properly resorts to either one of them gets the results of both.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Children, not the wise, speak of knowledge and the Yoga of action, or the performance of action, as though they are distinct and different; he who is truly established in one, obtains the fruits of both.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_4.mp3]
gita_verse:5.5	<center><big>यत्सांख्यैः प्राप्यते स्थानं तद्योगैरपि गम्यते।<br><br>एकं सांख्यं च योगं च यः पश्यति स पश्यति।।5.5।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br><br>yat sānkhyaiḥ prāpyate sthānaṁ tad yogair api gamyate<br>ekaṁ sānkhyaṁ cha yogaṁ cha yaḥ paśhyati sa paśhyati<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The state that is reached by the Sankhyas, and that is also reached by the yogis, is seen by one who sees Sankhya and yoga as one.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That place which is reached by the Sankhyas or the Jnanis is also reached by the Yogis (Karma Yogis). He who sees knowledge and the performance of action (Karma Yoga) as one, sees truly.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_5.mp3]
gita_verse:5.6	<center><big>संन्यासस्तु महाबाहो दुःखमाप्तुमयोगतः।<br><br>योगयुक्तो मुनिर्ब्रह्म नचिरेणाधिगच्छति।।5.6।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sannyāsas tu mahā-bāho duḥkham āptum ayogataḥ<br>yoga-yukto munir brahma na chireṇādhigachchhati<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But, O mighty-armed one, renunciation is hard to attain without (Karma-) yoga. The meditative man equipped with yoga attains Brahman without delay.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But, O mighty-armed Arjuna, renunciation is hard to attain without Yoga; the sage who is in harmony with Yoga quickly goes to Brahman.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_6.mp3]
gita_verse:5.7	<center><big>योगयुक्तो विशुद्धात्मा विजितात्मा जितेन्द्रियः।<br><br>सर्वभूतात्मभूतात्मा कुर्वन्नपि न लिप्यते।।5.7।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yoga-yukto viśhuddhātmā vijitātmā jitendriyaḥ<br>sarva-bhūtātma-bhūtātmā kurvann api na lipyate<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Endowed with yoga, pure in mind, controlled in body, a conqueror of the organs, the Self of the selves of all beings—he does not become tainted even while performing actions. When this person resorts to nitya and naimittika rites and duties as a means to the achievement of full illumination, and thus becomes fully enlightened, then, even when he acts through the apparent functions of the mind, organs, etc., he does not become affected.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who is devoted to the path of action, whose mind is pure, who has conquered the self, who has subdued his senses, and who realizes his Self as the Self in all beings, though acting, is not tainted.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_7.mp3]
gita_verse:5.8-9	<center><big>नैव किंचित्करोमीति युक्तो मन्येत तत्त्ववित्।<br><br>पश्यन् श्रृणवन्स्पृशञ्जिघ्रन्नश्नन्गच्छन्स्वपन् श्वसन्।।5.8।।<br> <br><br>प्रलपन्विसृजन्गृह्णन्नुन्मिषन्निमिषन्नपि।<br><br>इन्द्रियाणीन्द्रियार्थेषु वर्तन्त इति धारयन्।।5.9।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>naiva kiñchit karomīti yukto manyeta tattva-vit<br>paśhyañ śhṛiṇvan spṛiśhañjighrann aśhnangachchhan svapañśhvasan<br> pralapan visṛijan gṛihṇann unmiṣhan nimiṣhann api<br>indriyāṇīndriyārtheṣhu vartanta iti dhārayan<br><br>pralapan visṛjan gṛhṇann unmiṣan nimiṣann api indriyāṇīndriyārtheṣu vartanta iti dhārayan<br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>- Remaining absorbed in the Self, the knower of Reality should think, 'I certainly do not do anything', even while seeing, hearing, touching, smelling, eating, moving, sleeping, breathing, speaking, releasing, holding, opening, and closing the eyes—remembering that the organs function in relation to the objects of the organs. - Remaining absorbed in the Self, the knower of Reality should think, 'I certainly do not do anything', even while seeing, hearing, touching, smelling, eating, moving, sleeping, breathing, speaking, releasing, holding, opening, and closing the eyes—remembering that the organs function in relation to the objects of the organs.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>I do nothing at all," thus would the harmonized knower of Truth think, seeing, hearing, touching, smelling, eating, going, sleeping, and breathing. Speaking, letting go, seizing, opening, and closing the eyes, one should be convinced that the senses move among the sense-objects.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_8-9.mp3]
gita_verse:5.10	<center><big>ब्रह्मण्याधाय कर्माणि सङ्गं त्यक्त्वा करोति यः।<br><br>लिप्यते न स पापेन पद्मपत्रमिवाम्भसा।।5.10।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>brahmaṇyādhāya karmāṇi saṅgaṁ tyaktvā karoti yaḥ<br>lipyate na sa pāpena padma-patram ivāmbhasā<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One who acts by dedicating their actions to Brahman and by renouncing attachment, they do not become polluted by sin, just as a lotus leaf is not by water.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who does actions, offering them to Brahman and abandoning attachment, is not tainted by sin, just as a lotus leaf is not tainted by water.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_10.mp3]
gita_verse:5.11	<center><big>कायेन मनसा बुद्ध्या केवलैरिन्द्रियैरपि।<br><br>योगिनः कर्म कुर्वन्ति सङ्गं त्यक्त्वाऽऽत्मशुद्धये।।5.11।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kāyena manasā buddhyā kevalair indriyair api<br>yoginaḥ karma kurvanti saṅgaṁ tyaktvātma-śhuddhaye<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>By giving up attachment, the yogis undertake work solely through the body, mind, intellect, and even the organs, for their own purification.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Yogis, having abandoned attachment, perform actions only through the body, mind, intellect, and even the senses, for the purification of the self.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_11.mp3]
gita_verse:5.12	<center><big>युक्तः कर्मफलं त्यक्त्वा शान्तिमाप्नोति नैष्ठिकीम्।<br><br>अयुक्तः कामकारेण फले सक्तो निबध्यते।।5.12।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yuktaḥ karma-phalaṁ tyaktvā śhāntim āpnoti naiṣhṭhikīm<br>ayuktaḥ kāma-kāreṇa phale sakto nibadhyate<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Giving up the results of work by becoming resolute in faith, one attains peace arising from steadfastness. One who is lacking in resolute faith, being attached to the results under the impulse of desire, becomes bound.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The one who is united (the well-poised or harmonized) having abandoned the fruit of action attains eternal peace; whereas the one who is not united (the unsteady or unbalanced), impelled by desire and attached to the fruit, is bound.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_12.mp3]
gita_verse:5.13	<center><big>सर्वकर्माणि मनसा संन्यस्यास्ते सुखं वशी।<br><br>नवद्वारे पुरे देही नैव कुर्वन्न कारयन्।।5.13।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sarva-karmāṇi manasā sannyasyāste sukhaṁ vaśhī<br>nava-dvāre pure dehī naiva kurvan na kārayan<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The embodied man of self-control, having given up all actions mentally, continues happily in the city of nine gates, without doing or causing anyone else to do anything.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Mentally renouncing all actions and being self-controlled, the embodied one happily rests in the nine-gated city, neither acting nor causing others (body and senses) to act.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_13.mp3]
gita_verse:5.14	<center><big>न कर्तृत्वं न कर्माणि लोकस्य सृजति प्रभुः।<br><br>न कर्मफलसंयोगं स्वभावस्तु प्रवर्तते।।5.14।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na kartṛitvaṁ na karmāṇi lokasya sṛijati prabhuḥ<br>na karma-phala-saṅyogaṁ svabhāvas tu pravartate<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Self does not create agency or any objects of desire for anyone, nor does it associate with the results of actions; rather, it is Nature that acts.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Neither does the Lord create agency nor actions for the world, nor union with the fruits of actions; rather, it is Nature that acts.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_14.mp3]
gita_verse:5.15	<center><big>नादत्ते कस्यचित्पापं न चैव सुकृतं विभुः।<br><br>अज्ञानेनावृतं ज्ञानं तेन मुह्यन्ति जन्तवः।।5.15।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>nādatte kasyachit pāpaṁ na chaiva sukṛitaṁ vibhuḥ<br>ajñānenāvṛitaṁ jñānaṁ tena muhyanti jantavaḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Omnipresent neither accepts anyone's sin nor even virtue; knowledge remains covered by ignorance, thus the creatures become deluded.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Lord takes neither the demerit nor the merit of any; knowledge is enveloped by ignorance, and beings are deluded.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_15.mp3]
gita_verse:5.16	<center><big>ज्ञानेन तु तदज्ञानं येषां नाशितमात्मनः।<br><br>तेषामादित्यवज्ज्ञानं प्रकाशयति तत्परम्।।5.16।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>jñānena tu tad ajñānaṁ yeṣhāṁ nāśhitam ātmanaḥ<br>teṣhām āditya-vaj jñānaṁ prakāśhayati tat param<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But in the case of those whose ignorance is destroyed by knowledge (of the Self), their knowledge, like the sun, reveals that supreme Reality.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But to those whose ignorance is destroyed by knowledge of the Self, like the sun, knowledge reveals the Supreme Brahman.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_16.mp3]
gita_verse:5.17	<center><big>तद्बुद्धयस्तदात्मानस्तन्निष्ठास्तत्परायणाः।<br><br>गच्छन्त्यपुनरावृत्तिं ज्ञाननिर्धूतकल्मषाः।।5.17।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tad-buddhayas tad-ātmānas tan-niṣhṭhās tat-parāyaṇāḥ<br>gachchhantyapunar-āvṛittiṁ jñāna-nirdhūta-kalmaṣhāḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Those whose intellect is absorbed in That, whose Self is That, who are steadfast in That, and who have That as their supreme Goal—they attain the state of non-returning, their impurities having been removed by Knowledge.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Their intellect absorbed in That, their self being That, established in That, with That as their supreme goal, they go whence there is no return, their sins dispelled by knowledge.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_17.mp3]
gita_verse:5.18	<center><big>विद्याविनयसंपन्ने ब्राह्मणे गवि हस्तिनि।<br><br>शुनि चैव श्वपाके च पण्डिताः समदर्शिनः।।5.18।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>vidyā-vinaya-sampanne brāhmaṇe gavi hastini<br>śhuni chaiva śhva-pāke cha paṇḍitāḥ sama-darśhinaḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The learned ones look with equanimity on a Brahmana endowed with learning and humility, a cow, an elephant, and even a dog, as well as one who eats dog meat.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Sages look with an equal eye on a Brahmana endowed with learning and humility, on a cow, an elephant, a dog, and even an outcaste.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_18.mp3]
gita_verse:5.19	<center><big>इहैव तैर्जितः सर्गो येषां साम्ये स्थितं मनः।<br><br>निर्दोषं हि समं ब्रह्म तस्माद्ब्रह्मणि ते स्थिताः।।5.19।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ihaiva tair jitaḥ sargo yeṣhāṁ sāmye sthitaṁ manaḥ<br>nirdoṣhaṁ hi samaṁ brahma tasmād brahmaṇi te sthitāḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Here itself is mirth attained by those whose minds are established in sameness. Since Brahman is the same in all and free from defects, they are established in Brahman.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Even here in this world, those whose minds rest in reality overcome birth; Brahman is indeed spotless and real; therefore they are established in Brahman.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_19.mp3]
gita_verse:5.20	<center><big>न प्रहृष्येत्प्रियं प्राप्य नोद्विजेत्प्राप्य चाप्रियम्।<br><br>स्थिरबुद्धिरसम्मूढो ब्रह्मविद्ब्रह्मणि स्थितः।।5.20।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na prahṛiṣhyet priyaṁ prāpya nodvijet prāpya chāpriyam<br>sthira-buddhir asammūḍho brahma-vid brahmaṇi sthitaḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>A knower of Brahman, who is established in Brahman, should have their intellect steady and should not be deluded. They should not get delighted by getting what is desirable, nor become dejected by getting what is undesirable.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Resting in Brahman, with a steady intellect and undeluded, the knower of Brahman neither rejoices upon obtaining what is pleasant nor grieves upon obtaining what is unpleasant.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_20.mp3]
gita_verse:5.21	<center><big>बाह्यस्पर्शेष्वसक्तात्मा विन्दत्यात्मनि यत्सुखम्।<br><br>स ब्रह्मयोगयुक्तात्मा सुखमक्षयमश्नुते।।5.21।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>bāhya-sparśheṣhvasaktātmā vindatyātmani yat sukham<br>sa brahma-yoga-yuktātmā sukham akṣhayam aśhnute<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>With his heart unattached to external objects, he gets the bliss that is in the Self. With his heart absorbed in meditation on Brahman, he acquires undying Bliss.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>With the self unattached to external contacts, he finds happiness in the Self; with the self engaged in the meditation of Brahman, he attains endless happiness.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_21.mp3]
gita_verse:5.22	<center><big>ये हि संस्पर्शजा भोगा दुःखयोनय एव ते।<br><br>आद्यन्तवन्तः कौन्तेय न तेषु रमते बुधः।।5.22।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ye hi sansparśha-jā bhogā duḥkha-yonaya eva te<br>ādyantavantaḥ kaunteya na teṣhu ramate budhaḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Since enjoyments that result from contact with objects are indeed the sources of sorrow, having a beginning and an end, O son of Kunti, the wise one does not delight in them.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The enjoyments that arise from contact are only sources of pain, for they have a beginning and an end, O Arjuna; the wise do not rejoice in them.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_22.mp3]
gita_verse:5.23	<center><big>शक्नोतीहैव यः सोढुं प्राक्शरीरविमोक्षणात्।<br><br>कामक्रोधोद्भवं वेगं स युक्तः स सुखी नरः।।5.23।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhaknotīhaiva yaḥ soḍhuṁ prāk śharīra-vimokṣhaṇāt<br>kāma-krodhodbhavaṁ vegaṁ sa yuktaḥ sa sukhī naraḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One who can withstand here itself, before departing from the body, the impulse arising from desire and anger, that person is a yogi; they are happy.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who is able, while still here in this world, to withstand the impulse born out of desire and anger before the liberation from the body, he is a Yogi, and he is a happy man.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_23.mp3]
gita_verse:5.24	<center><big>योऽन्तःसुखोऽन्तरारामस्तथान्तर्ज्योतिरेव यः।<br><br>स योगी ब्रह्मनिर्वाणं ब्रह्मभूतोऽधिगच्छति।।5.24।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yo 'ntaḥ-sukho 'ntar-ārāmas tathāntar-jyotir eva yaḥ<br>sa yogī brahma-nirvāṇaṁ brahma-bhūto 'dhigachchhati<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One who is content within, whose pleasure is within, and whose light is only within, that yogi, having become Brahman, attains absorption into Brahman.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who is happy within, who rejoices within, and who is illuminated within, that Yogi attains absolute freedom, or Moksha, becoming Brahman himself.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_24.mp3]
gita_verse:5.25	<center><big>लभन्ते ब्रह्मनिर्वाणमृषयः क्षीणकल्मषाः।<br><br>छिन्नद्वैधा यतात्मानः सर्वभूतहिते रताः।।5.25।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>labhante brahma-nirvāṇam ṛiṣhayaḥ kṣhīṇa-kalmaṣhāḥ<br>chhinna-dvaidhā yatātmānaḥ sarva-bhūta-hite ratāḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The seers whose sins have been attenuated, who are free from doubt, whose senses are under control, who are engaged in doing good to all beings, attain absorption in Brahman.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The sages obtain absolute freedom or Moksha when their sins have been destroyed, their dualities have been torn asunder, they are self-controlled, and they are intent on the welfare of all beings.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_25.mp3]
gita_verse:5.26	<center><big>कामक्रोधवियुक्तानां यतीनां यतचेतसाम्।<br><br>अभितो ब्रह्मनिर्वाणं वर्तते विदितात्मनाम्।।5.26।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kāma-krodha-viyuktānāṁ yatīnāṁ yata-chetasām<br>abhito brahma-nirvāṇaṁ vartate viditātmanām<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>To those monks who have control over their internal organs, who are free from desire and anger, who have known the Self, there is absorption into Brahman either way.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Absolute freedom exists on all sides for those self-controlled ascetics who are free from desire and anger, who have controlled their thoughts, and who have realized the Self.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_26.mp3]
gita_verse:5.27-28	<center><big>स्पर्शान्कृत्वा बहिर्बाह्यांश्चक्षुश्चैवान्तरे भ्रुवोः।<br><br>प्राणापानौ समौ कृत्वा नासाभ्यन्तरचारिणौ।।5.27।।<br> <br><br>यतेन्द्रियमनोबुद्धिर्मुनिर्मोक्षपरायणः।<br><br>विगतेच्छाभयक्रोधो यः सदा मुक्त एव सः।।5.28।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sparśhān kṛitvā bahir bāhyānśh chakṣhuśh chaivāntare bhruvoḥ<br>prāṇāpānau samau kṛitvā nāsābhyantara-chāriṇau<br> yatendriya-mano-buddhir munir mokṣha-parāyaṇaḥ<br>vigatechchhā-bhaya-krodho yaḥ sadā mukta eva saḥ<br><br>yatendriya-mano-buddhir  munir   mokṣa-parāyaṇaḥ vigatecchā-bhaya-krodho yaḥ sadā    mukta   eva saḥ<br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>- Keeping external objects outside, fixing the eyes at the juncture of the eye-brows, and controlling the outgoing and incoming breaths that move through the nostrils, the contemplative who has mastery over his organs, mind, and intellect should be fully intent on Liberation and free from desire, fear, and anger. He who is ever thus is verily free. - Keeping external objects outside, fixing the eyes at the juncture of the eye-brows, and controlling the outgoing and incoming breaths that move through the nostrils, the contemplative who has mastery over his organs, mind, and intellect should be fully intent on Liberation and free from desire, fear, and anger. He who is ever thus is verily free.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Shutting out all external contacts and fixing the gaze between the eyebrows, realizing the outgoing and incoming breaths moving within the nostrils. With the senses, mind, and intellect ever controlled, having liberation as their supreme goal, free from desire, fear, and anger, the sage is truly liberated forever.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_27-28.mp3]
gita_verse:5.29	<center><big>भोक्तारं यज्ञतपसां सर्वलोकमहेश्वरम्।<br><br>सुहृदं सर्वभूतानां ज्ञात्वा मां शान्तिमृच्छति।।5.29।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>bhoktāraṁ yajña-tapasāṁ sarva-loka-maheśhvaram<br>suhṛidaṁ sarva-bhūtānāṁ jñātvā māṁ śhāntim ṛichchhati<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One attains peace by knowing Me, who am the great Lord of all the worlds, the enjoyer of sacrifices and austerities, and the friend of all creatures.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who knows Me as the enjoyer of sacrifices and austerities, the great Lord of all the worlds, and the friend of all beings, attains peace.<br><br>[sound:gita_5_29.mp3]
gita_verse:6.1	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाच<br><br>अनाश्रितः कर्मफलं कार्यं कर्म करोति यः।<br><br>स संन्यासी च योगी च न निरग्निर्न चाक्रियः।।6.1।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī bhagavān uvācha<br>anāśhritaḥ karma-phalaṁ kāryaṁ karma karoti yaḥ<br>sa sannyāsī cha yogī cha na niragnir na chākriyaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "He who performs an action which is his duty, without depending on the result of the action, is a monk and a yogi; not so in he who does not keep afire and is actionless."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said: He who performs his bounden duty without depending on the fruits of his actions—he is a sannyasi and a yogi, not he who is without fire and without action.<br><br>[sound:gita_6_1.mp3]
gita_verse:6.2	<center><big>यं संन्यासमिति प्राहुर्योगं तं विद्धि पाण्डव।<br><br>न ह्यसंन्यस्तसङ्कल्पो योगी भवति कश्चन।।6.2।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yaṁ sannyāsam iti prāhur yogaṁ taṁ viddhi pāṇḍava<br>na hyasannyasta-saṅkalpo yogī bhavati kaśhchana<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That which they call monasticism, know that to be Yoga, O Pandava, for nobody who has not given up expectations can be a yogi.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Do you, O Arjuna, know that Yoga is what they call renunciation; no one indeed becomes a Yogi who has not renounced their thoughts.<br><br>[sound:gita_6_2.mp3]
gita_verse:6.3	<center><big>आरुरुक्षोर्मुनेर्योगं कर्म कारणमुच्यते।<br><br>योगारूढस्य तस्यैव शमः कारणमुच्यते।।6.3।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ārurukṣhor muner yogaṁ karma kāraṇam uchyate<br>yogārūḍhasya tasyaiva śhamaḥ kāraṇam uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For the sage who wishes to ascend to (Dhyana-) yoga, action is said to be the means. For that person, once he has ascended to (Dhyana-)yoga, inaction alone is said to be the means.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>For a sage who wishes to attain to Yoga, action is said to be the means; for the same sage who has attained Yoga, inaction is said to be the means.<br><br>[sound:gita_6_3.mp3]
gita_verse:6.4	<center><big>यदा हि नेन्द्रियार्थेषु न कर्मस्वनुषज्जते।<br><br>सर्वसङ्कल्पसंन्यासी योगारूढस्तदोच्यते।।6.4।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yadā hi nendriyārtheṣhu na karmasv-anuṣhajjate<br>sarva-saṅkalpa-sannyāsī yogārūḍhas tadochyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Verily, when a man who has given up thought about everything does not get attached to sense-objects or actions, he is then said to be established in Yoga.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>When a person is not attached to the sense-objects or to actions, having renounced all thoughts, then they are said to have attained Yoga.<br><br>[sound:gita_6_4.mp3]
gita_verse:6.5	<center><big>उद्धरेदात्मनाऽऽत्मानं नात्मानमवसादयेत्।<br><br>आत्मैव ह्यात्मनो बन्धुरात्मैव रिपुरात्मनः।।6.5।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>uddhared ātmanātmānaṁ nātmānam avasādayet<br>ātmaiva hyātmano bandhur ātmaiva ripur ātmanaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One should save oneself by oneself; one should not degrade oneself. For oneself is indeed one's own friend; oneself is indeed one's own enemy.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>One should raise oneself by one's own self alone; let not one lower oneself; for the self alone is one's own friend, and the self alone is one's own enemy.<br><br>[sound:gita_6_5.mp3]
gita_verse:6.6	<center><big>बन्धुरात्माऽऽत्मनस्तस्य येनात्मैवात्मना जितः।<br><br>अनात्मनस्तु शत्रुत्वे वर्तेतात्मैव शत्रुवत्।।6.6।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>bandhur ātmātmanas tasya yenātmaivātmanā jitaḥ<br>anātmanas tu śhatrutve vartetātmaiva śhatru-vat<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who has conquered his own self by the self, his self is his own friend. But for one who has not conquered his own self, his self itself acts like an enemy.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Self is the friend of the self of him by whom the Self has been conquered; but to the unconquered self, this Self stands in the position of an enemy, like an external foe.<br><br>[sound:gita_6_6.mp3]
gita_verse:6.7	<center><big>जितात्मनः प्रशान्तस्य परमात्मा समाहितः।<br><br>शीतोष्णसुखदुःखेषु तथा मानापमानयोः।।6.7।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>jitātmanaḥ praśhāntasya paramātmā samāhitaḥ<br>śhītoṣhṇa-sukha-duḥkheṣhu tathā mānāpamānayoḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The supreme Self of one who has control over the aggregate of his body and organs, and who is tranquil, becomes manifest. He should be poised in the midst of cold and heat, happiness and sorrow, as well as honor and dishonor.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Supreme Self of him who is self-controlled and peaceful remains balanced in cold and heat, pleasure and pain, as well as in honor and dishonor.<br><br>[sound:gita_6_7.mp3]
gita_verse:6.8	<center><big>ज्ञानविज्ञानतृप्तात्मा कूटस्थो विजितेन्द्रियः।<br><br>युक्त इत्युच्यते योगी समलोष्टाश्मकाञ्चनः।।6.8।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>jñāna-vijñāna-tṛiptātmā kūṭa-stho vijitendriyaḥ<br>yukta ityuchyate yogī sama-loṣhṭāśhma-kāñchanaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One whose mind is satisfied with knowledge and realization, who is unmoved, who has his organs under control, is said to be Self-absorbed. The yogi treats all alike, a lump of earth, a stone, and gold.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Yogi who is satisfied with the knowledge and wisdom of the Self, who has conquered the senses, and to whom a clod of earth, a piece of stone, and gold are all the same, is said to have attained Nirvikalpa Samadhi.<br><br>[sound:gita_6_8.mp3]
