Neither by the Vedas, nor by austerity, nor by gift, nor by sacrifice can I be seen in this form as thou hast seen Me so easily.<br><br>[sound:gita_11_52-53.mp3]
gita_verse:11.54	<center><big>भक्त्या त्वनन्यया शक्यमहमेवंविधोऽर्जुन।<br><br>ज्ञातुं दृष्टुं च तत्त्वेन प्रवेष्टुं च परंतप।।11.54।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>bhaktyā tv ananyayā śhakya aham evaṁ-vidho ’rjuna<br>jñātuṁ draṣhṭuṁ cha tattvena praveṣhṭuṁ cha parantapa<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But, O Arjuna, by single-minded devotion am I, in this form, able to be known and seen in reality, and also entered into, O destroyer of foes.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But by single-minded devotion, I can be known, seen, and entered into in reality, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_11_54.mp3]
gita_verse:11.55	<center><big>मत्कर्मकृन्मत्परमो मद्भक्तः सङ्गवर्जितः।<br><br>निर्वैरः सर्वभूतेषु यः स मामेति पाण्डव।।11.55।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>mat-karma-kṛin mat-paramo mad-bhaktaḥ saṅga-varjitaḥ<br>nirvairaḥ sarva-bhūteṣhu yaḥ sa mām eti pāṇḍava<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O son of Pandu, he who works for Me, accepts Me as the supreme goal, is devoted to Me, is devoid of attachment and free from enmity towards all beings—he attains Me.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who does all actions for Me, who regards Me as the Supreme, who is devoted to Me, who is free from attachment, who bears no enmity towards any creature, he comes to Me, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_11_55.mp3]
gita_verse:12.1	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाचएवं सततयुक्ता ये भक्तास्त्वां पर्युपासते।येचाप्यक्षरमव्यक्तं तेषां के योगवित्तमाः।।12.1।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>evaṁ satata-yuktā ye bhaktās tvāṁ paryupāsate<br>ye chāpy akṣharam avyaktaṁ teṣhāṁ ke yoga-vittamāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said: "Which of these devotees, who are ever dedicated and meditate on You, and those who meditate on the Unmanifested and Immutable, are the best experiencers of yoga [here, yoga means samadhi, spiritual absorption]?"<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "Which of them are better versed in Yoga—those who steadfastly worship You, or those who worship the imperishable and the unmanifested?"<br><br>[sound:gita_12_1.mp3]
gita_verse:12.2	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाचमय्यावेश्य मनो ये मां नित्ययुक्ता उपासते।श्रद्धया परयोपेतास्ते मे युक्ततमा मताः।।12.2।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī-bhagavān uvācha<br>mayy āveśhya mano ye māṁ nitya-yuktā upāsate<br>śhraddhayā parayopetās te me yuktatamā matāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "Those who meditate on Me, fixing their minds on Me with steadfast devotion, endowed with supreme faith—they are considered to be the most perfect yogis according to Me."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "In My opinion, those who fix their minds on Me, worship Me ever steadfastly, and are endowed with supreme faith, are the best in Yoga."<br><br>[sound:gita_12_2.mp3]
gita_verse:12.3-4	<center><big>ये त्वक्षरमनिर्देश्यमव्यक्तं पर्युपासते।सर्वत्रगमचिन्त्यं च कूटस्थमचलं ध्रुवम्।।12.3।।<br><br>संनियम्येन्द्रियग्रामं सर्वत्र समबुद्धयः।ते प्राप्नुवन्ति मामेव सर्वभूतहिते रताः।।12.4।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ye tv akṣharam anirdeśhyam avyaktaṁ paryupāsate<br>sarvatra-gam achintyañcha kūṭa-stham achalandhruvam<br> sanniyamyendriya-grāmaṁ sarvatra sama-buddhayaḥ<br>te prāpnuvanti mām eva sarva-bhūta-hite ratāḥ<br><br>sanniyamyendriya-grāmaṁ  sarvatra    sama-buddhayaḥ  te  prāpnuvanti mām eva sarva-bhūta-hite    ratāḥ<br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Those, however, who meditate in every way on the immutable, the indefinable, the unmanifest, which is all-pervasive, incomprehensible, unchanging, immovable, and constant. By fully controlling all the organs and remaining even-minded at all times, they, engaged in the welfare of all beings, attain Me alone.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Those who worship the imperishable, the indefinable, the unmanifest, the omnipresent, the unthinkable, the immovable, and the eternal. Having restrained all the senses, being even-minded everywhere, and intent on the welfare of all beings, they verily come unto Me.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_3-4.mp3]
gita_verse:12.5	<center><big>क्लेशोऽधिकतरस्तेषामव्यक्तासक्तचेतसाम्।<br><br>अव्यक्ता हि गतिर्दुःखं देहवद्भिरवाप्यते।।12.5।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kleśho ’dhikataras teṣhām avyaktāsakta-chetasām<br>avyaktā hi gatir duḥkhaṁ dehavadbhir avāpyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For those whose minds are attached to the Unmanifested, the struggle is greater; for the Goal, which is the Unmanifest, is attained with difficulty by the embodied ones.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Greater is their trouble whose minds are set on the unmanifested, for the goal of the unmanifested is very hard for the embodied to reach.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_5.mp3]
gita_verse:12.6-7	<center><big>ये तु सर्वाणि कर्माणि मयि संन्यस्य मत्पराः।अनन्येनैव योगेन मां ध्यायन्त उपासते।।12.6।।<br><br>तेषामहं समुद्धर्ता मृत्युसंसारसागरात्।भवामि नचिरात्पार्थ मय्यावेशितचेतसाम्।।12.7।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ye tu sarvāṇi karmāṇi mayi sannyasya mat-paraḥ<br>ananyenaiva yogena māṁ dhyāyanta upāsate<br><br>teṣhām ahaṁ samuddhartā mṛityu-saṁsāra-sāgarāt<br>bhavāmi na chirāt pārtha mayy āveśhita-chetasām<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>As for those who, having dedicated all actions to Me and accepted Me as the supreme, meditate on Me with single-minded concentration only-. O son of Prtha, for those who have their minds absorbed in Me, I become, without delay, the deliverer from the sea of the world, which is fraught with death.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But to those who worship Me, renouncing all actions in Me, regarding Me as the supreme goal, meditating on Me with single-minded yoga. To those whose minds are set on Me, O Arjuna, verily I soon become the savior out of the ocean of Samsara.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_6-7.mp3]
gita_verse:12.8	<center><big>मय्येव मन आधत्स्व मयि बुद्धिं निवेशय।निवसिष्यसि मय्येव अत ऊर्ध्वं न संशयः।।12.8।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>mayy eva mana ādhatsva mayi buddhiṁ niveśhaya<br>nivasiṣhyasi mayy eva ata ūrdhvaṁ na sanśhayaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Fix the mind on Me alone; in Me alone let the intellect rest. There is no doubt that hereafter you will dwell in Me alone.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Fix your mind on Me, and your intellect in Me. Then you will certainly live in Me alone hereafter.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_8.mp3]
gita_verse:12.9	<center><big>अथ चित्तं समाधातुं न शक्नोषि मयि स्थिरम्।अभ्यासयोगेन ततो मामिच्छाप्तुं धनञ्जय।।12.9।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>atha chittaṁ samādhātuṁ na śhaknoṣhi mayi sthiram<br>abhyāsa-yogena tato mām ichchhāptuṁ dhanañjaya<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>If, however, you are unable to establish the mind steadily on Me, then, O Dhananjaya, seek to attain Me through the yoga of practice.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>If you are unable to fix your mind steadily on Me, then seek to reach Me through the yoga of constant practice, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_9.mp3]
gita_verse:12.10	<center><big>अभ्यासेऽप्यसमर्थोऽसि मत्कर्मपरमो भव।मदर्थमपि कर्माणि कुर्वन् सिद्धिमवाप्स्यसि।।12.10।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>abhyāse ’py asamartho ’si mat-karma-paramo bhava<br>mad-artham api karmāṇi kurvan siddhim avāpsyasi<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>If you are unable even to practice, be intent on works for Me. By undertaking works for Me as well, you will attain perfection. [Identify with Brahman.]<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>If you are unable to practice even this Abhyasa Yoga, be intent on doing actions for My sake; even by doing actions for My sake, you will attain perfection.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_10.mp3]
gita_verse:12.11	<center><big>अथैतदप्यशक्तोऽसि कर्तुं मद्योगमाश्रितः।सर्वकर्मफलत्यागं ततः कुरु यतात्मवान्।।12.11।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>athaitad apy aśhakto ’si kartuṁ mad-yogam āśhritaḥ<br>sarva-karma-phala-tyāgaṁ tataḥ kuru yatātmavān<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>If you are unable to do even this, then resort to the Yoga for Me and afterwards, control your mind and renounce the results of all your works.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>If you are unable to do even this, then, resort to union with Me and renounce the fruits of all actions with self-control.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_11.mp3]
gita_verse:12.12	<center><big>श्रेयो हि ज्ञानमभ्यासाज्ज्ञानाद्ध्यानं विशिष्यते।ध्यानात्कर्मफलत्यागस्त्यागाच्छान्तिरनन्तरम्।।12.12।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhreyo hi jñānam abhyāsāj jñānād dhyānaṁ viśhiṣhyate<br>dhyānāt karma-phala-tyāgas tyāgāch chhāntir anantaram<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Knowledge is certainly superior to practice; meditation surpasses knowledge. The renunciation of the results of works surpasses meditation. From renunciation, peace follows immediately.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Better indeed is knowledge than practice; better than knowledge is meditation; better than meditation is the renunciation of the fruits of actions: peace immediately follows renunciation.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_12.mp3]
gita_verse:12.13-14	<center><big>अद्वेष्टा सर्वभूतानां मैत्रः करुण एव च।निर्ममो निरहङ्कारः समदुःखसुखः क्षमी।।12.13।।<br><br>सन्तुष्टः सततं योगी यतात्मा दृढनिश्चयः।मय्यर्पितमनोबुद्धिर्यो मद्भक्तः स मे प्रियः।।12.14।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>adveṣhṭā sarva-bhūtānāṁ maitraḥ karuṇa eva cha<br>nirmamo nirahankāraḥ sama-duḥkha-sukhaḥ kṣhamī<br><br>santuṣhṭaḥ satataṁ yogī yatātmā dṛiḍha-niśhchayaḥ<br>mayy arpita-mano-buddhir yo mad-bhaktaḥ sa me priyaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who is not hateful towards any creature, who is friendly and compassionate, who has no concept of 'mine' and no sense of egoism, who remains the same in sorrow and happiness, and who is forgiving; He who is ever content, who is a yogi, who has self-control, who has firm conviction, and who has dedicated his mind and intellect to Me—he who is such a devotee of Mine is dear to Me.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who hates no creature, is friendly and compassionate to all, is free from attachment and egoism, is balanced in pleasure and pain, and is forgiving. Ever content, steady in meditation, self-controlled, possessing firm conviction, with the mind and intellect dedicated to Me, he, My devotee, is dear to Me.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_13-14.mp3]
gita_verse:12.15	<center><big>यस्मान्नोद्विजते लोको लोकान्नोद्विजते च यः।हर्षामर्षभयोद्वेगैर्मुक्तो यः स च मे प्रियः।।12.15।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yasmān nodvijate loko lokān nodvijate cha yaḥ<br>harṣhāmarṣha-bhayodvegair mukto yaḥ sa cha me priyaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He, too, owing to whom the world is not disturbed, and who is not disturbed by the world, who is free from joy, impatience, fear, and anxiety, is dear to me.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He whom the world does not agitate, and who cannot be agitated by the world, and who is freed from joy, anger, fear, and anxiety—he is dear to Me.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_15.mp3]
gita_verse:12.16	<center><big>अनपेक्षः शुचिर्दक्ष उदासीनो गतव्यथः।सर्वारम्भपरित्यागी यो मद्भक्तः स मे प्रियः।।12.16।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>anapekṣhaḥ śhuchir dakṣha udāsīno gata-vyathaḥ<br>sarvārambha-parityāgī yo mad-bhaktaḥ sa me priyaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who has no desires, who is pure, dexterous, impartial, free from fear, and who has renounced every undertaking—such a devotee of Mine is dear to Me.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who is free from wants, pure, expert, unconcerned, and free from pain, renouncing all undertakings and commencements, he who is devoted to Me is dear to Me.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_16.mp3]
gita_verse:12.17	<center><big>यो न हृष्यति न द्वेष्टि न शोचति न काङ्क्षति।शुभाशुभपरित्यागी भक्ितमान्यः स मे प्रियः।।12.17।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yo na hṛiṣhyati na dveṣhṭi na śhochati na kāṅkṣhati<br>śhubhāśhubha-parityāgī bhaktimān yaḥ sa me priyaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who does not rejoice, nor fret, nor lament, nor hanker; who gives up both good and bad, and is filled with devotion—he is dear to Me.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who neither rejoices nor hates, nor grieves nor desires, renouncing both good and evil, and who is full of devotion, is dear to Me.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_17.mp3]
gita_verse:12.18-19	<center><big>समः शत्रौ च मित्रे च तथा मानापमानयोः।शीतोष्णसुखदुःखेषु समः सङ्गविवर्जितः।।12.18।।<br><br>तुल्यनिन्दास्तुतिर्मौनी सन्तुष्टो येनकेनचित्।अनिकेतः स्थिरमतिर्भक्ितमान्मे प्रियो नरः।।12.19।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>samaḥ śhatrau cha mitre cha tathā mānāpamānayoḥ<br>śhītoṣhṇa-sukha-duḥkheṣhu samaḥ saṅga-vivarjitaḥ<br><br>tulya-nindā-stutir maunī santuṣhṭo yena kenachit<br>aniketaḥ sthira-matir bhaktimān me priyo naraḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who is the same towards friend and foe, and in honor and dishonor; who is the same under cold, heat, happiness, and sorrow; who is free from attachment to all. The person to whom denunciation and praise are the same, who is silent, content with anything, homeless, steadfast-minded, and full of devotion is dear to me.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who is the same to foe and friend, and also in honor and dishonor, who is the same in cold and heat, in pleasure and pain, and who is free from attachment. He to whom censure and praise are equal, who is silent, content with anything, homeless, of a steady mind, and full of devotion; that man is dear to me.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_18-19.mp3]
gita_verse:12.20	<center><big>ये तु धर्म्यामृतमिदं यथोक्तं पर्युपासते।श्रद्दधाना मत्परमा भक्तास्तेऽतीव मे प्रियाः।।12.20।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ye tu dharmyāmṛitam idaṁ yathoktaṁ paryupāsate<br>śhraddadhānā mat-paramā bhaktās te ’tīva me priyāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But those devotees who accept Me as the supreme Goal, and with faith seek for this ambrosia—nectar in the form of virtue—which is indistinguishable from the virtues as stated above, they are very dear to Me.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>They who follow this immortal Dharma, endowed with faith and regarding Me as their supreme goal, are exceedingly dear to Me.<br><br>[sound:gita_12_20.mp3]
gita_verse:13.1	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाच<br><br>प्रकृतिं पुरुषं चैव क्षेत्रं क्षेत्रज्ञमेव च।<br><br>एतद्वेदितुमिच्छामि ज्ञानं ज्ञेयं च केशव।।13.1।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>prakṛitiṁ puruṣhaṁ chaiva kṣhetraṁ kṣhetra-jñam eva cha<br>etad veditum ichchhāmi jñānaṁ jñeyaṁ cha keśhava<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Swami Gambhirananda has not translated this verse. gita_verse:13.2	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाचइदं शरीरं कौन्तेय क्षेत्रमित्यभिधीयते।एतद्यो वेत्ति तं प्राहुः क्षेत्रज्ञ इति तद्विदः।।13.2।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī-bhagavān uvācha<br>idaṁ śharīraṁ kaunteya kṣhetram ity abhidhīyate<br>etad yo vetti taṁ prāhuḥ kṣhetra-jña iti tad-vidaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "O son of Kunti, this body is referred to as the 'field'. gita_verse:13.3	<center><big>क्षेत्रज्ञं चापि मां विद्धि सर्वक्षेत्रेषु भारत।<br><br>क्षेत्रक्षेत्रज्ञयोर्ज्ञानं यत्तज्ज्ञानं मतं मम।।13.3।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kṣhetra-jñaṁ chāpi māṁ viddhi sarva-kṣhetreṣhu bhārata<br>kṣhetra-kṣhetrajñayor jñānaṁ yat taj jñānaṁ mataṁ mama<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>And, O scion of the Bharata dynasty, understand Me to be the 'Knower of the field' in all the fields. Knowledge of both the field and the knower of the field is considered by Me to be the knowledge.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_3.mp3]
gita_verse:13.4	<center><big>तत्क्षेत्रं यच्च यादृक् च यद्विकारि यतश्च यत्।स च यो यत्प्रभावश्च तत्समासेन मे श्रृणु।।13.4।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tat kṣhetraṁ yach cha yādṛik cha yad-vikāri yataśh cha yat<br>sa cha yo yat-prabhāvaśh cha tat samāsena me śhṛiṇu<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Hear from Me in brief about all that, what that field is and how it is; what its changes are, and what causes what effect; and who He is, and what His powers are.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Hear from Me in brief what the field is, of what nature it is, what its modifications are, whence it is, who He is, and what His powers are.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_4.mp3]
gita_verse:13.5	<center><big>ऋषिभिर्बहुधा गीतं छन्दोभिर्विविधैः पृथक्।ब्रह्मसूत्रपदैश्चैव हेतुमद्भिर्विनिश्िचतैः।।13.5।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ṛiṣhibhir bahudhā gītaṁ chhandobhir vividhaiḥ pṛithak<br>brahma-sūtra-padaiśh chaiva hetumadbhir viniśhchitaiḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>It has been sung of in various ways by the Rsis, separately by the different branches of Vedic texts, and also by the rational and convincing sentences themselves which are indicative of and lead to Brahman.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Sages have sung in many ways, with various distinctive chants and also with suggestive words indicative of the Absolute, full of reasoning and decisive.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_5.mp3]
gita_verse:13.6	<center><big>महाभूतान्यहङ्कारो बुद्धिरव्यक्तमेव च।इन्द्रियाणि दशैकं च पञ्च चेन्द्रियगोचराः।।13.6।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>mahā-bhūtāny ahankāro buddhir avyaktam eva cha<br>indriyāṇi daśhaikaṁ cha pañcha chendriya-gocharāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The great elements, egoism, intellect, and the Unmanifest itself; the ten organs and the one, and the five objects of the senses;<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The great elements, egoism, intellect, and also the Unmanifested Nature, the ten senses, and one mind, and the five objects of the senses.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_6.mp3]
gita_verse:13.7	<center><big>इच्छा द्वेषः सुखं दुःखं सङ्घातश्चेतनाधृतिः।एतत्क्षेत्रं समासेन सविकारमुदाहृतम्।।13.7।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ichchhā dveṣhaḥ sukhaṁ duḥkhaṁ saṅghātaśh chetanā dhṛitiḥ<br>etat kṣhetraṁ samāsena sa-vikāram udāhṛitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Desire, repulsion, happiness, sorrow, the aggregate (of body and organs), sentience, fortitude—this field, together with its modifications, has been spoken of briefly.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Desire, hatred, pleasure, pain, the aggregate (body), intelligence, and fortitude—the field has thus been briefly described with its modifications.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_7.mp3]
gita_verse:13.8-12	<center><big>अमानित्वमदम्भित्वमहिंसा क्षान्तिरार्जवम्।आचार्योपासनं शौचं स्थैर्यमात्मविनिग्रहः।।13.8।।<br><br>इन्द्रियार्थेषु वैराग्यमनहङ्कार एव च।जन्ममृत्युजराव्याधिदुःखदोषानुदर्शनम्।।13.9।।<br><br>असक्ितरनभिष्वङ्गः पुत्रदारगृहादिषु।नित्यं च समचित्तत्वमिष्टानिष्टोपपत्तिषु।।13.10।।<br><br>मयि चानन्ययोगेन भक्ितरव्यभिचारिणी।विविक्तदेशसेवित्वमरतिर्जनसंसदि।।13.11।।<br><br>अध्यात्मज्ञाननित्यत्वं तत्त्वज्ञानार्थदर्शनम्।एतज्ज्ञानमिति प्रोक्तमज्ञानं यदतोन्यथा।।13.12।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>amānitvam adambhitvam ahinsā kṣhāntir ārjavam<br>āchāryopāsanaṁ śhauchaṁ sthairyam ātma-vinigrahaḥ<br><br>indriyārtheṣhu vairāgyam anahankāra eva cha<br>janma-mṛityu-jarā-vyādhi-duḥkha-doṣhānudarśhanam<br><br>asaktir anabhiṣhvaṅgaḥ putra-dāra-gṛihādiṣhu<br>nityaṁ cha sama-chittatvam iṣhṭāniṣhṭopapattiṣhu<br><br>mayi chānanya-yogena bhaktir avyabhichāriṇī<br>vivikta-deśha-sevitvam aratir jana-sansadi<br><br>adhyātma-jñāna-nityatvaṁ tattva-jñānārtha-darśhanam<br>etaj jñānam iti proktam ajñānaṁ yad ato ’nyathā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Humility, unpretentiousness, non-injury, forbearance, sincerity, service to the teacher, cleanliness, steadiness, and control of the body and its organs; Non-attachment to objects of the senses, and also the absence of egotism; seeing the evil in birth, death, aging, diseases, and miseries; Non-attachment and absence of fondness with regard to sons, wives, homes, etc., and constant equanimity of the mind with regard to the attainment of both the desirable and the undesirable; And unwavering devotion to Me with single-minded concentration; inclination to retreat to a clean place; lack of delight in a crowd of people; Steadfastness in the knowledge of the Self, contemplation on the Goal of the knowledge of Reality—this is spoken of as Knowledge. Ignorance is that which is other than this.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Humility, unpretentiousness, non-injury, forgiveness, uprightness, service to the teacher, purity, steadfastness, and self-control. Indifference to the objects of the senses and also absence of egoism; perceiving the evil in birth, death, old age, sickness, and pain. Non-attachment, non-identification of the Self with son, wife, home, and the rest, and constant even-mindedness in the face of the attainment of both desirable and undesirable. Unswerving devotion to Me through the Yoga of non-separation, resorting to solitary places, and a distaste for the company of people. Constancy in Self-knowledge, the perception of the end of true knowledge—this is declared to be knowledge, and what is opposed to it is ignorance.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_8-12.mp3]
gita_verse:13.13	<center><big>ज्ञेयं यत्तत्प्रवक्ष्यामि यज्ज्ञात्वाऽमृतमश्नुते।अनादिमत्परं ब्रह्म न सत्तन्नासदुच्यते।।13.13।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>jñeyaṁ yat tat pravakṣhyāmi yaj jñātvāmṛitam aśhnute<br>anādi mat-paraṁ brahma na sat tan nāsad uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>I shall speak of that which is to be known, by realizing which one attains immortality. The supreme Brahman is without any beginning; that is called neither being nor non-being.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>I will declare that which is to be known, knowing which one attains immortality; the beginningless Supreme Brahman, which is neither being nor non-being.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_13.mp3]
gita_verse:13.14	<center><big>सर्वतः पाणिपादं तत्सर्वतोऽक्षिशिरोमुखम्।सर्वतः श्रुतिमल्लोके सर्वमावृत्य तिष्ठति।।13.14।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sarvataḥ pāṇi-pādaṁ tat sarvato ’kṣhi-śhiro-mukham<br>sarvataḥ śhrutimal loke sarvam āvṛitya tiṣhṭhati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That Knowable, which has hands and feet everywhere, which has eyes, heads, and mouths everywhere, which has ears everywhere, exists in creatures by pervading them all.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>With hands and feet everywhere, with eyes, heads, and mouths everywhere, with ears everywhere, He exists in the worlds, enveloping all.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_14.mp3]
gita_verse:13.15	<center><big>सर्वेन्द्रियगुणाभासं सर्वेन्द्रियविवर्जितम्।असक्तं सर्वभृच्चैव निर्गुणं गुणभोक्तृ च।।13.15।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sarvendriya-guṇābhāsaṁ sarvendriya-vivarjitam<br>asaktaṁ sarva-bhṛich chaiva nirguṇaṁ guṇa-bhoktṛi cha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Shining through the functions of all the organs, yet devoid of all the organs; unattached, and verily the supporter of all; without quality, and the perceiver of qualities.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Shining by the functions of all the senses, yet without being attached to them; unattached, yet supporting all; devoid of qualities, yet the experiencer of them.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_15.mp3]
gita_verse:13.16	<center><big>बहिरन्तश्च भूतानामचरं चरमेव च।सूक्ष्मत्वात्तदविज्ञेयं दूरस्थं चान्तिके च तत्।।13.16।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>bahir antaśh cha bhūtānām acharaṁ charam eva cha<br>sūkṣhmatvāt tad avijñeyaṁ dūra-sthaṁ chāntike cha tat<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Existing both outside and inside all beings, moving and non-moving, It is incomprehensible due to Its subtlety. It is far away, yet near.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>It is within and without all beings, both the unmoving and the moving; It is subtle and unknowable, and It is near and far away.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_16.mp3]
gita_verse:13.17	<center><big>अविभक्तं च भूतेषु विभक्तमिव च स्थितम्।भूतभर्तृ च तज्ज्ञेयं ग्रसिष्णु प्रभविष्णु च।।13.17।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>avibhaktaṁ cha bhūteṣhu vibhaktam iva cha sthitam<br>bhūta-bhartṛi cha taj jñeyaṁ grasiṣhṇu prabhaviṣhṇu cha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Knowable, though undivided, appears to exist as divided in all beings, and It is the sustainer, devourer, and originator of all beings.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Undivided yet, It exists as if divided in beings; It is to be known as the supporter of beings; It devours and It generates.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_17.mp3]
gita_verse:13.18	<center><big>ज्योतिषामपि तज्ज्योतिस्तमसः परमुच्यते।ज्ञानं ज्ञेयं ज्ञानगम्यं हृदि सर्वस्य विष्ठितम्।।13.18।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>jyotiṣhām api taj jyotis tamasaḥ param uchyate<br>jñānaṁ jñeyaṁ jñāna-gamyaṁ hṛidi sarvasya viṣhṭhitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That is the Light of all lights; It is spoken of as beyond darkness. It is Knowledge, the Knowable, and the Known. It is specially situated in the hearts of all.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That Light of all lights is said to be beyond darkness: knowledge, the knowable, and the goal of knowledge, seated in the hearts of all.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_18.mp3]
gita_verse:13.19	<center><big>इति क्षेत्रं तथा ज्ञानं ज्ञेयं चोक्तं समासतः।मद्भक्त एतद्विज्ञाय मद्भावायोपपद्यते।।13.19।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>iti kṣhetraṁ tathā jñānaṁ jñeyaṁ choktaṁ samāsataḥ<br>mad-bhakta etad vijñāya mad-bhāvāyopapadyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Thus, in brief, the field, Knowledge, and the Knowable have been spoken of. By understanding this, My devotee becomes qualified for My state.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Thus, the field, as well as knowledge and the knowable, have been briefly stated. My devotee, knowing this, enters into My being.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_19.mp3]
gita_verse:13.20	<center><big>प्रकृतिं पुरुषं चैव विद्ध्यनादी उभावपि।विकारांश्च गुणांश्चैव विद्धि प्रकृतिसंभवान्।।13.20।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>prakṛitiṁ puruṣhaṁ chaiva viddhy anādī ubhāv api<br>vikārānśh cha guṇānśh chaiva viddhi prakṛiti-sambhavān<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Know both Nature and the individual soul to be verily without beginning; know the modifications as well as the qualities to be born of Nature.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Know that Nature (matter) and the Spirit are both beginningless, and know also that all modifications and qualities are born from Nature.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_20.mp3]
gita_verse:13.21	<center><big>कार्यकारणकर्तृत्वे हेतुः प्रकृतिरुच्यते।पुरुषः सुखदुःखानां भोक्तृत्वे हेतुरुच्यते।।13.21।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kārya-kāraṇa-kartṛitve hetuḥ prakṛitir uchyate<br>puruṣhaḥ sukha-duḥkhānāṁ bhoktṛitve hetur uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>With regard to the source of the body and its organs, Nature is said to be the cause; the soul is the cause so far as the enjoyment of happiness and sorrow is concerned.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>In the production of the effect and the cause, Nature (matter) is said to be the cause; in the experience of pleasure and pain, the soul is said to be the one responsible.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_21.mp3]
gita_verse:13.22	<center><big>पुरुषः प्रकृतिस्थो हि भुङ्क्ते प्रकृतिजान्गुणान्।कारणं गुणसङ्गोऽस्य सदसद्योनिजन्मसु।।13.22।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>puruṣhaḥ prakṛiti-stho hi bhuṅkte prakṛiti-jān guṇān<br>kāraṇaṁ guṇa-saṅgo ’sya sad-asad-yoni-janmasu<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Since the soul is seated in Nature, therefore it experiences the qualities born of Nature. Contact with the qualities is the cause of its births in good and evil wombs.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The soul seated in Nature experiences the qualities born of Nature; attachment to the qualities is the cause of its birth in good and evil wombs.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_22.mp3]
gita_verse:13.23	<center><big>उपद्रष्टाऽनुमन्ता च भर्ता भोक्ता महेश्वरः।परमात्मेति चाप्युक्तो देहेऽस्मिन्पुरुषः परः।।13.23।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>upadraṣhṭānumantā cha bhartā bhoktā maheśhvaraḥ<br>paramātmeti chāpy ukto dehe ’smin puruṣhaḥ paraḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who is the Witness, the Permitter, the Sustainer, the Experiencer, the great Lord, and who is also spoken of as the transcendental Self, is the supreme Person in this body.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Supreme Soul in this body is also called the observer, the permitter, the sustainer, the enjoyer, the great Lord, and the Supreme Self.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_23.mp3]
gita_verse:13.24	<center><big>य एवं वेत्ति पुरुषं प्रकृतिं च गुणैःसह।सर्वथा वर्तमानोऽपि न स भूयोऽभिजायते।।13.24।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ya evaṁ vetti puruṣhaṁ prakṛitiṁ cha guṇaiḥ saha<br>sarvathā vartamāno ’pi na sa bhūyo ’bhijāyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who knows thus the Person, Nature, and Qualities will not be born again, no matter how he may live.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who thus knows the Spirit and Matter together with their qualities, in whatever condition he may be, he is not reborn.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_24.mp3]
gita_verse:13.25	<center><big>ध्यानेनात्मनि पश्यन्ति केचिदात्मानमात्मना।अन्ये सांख्येन योगेन कर्मयोगेन चापरे।।13.25।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dhyānenātmani paśhyanti kechid ātmānam ātmanā<br>anye sānkhyena yogena karma-yogena chāpare<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Some realize the Self in their intellect through meditation, others through Sankhya-Yoga, and still others through Karma-Yoga, with the help of the internal organ.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Some behold the Self within themselves through meditation, others through the Yoga of knowledge, and still others through the Yoga of action.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_25.mp3]
gita_verse:13.26	<center><big>अन्ये त्वेवमजानन्तः श्रुत्वाऽन्येभ्य उपासते।तेऽपि चातितरन्त्येव मृत्युं श्रुतिपरायणाः।।13.26।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>anye tv evam ajānantaḥ śhrutvānyebhya upāsate<br>te ’pi chātitaranty eva mṛityuṁ śhruti-parāyaṇāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Others, again, who do not know thus, take to thinking after hearing from others; they too, who are devoted to hearing, certainly overcome death.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Others, too, who do not know thus, worship, having heard of It from others; they, too, cross beyond death, regarding what they have heard as the supreme refuge.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_26.mp3]
gita_verse:13.27	<center><big>यावत्सञ्जायते किञ्चित्सत्त्वं स्थावरजङ्गमम्।क्षेत्रक्षेत्रज्ञसंयोगात्तद्विद्धि भरतर्षभ।।13.27।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yāvat sañjāyate kiñchit sattvaṁ sthāvara-jaṅgamam<br>kṣhetra-kṣhetrajña-sanyogāt tad viddhi bharatarṣhabha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O scion of the Bharata dynasty, whatever object, moving or non-moving, comes into existence, know that to be from the combination of the field and the Knower of the field!<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Wherever a being is born, whether unmoving or moving, know thou, O best of the Bharatas (Arjuna), that it is from the union of the field and its knower.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_27.mp3]
gita_verse:13.28	<center><big>समं सर्वेषु भूतेषु तिष्ठन्तं परमेश्वरम्।विनश्यत्स्वविनश्यन्तं यः पश्यति स पश्यति।।13.28।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>samaṁ sarveṣhu bhūteṣhu tiṣhṭhantaṁ parameśhvaram<br>vinaśhyatsv avinaśhyantaṁ yaḥ paśhyati sa paśhyati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who sees the Supreme Lord existing truly in all beings, and the Imperishable among the perishable, sees indeed.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who sees the Supreme Lord existing truly in all beings, the imperishable within the perishable, sees indeed.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_28.mp3]
gita_verse:13.29	<center><big>समं पश्यन्हि सर्वत्र समवस्थितमीश्वरम्।न हिनस्त्यात्मनाऽऽत्मानं ततो याति परां गतिम्।।13.29।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>samaṁ paśhyan hi sarvatra samavasthitam īśhvaram<br>na hinasty ātmanātmānaṁ tato yāti parāṁ gatim<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Since, by truly seeing God, who is present everywhere alike, he does not injure the Self by the Self, he therefore attains the supreme Goal.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>For he who truly sees the same Lord dwelling everywhere does not destroy the Self by the self; rather, he attains the highest goal.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_29.mp3]
gita_verse:13.30	<center><big>प्रकृत्यैव च कर्माणि क्रियमाणानि सर्वशः।यः पश्यति तथाऽऽत्मानमकर्तारं स पश्यति।।13.30।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>prakṛityaiva cha karmāṇi kriyamāṇāni sarvaśhaḥ<br>yaḥ paśhyati tathātmānam akartāraṁ sa paśhyati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>And he who sees actions being done in various ways by Nature itself, and also the Self as the non-agent, he sees.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He sees, who sees that all actions are performed solely by Nature and that the Self is without action.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_30.mp3]
gita_verse:13.31	<center><big>यदा भूतपृथग्भावमेकस्थमनुपश्यति।तत एव च विस्तारं ब्रह्म सम्पद्यते तदा।।13.31।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yadā bhūta-pṛithag-bhāvam eka-stham anupaśhyati<br>tata eva cha vistāraṁ brahma sampadyate tadā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>When one realizes that the state of diversity of living things is rooted in the One, and that their manifestation also comes from That, then one becomes identified with Brahman.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>When a person sees all beings as resting in the One and emanating from the One alone, they then become Brahman.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_31.mp3]
gita_verse:13.32	<center><big>अनादित्वान्निर्गुणत्वात्परमात्मायमव्ययः।शरीरस्थोऽपि कौन्तेय न करोति न लिप्यते।।13.32।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>anāditvān nirguṇatvāt paramātmāyam avyayaḥ<br>śharīra-stho ’pi kaunteya na karoti na lipyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Being without beginning and without end, O son of Kunti, this immutable, supreme Self does not act, nor is It affected [Also translated as tainted.-Tr.], although It exists in the body.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Being without beginning, devoid of any qualities, the Supreme Self, imperishable, though dwelling in the body, O Arjuna, neither acts nor is tainted.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_32.mp3]
gita_verse:13.33	<center><big>यथा सर्वगतं सौक्ष्म्यादाकाशं नोपलिप्यते।सर्वत्रावस्थितो देहे तथाऽऽत्मा नोपलिप्यते।।13.33।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yathā sarva-gataṁ saukṣhmyād ākāśhaṁ nopalipyate<br>sarvatrāvasthito dehe tathātmā nopalipyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>As the all-pervading space is not defiled, due to its subtlety, similarly the Self, present everywhere in bodies, is not defiled.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>As the all-pervading ether is not tainted, due to its subtlety, so the Self seated everywhere in the body is not tainted either.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_33.mp3]
gita_verse:13.34	<center><big>यथा प्रकाशयत्येकः कृत्स्नं लोकमिमं रविः।क्षेत्रं क्षेत्री तथा कृत्स्नं प्रकाशयति भारत।।13.34।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yathā prakāśhayaty ekaḥ kṛitsnaṁ lokam imaṁ raviḥ<br>kṣhetraṁ kṣhetrī tathā kṛitsnaṁ prakāśhayati bhārata<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>As the single sun illuminates this entire world, similarly, O descendant of the Bharata dynasty, the Knower of the field illuminates the entire field.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Just as the one sun illuminates the entire world, so too does the Lord of the field (Supreme Self) illuminate the entire field, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_34.mp3]
gita_verse:13.35	<center><big>क्षेत्रक्षेत्रज्ञयोरेवमन्तरं ज्ञानचक्षुषा।भूतप्रकृतिमोक्षं च ये विदुर्यान्ति ते परम्।।13.35।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kṣhetra-kṣhetrajñayor evam antaraṁ jñāna-chakṣhuṣhā<br>bhūta-prakṛiti-mokṣhaṁ cha ye vidur yānti te param<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Those who, through the eye of wisdom, know the distinction between the field and the Knower of the field, and the annihilation of the Matrix of beings, reach the Supreme.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>They who, by the eye of knowledge, perceive the distinction between the field and its knower, as well as the liberation from the Nature of being, go to the Supreme.<br><br>[sound:gita_13_35.mp3]
gita_verse:14.1	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाचपरं भूयः प्रवक्ष्यामि ज्ञानानां ज्ञानमुत्तमम्।यज्ज्ञात्वा मुनयः सर्वे परां सिद्धिमितो गताः।।14.1।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī-bhagavān uvācha<br>paraṁ bhūyaḥ pravakṣhyāmi jñānānāṁ jñānam uttamam<br>yaj jñātvā munayaḥ sarve parāṁ siddhim ito gatāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "I shall speak again of the supreme knowledge, the best of all knowledge, by realizing which all the contemplatives have reached the highest perfection from here."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "I will again declare to thee that supreme knowledge, the best of all knowledge, having known which all the sages have gone to supreme perfection after this life."<br><br>[sound:gita_14_1.mp3]
gita_verse:14.2	<center><big>इदं ज्ञानमुपाश्रित्य मम साधर्म्यमागताः।सर्गेऽपि नोपजायन्ते प्रलये न व्यथन्ति च।।14.2।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>idaṁ jñānam upāśhritya mama sādharmyam āgatāḥ<br>sarge ’pi nopajāyante pralaye na vyathanti cha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Those who attain identity with Me by resorting to this Knowledge are not born even during creation, nor do they suffer pain during dissolution.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Those who, having taken refuge in this knowledge, have attained unity with Me, are neither born at the time of creation nor disturbed at the time of dissolution.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_2.mp3]
gita_verse:14.3-4	<center><big>मम योनिर्महद्ब्रह्म तस्मिन् गर्भं दधाम्यहम्।संभवः सर्वभूतानां ततो भवति भारत।।14.3।।<br><br>सर्वयोनिषु कौन्तेय मूर्तयः सम्भवन्ति याः।तासां ब्रह्म महद्योनिरहं बीजप्रदः पिता।।14.4।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>mama yonir mahad brahma tasmin garbhaṁ dadhāmy aham<br>sambhavaḥ sarva-bhūtānāṁ tato bhavati bhārata<br><br>sarva-yoniṣhu kaunteya mūrtayaḥ sambhavanti yāḥ<br>tāsāṁ brahma mahad yonir ahaṁ bīja-pradaḥ pitā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>My womb is the great sustainer. In it, I place the seed. From that, O scion of the Bharata dynasty, all things are born. O son of Kunti, whatever forms are born from all the wombs, of them the great sustainer is the womb; I am the father who deposits the seed.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>My womb is the great Brahma; in it I place the germ; thence, O Arjuna, is the birth of all beings. Whatever forms are produced, O Arjuna, in any womb whatsoever, the great Brahma is their womb, and I am the seed-giving father.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_3-4.mp3]
gita_verse:14.5	<center><big>सत्त्वं रजस्तम इति गुणाः प्रकृतिसंभवाः।निबध्नन्ति महाबाहो देहे देहिनमव्ययम्।।14.5।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sattvaṁ rajas tama iti guṇāḥ prakṛiti-sambhavāḥ<br>nibadhnanti mahā-bāho dehe dehinam avyayam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O mighty-armed one, the qualities, viz. sattva, rajas, and tamas, born of Nature, are the immutable embodiments belonging to the body.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>These qualities, O Arjuna, born of Nature, bind fast in the body of the embodied, the indestructible: purity, passion, and inertia.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_5.mp3]
gita_verse:14.6	<center><big>तत्र सत्त्वं निर्मलत्वात्प्रकाशकमनामयम्।सुखसङ्गेन बध्नाति ज्ञानसङ्गेन चानघ।।14.6।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tatra sattvaṁ nirmalatvāt prakāśhakam anāmayam<br>sukha-saṅgena badhnāti jñāna-saṅgena chānagha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Among them, sattva, being pure and nirmala (pure-transparent, i.e., capable of resisting any form of ignorance, and hence an illuminator, i.e. a revealer of Consciousness), is harmless. O sinless one, it binds through attachment to happiness and attachment to knowledge.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Of these, sattva, which is luminous and healthy due to its stainlessness, binds one by attachment to happiness and knowledge, O sinless one.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_6.mp3]
gita_verse:14.7	<center><big>रजो रागात्मकं विद्धि तृष्णासङ्गसमुद्भवम्।तन्निबध्नाति कौन्तेय कर्मसङ्गेन देहिनम्।।14.7।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>rajo rāgātmakaṁ viddhi tṛiṣhṇā-saṅga-samudbhavam<br>tan nibadhnāti kaunteya karma-saṅgena dehinam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Know rajas to be of the nature of passion, born of hankering and attachment. O son of Kunti, it binds the embodied one through attachment to action.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Know, O Arjuna, that Rajas is of the nature of passion, the source of thirst and attachment; it binds fast the embodied one by attachment to action.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_7.mp3]
gita_verse:14.8	<center><big>तमस्त्वज्ञानजं विद्धि मोहनं सर्वदेहिनाम्।प्रमादालस्यनिद्राभिस्तन्निबध्नाति भारत।।14.8।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tamas tv ajñāna-jaṁ viddhi mohanaṁ sarva-dehinām<br>pramādālasya-nidrābhis tan nibadhnāti bhārata<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>On the other hand, know tamas, which deludes all embodied beings, to be born of ignorance. O scion of the Bharata dynasty, it binds through inadvertence, laziness, and sleep.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But know thou Tamas to be born of ignorance, deluding all embodied beings; it binds fast, O Arjuna, through heedlessness, indolence, and sleep.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_8.mp3]
gita_verse:14.9	<center><big>सत्त्वं सुखे सञ्जयति रजः कर्मणि भारत।ज्ञानमावृत्य तु तमः प्रमादे सञ्जयत्युत।।14.9।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sattvaṁ sukhe sañjayati rajaḥ karmaṇi bhārata<br>jñānam āvṛitya tu tamaḥ pramāde sañjayaty uta<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O scion of the Bharata dynasty, sattva attaches one to happiness, rajas to action, while tamas, obscuring knowledge, leads to inadvertence as well.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Sattva attaches to happiness, Rajas to action, O Arjuna, while Tamas, verily shrouding knowledge, attaches to heedlessness.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_9.mp3]
gita_verse:14.10	<center><big>रजस्तमश्चाभिभूय सत्त्वं भवति भारत।रजः सत्त्वं तमश्चैव तमः सत्त्वं रजस्तथा।।14.10।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>rajas tamaśh chābhibhūya sattvaṁ bhavati bhārata<br>rajaḥ sattvaṁ tamaśh chaiva tamaḥ sattvaṁ rajas tathā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O scion of the Bharata dynasty, sattva increases by subduing rajas and tamas; rajas increases by overpowering sattva and tamas; and tamas increases by dominating over sattva and rajas.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Now, O Arjuna, Sattva prevails, having overpowered Rajas and Tamas; then Rajas, having overpowered Sattva and Tamas; and then Tamas, having overpowered Sattva and Rajas.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_10.mp3]
gita_verse:14.11-13	<center><big>सर्वद्वारेषु देहेऽस्मिन्प्रकाश उपजायते।ज्ञानं यदा तदा विद्याद्विवृद्धं सत्त्वमित्युत।।14.11।।<br><br>लोभः प्रवृत्तिरारम्भः कर्मणामशमः स्पृहा।रजस्येतानि जायन्ते विवृद्धे भरतर्षभ।।14.12।।<br><br>अप्रकाशोऽप्रवृत्तिश्च प्रमादो मोह एव च।तमस्येतानि जायन्ते विवृद्धे कुरुनन्दन।।14.13।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sarva-dvāreṣhu dehe ’smin prakāśha upajāyate<br>jñānaṁ yadā tadā vidyād vivṛiddhaṁ sattvam ity uta<br><br>lobhaḥ pravṛittir ārambhaḥ karmaṇām aśhamaḥ spṛihā<br>rajasy etāni jāyante vivṛiddhe bharatarṣhabha<br><br><br>aprakāśho ’pravṛittiśh cha pramādo moha eva cha<br>tamasy etāni jāyante vivṛiddhe kuru-nandana<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>When the illumination of knowledge radiates through all the doors of the senses in this body, then one should know that sattva has greatly increased. O best of the Bharata dynasty, when rajas becomes predominant, these come into being: avarice, restlessness, undertaking of actions, agitation, and craving. O descendant of the Kuru dynasty, when tamas predominates, these come into being without exception: non-discrimination, inactivity, inadvertence, and delusion.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>When the wisdom-light shines through every gate of this body, then it may be known that Sattva is predominant. Greed, activity, the undertaking of actions, restlessness, and longing—these arise when Rajas is predominant, O Arjuna. Darkness, inertia, carelessness, and delusion—these arise when Tamas is predominant, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_11-13.mp3]
gita_verse:14.14-15	<center><big>यदा सत्त्वे प्रवृद्धे तु प्रलयं याति देहभृत्।तदोत्तमविदां लोकानमलान्प्रतिपद्यते।।14.14।।<br><br>रजसि प्रलयं गत्वा कर्मसङ्गिषु जायते।तथा प्रलीनस्तमसि मूढयोनिषु जायते।।14.15।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yadā sattve pravṛiddhe tu pralayaṁ yāti deha-bhṛit<br>tadottama-vidāṁ lokān amalān pratipadyate<br><br>rajasi pralayaṁ gatvā karma-saṅgiṣhu jāyate<br>tathā pralīnas tamasi mūḍha-yoniṣhu jāyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>When an embodied one undergoes death while sattva is exclusively predominant, then he attains the untainted worlds of those who know the highest (entities). When one dies while rajas predominates, they are born among people attached to activity. Similarly, when one dies while tamas predominates, they take birth among the stupid species.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>If the embodied one meets death when Sattva is predominant, then they attain the spotless worlds of the knowers of the Highest. Meeting death in Rajas, he is born among those who are attached to action; and dying in Tamas, he is born in the womb of the thoughtless.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_14-15.mp3]
gita_verse:14.16	<center><big>कर्मणः सुकृतस्याहुः सात्त्विकं निर्मलं फलम्।रजसस्तु फलं दुःखमज्ञानं तमसः फलम्।।14.16।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>karmaṇaḥ sukṛitasyāhuḥ sāttvikaṁ nirmalaṁ phalam<br>rajasas tu phalaṁ duḥkham ajñānaṁ tamasaḥ phalam<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>They say that the result of good work is pure and is born of Sattva. But the result of Rajas is sorrow; the result of Tamas is ignorance.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>They say that the fruit of good action is Sattvic and pure; indeed, the fruit of Rajas is pain, and the fruit of Tamas is ignorance.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_16.mp3]
gita_verse:14.17	<center><big>सत्त्वात्सञ्जायते ज्ञानं रजसो लोभ एव च।प्रमादमोहौ तमसो भवतोऽज्ञानमेव च।।14.17।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sattvāt sañjāyate jñānaṁ rajaso lobha eva cha<br>pramāda-mohau tamaso bhavato ’jñānam eva cha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>From sattva is born knowledge, and from rajas, avarice indeed. From tamas are born inadvertence, delusion, and ignorance, to be sure.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>From Sattva arises knowledge, and greed from Rajas; heedlessness and delusion arise from Tamas, and also ignorance.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_17.mp3]
gita_verse:14.18	<center><big>ऊर्ध्वं गच्छन्ति सत्त्वस्था मध्ये तिष्ठन्ति राजसाः।जघन्यगुणवृत्तिस्था अधो गच्छन्ति तामसाः।।14.18।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ūrdhvaṁ gachchhanti sattva-sthā madhye tiṣhṭhanti rājasāḥ<br>jaghanya-guṇa-vṛitti-sthā adho gachchhanti tāmasāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>People who conform to sattva go higher up; those who conform to rajas stay in the middle; those who conform to tamas, who conform to the actions of the lowest quality, go down.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Those seated in Sattva ascend; those of Rajasic nature dwell in the middle; and those of Tamasic nature, abiding in the function of the lowest Guna, descend.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_18.mp3]
gita_verse:14.19	<center><big>नान्यं गुणेभ्यः कर्तारं यदा द्रष्टानुपश्यति।गुणेभ्यश्च परं वेत्ति मद्भावं सोऽधिगच्छति।।14.19।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>nānyaṁ guṇebhyaḥ kartāraṁ yadā draṣhṭānupaśhyati<br>guṇebhyaśh cha paraṁ vetti mad-bhāvaṁ so ’dhigachchhati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>When the witness sees none other than the qualities as the agent, and knows that which is superior to the qualities, he attains My nature.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>When the seer beholds no agent other than the Gunas and knows that which is higher than them, he attains to My Being.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_19.mp3]
gita_verse:14.20	<center><big>गुणानेतानतीत्य त्रीन्देही देहसमुद्भवान्।जन्ममृत्युजरादुःखैर्विमुक्तोऽमृतमश्नुते।।14.20।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>guṇān etān atītya trīn dehī deha-samudbhavān<br>janma-mṛityu-jarā-duḥkhair vimukto ’mṛitam aśhnute<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Having transcended these three qualities, which are the origin of the body, the embodied one becomes free from birth, death, old age, and sorrows, and experiences Immortality.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The embodied one, having crossed beyond these three Gunas from which the body is evolved, is freed from birth, death, decay, and pain, and attains immortality.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_20.mp3]
gita_verse:14.21	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाचकैर्लिंगैस्त्रीन्गुणानेतानतीतो भवति प्रभो।किमाचारः कथं चैतांस्त्रीन्गुणानतिवर्तते।।14.21।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>kair liṅgais trīn guṇān etān atīto bhavati prabho<br>kim āchāraḥ kathaṁ chaitāns trīn guṇān ativartate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O Lord, by what signs is one known who has gone beyond these three qualities? What is their behavior, and how do they transcend these three qualities?"<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "What are the marks of one who has transcended the three qualities, O Lord? What is their conduct, and how do they go beyond these three qualities?"<br><br>[sound:gita_14_21.mp3]
gita_verse:14.22-23	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाचप्रकाशं च प्रवृत्तिं च मोहमेव च पाण्डव।न द्वेष्टि सम्प्रवृत्तानि न निवृत्तानि काङ्क्षति।।14.22।।<br><br>उदासीनवदासीनो गुणैर्यो न विचाल्यते।गुणा वर्तन्त इत्येव योऽवतिष्ठति नेङ्गते।।14.23।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī-bhagavān uvācha<br>prakāśhaṁ cha pravṛittiṁ cha moham eva cha pāṇḍava<br>na dveṣhṭi sampravṛittāni na nivṛittāni kāṅkṣhati<br><br><br>udāsīna-vad āsīno guṇair yo na vichālyate<br>guṇā vartanta ity evaṁ yo ’vatiṣhṭhati neṅgate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "O son of Pandu, he neither dislikes illumination (knowledge), activity, nor delusion when they appear, nor does he long for them when they disappear." He who, sitting like one indifferent, is not distracted by the three qualities; he who, thinking that the qualities alone act, remains firm and does not move surely;<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "When light, activity, and delusion are present, he does not hate them, nor does he long for them when they are absent. He who, seated like one unconcerned, is not moved by the dualities, and who, knowing that the dualities are active, is self-centered and does not move.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_22-23.mp3]
gita_verse:14.24-25	<center><big>समदुःखसुखः स्वस्थः समलोष्टाश्मकाञ्चनः।तुल्यप्रियाप्रियो धीरस्तुल्यनिन्दात्मसंस्तुतिः।।14.24।।<br><br>मानापमानयोस्तुल्यस्तुल्यो मित्रारिपक्षयोः।सर्वारम्भपरित्यागी गुणातीतः स उच्यते।।14.25।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sama-duḥkha-sukhaḥ sva-sthaḥ sama-loṣhṭāśhma-kāñchanaḥ<br>tulya-priyāpriyo dhīras tulya-nindātma-sanstutiḥ<br><br>mānāpamānayos tulyas tulyo mitrāri-pakṣhayoḥ<br>sarvārambha-parityāgī guṇātītaḥ sa uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He to whom sorrow and happiness are alike, who is established in his own Self, to whom a lump of earth, iron, and gold are the same, to whom the agreeable and the disagreeable are the same, who is wise, to whom censure and his own praise are the same; He who is the same under honor and dishonor, who is equitably disposed towards both friends and foes, who has renounced all undertakings—he is said to have gone beyond dualities.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Who is the same in pleasure and pain, who dwells in the Self, to whom a clod of earth, a stone, and gold are all alike, who is the same to the dear and the unfriendly, who is firm, and to whom censure and praise are one and the same. Who is the same in honor and dishonor, the same to friend and foe, abandoning all undertakings, he is said to have transcended the dualities.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_24-25.mp3]
gita_verse:14.26	<center><big>मां च योऽव्यभिचारेण भक्ितयोगेन सेवते।स गुणान्समतीत्यैतान् ब्रह्मभूयाय कल्पते।।14.26।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>māṁ cha yo ’vyabhichāreṇa bhakti-yogena sevate<br>sa guṇān samatītyaitān brahma-bhūyāya kalpate<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>And he who serves Me through the unswerving Yoga of Devotion, he, having gone beyond these qualities, qualifies for becoming Brahman.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>And he who serves Me with unwavering devotion, he, crossing beyond the dualities, is fit for becoming Brahman.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_26.mp3]
gita_verse:14.27	<center><big>ब्रह्मणो हि प्रतिष्ठाऽहममृतस्याव्ययस्य च।शाश्वतस्य च धर्मस्य सुखस्यैकान्तिकस्य च।।14.27।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>brahmaṇo hi pratiṣhṭhāham amṛitasyāvyayasya cha<br>śhāśhvatasya cha dharmasya sukhasyaikāntikasya cha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>For I am the Abode of Brahman—the indestructible, immutable, eternal, Dharma, and absolute Bliss.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>For I am the abode of Brahman, the immortal, immutable, and everlasting Dharma, and absolute bliss.<br><br>[sound:gita_14_27.mp3]
gita_verse:15.1	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाचऊर्ध्वमूलमधःशाखमश्वत्थं प्राहुरव्ययम्।छन्दांसि यस्य पर्णानि यस्तं वेद स वेदवित्।।15.1।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī-bhagavān uvācha<br>ūrdhva-mūlam adhaḥ-śhākham aśhvatthaṁ prāhur avyayam<br>chhandānsi yasya parṇāni yas taṁ veda sa veda-vit<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "They say that the peepul tree, which has its roots upward and its branches downward, and of which the Vedas are the leaves, is imperishable. He who realizes it is a knower of the Vedas."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said: They (the wise) speak of the indestructible peepul tree, with its roots above and branches below, whose leaves are the meters or hymns; he who knows it is a knower of the Vedas.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_1.mp3]
gita_verse:15.2	<center><big>अधश्चोर्ध्वं प्रसृतास्तस्य शाखा     गुणप्रवृद्धा विषयप्रवालाः।अधश्च मूलान्यनुसन्ततानि     कर्मानुबन्धीनि मनुष्यलोके।।15.2।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>adhaśh chordhvaṁ prasṛitās tasya śhākhā<br>guṇa-pravṛiddhā viṣhaya-pravālāḥ<br>adhaśh cha mūlāny anusantatāni<br>karmānubandhīni manuṣhya-loke<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The branches of that Tree, extending downwards and upwards, are strengthened by the qualities and have sense-objects as their shoots. And the roots, which are followed by actions, spread downwards in the human world [According to A.G. and M.S. manusya-loke means a body distinguished by Brahminhood etc.].<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Its branches spread below and above, nourished by the Gunas; its buds are sense-objects, and its roots stretch forth below in the world of men, originating action.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_2.mp3]
gita_verse:15.3-4	<center><big>न रूपमस्येह तथोपलभ्यते    नान्तो न चादिर्न च संप्रतिष्ठा।अश्वत्थमेनं सुविरूढमूल    मसङ्गशस्त्रेण दृढेन छित्त्वा।।15.3।।<br><br>ततः पदं तत्परिमार्गितव्य    यस्मिन्गता न निवर्तन्ति भूयः।तमेव चाद्यं पुरुषं प्रपद्ये    यतः प्रवृत्तिः प्रसृता पुराणी।।15.4।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na rūpam asyeha tathopalabhyate<br>nānto na chādir na cha sampratiṣhṭhā<br>aśhvattham enaṁ su-virūḍha-mūlam<br>asaṅga-śhastreṇa dṛiḍhena chhittvā<br><br><br>tataḥ padaṁ tat parimārgitavyaṁ<br>yasmin gatā na nivartanti bhūyaḥ<br>tam eva chādyaṁ puruṣhaṁ prapadye<br>yataḥ pravṛittiḥ prasṛitā purāṇī<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Its form is not perceived here in that way; nor its end, nor beginning, nor its continuance. After felling this Peepul tree whose roots are well developed, with the strong sword of detachment. Thereafter, that state must be sought, going where they do not return again: I take refuge in that Primeval Person Himself, from whom the eternal Manifestation has ensued.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Its form is not perceived here as such, nor its end, origin, foundation, or resting place; having cut asunder this firmly rooted peepul tree with the strong axe of non-attachment. Then, that goal should be sought for, to which, having gone, none returns again. I seek refuge in that Primeval Purusha, from whence streamed forth the ancient activity or energy.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_3-4.mp3]
gita_verse:15.5	<center><big>निर्मानमोहा जितसङ्गदोषा    अध्यात्मनित्या विनिवृत्तकामाः।द्वन्द्वैर्विमुक्ताः सुखदुःखसंज्ञै    र्गच्छन्त्यमूढाः पदमव्ययं तत्।।15.5।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>nirmāna-mohā jita-saṅga-doṣhā<br>adhyātma-nityā vinivṛitta-kāmāḥ<br>dvandvair vimuktāḥ sukha-duḥkha-sanjñair<br>gachchhanty amūḍhāḥ padam avyayaṁ tat<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The wise ones, free from pride and non-discrimination, who have conquered the evil of association [hatred and love arising from association with foes and friends], who are ever devoted to spirituality, completely free from desires, and free from the dualities of happiness and sorrow, reach that undecaying state.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Free from pride and delusion, victorious over the evil of attachment, dwelling constantly in the Self, their desires having completely turned away, freed from the pairs of opposites known as pleasure and pain, they, the undeluded, reach the eternal goal.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_5.mp3]
gita_verse:15.6	<center><big>न तद्भासयते सूर्यो न शशाङ्को न पावकः।यद्गत्वा न निवर्तन्ते तद्धाम परमं मम।।15.6।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na tad bhāsayate sūryo na śhaśhāṅko na pāvakaḥ<br>yad gatvā na nivartante tad dhāma paramaṁ mama<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Neither the sun nor the moon nor fire illuminates That. That is My supreme Abode, to which they do not return.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Neither does the sun illuminate there, nor the moon, nor the fire; having gone there, they do not return; that is My supreme abode.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_6.mp3]
gita_verse:15.7	<center><big>ममैवांशो जीवलोके जीवभूतः सनातनः।मनःषष्ठानीन्द्रियाणि प्रकृतिस्थानि कर्षति।।15.7।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>mamaivānśho jīva-loke jīva-bhūtaḥ sanātanaḥ<br>manaḥ-ṣhaṣhṭhānīndriyāṇi prakṛiti-sthāni karṣhati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>It is indeed a part of Mine that, becoming the eternal individual soul in the region of living beings, draws the organs, which have the mind as their sixth, and which abide in Nature.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>An eternal portion of Myself having become a living soul in the world of life, draws to itself the five senses, with the mind as the sixth, abiding in Nature.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_7.mp3]
gita_verse:15.8	<center><big>शरीरं यदवाप्नोति यच्चाप्युत्क्रामतीश्वरः।गृहीत्वैतानि संयाति वायुर्गन्धानिवाशयात्।।15.8।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śharīraṁ yad avāpnoti yach chāpy utkrāmatīśhvaraḥ<br>gṛihītvaitāni sanyāti vāyur gandhān ivāśhayāt<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>When the master leaves it and even when he assumes a body, he departs taking these with him, just as the wind carries away odours from their receptacles.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>When the Lord, as the individual soul, obtains a body and when He leaves it, He takes these with Him, just as the wind takes the scents from their seats (flowers, etc.).<br><br>[sound:gita_15_8.mp3]
gita_verse:15.9	<center><big>श्रोत्रं चक्षुः स्पर्शनं च रसनं घ्राणमेव च।अधिष्ठाय मनश्चायं विषयानुपसेवते।।15.9।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrotraṁ chakṣhuḥ sparśhanaṁ cha rasanaṁ ghrāṇam eva cha<br>adhiṣhṭhāya manaśh chāyaṁ viṣhayān upasevate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>This one enjoys the objects by presiding over the ears, eyes, skin, tongue, nose, and mind.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Presiding over the ears, eyes, touch, taste, smell, and mind, it enjoys the objects of the senses.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_9.mp3]
gita_verse:15.10	<center><big>उत्क्रामन्तं स्थितं वापि भुञ्जानं वा गुणान्वितम्।विमूढा नानुपश्यन्ति पश्यन्ति ज्ञानचक्षुषः।।15.10।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>utkrāmantaṁ sthitaṁ vāpi bhuñjānaṁ vā guṇānvitam<br>vimūḍhā nānupaśhyanti paśhyanti jñāna-chakṣhuṣhaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Persons who are diversely deluded do not see it even when it is leaving, residing, experiencing, or in association with the qualities; those with the eye of knowledge see.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The deluded do not see Him who departs, stays, and enjoys; but those who possess the eye of knowledge behold Him.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_10.mp3]
gita_verse:15.11	<center><big>यतन्तो योगिनश्चैनं पश्यन्त्यात्मन्यवस्थितम्।यतन्तोऽप्यकृतात्मानो नैनं पश्यन्त्यचेतसः।।15.11।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yatanto yoginaśh chainaṁ paśhyanty ātmany avasthitam<br>yatanto ‘py akṛitātmāno nainaṁ paśhyanty achetasaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>And the diligent yogis see this one existing within themselves. gita_verse:15.12	<center><big>यदादित्यगतं तेजो जगद्भासयतेऽखिलम्।यच्चन्द्रमसि यच्चाग्नौ तत्तेजो विद्धि मामकम्।।15.12।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yad āditya-gataṁ tejo jagad bhāsayate ’khilam<br>yach chandramasi yach chāgnau tat tejo viddhi māmakam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That light in the sun which illuminates the whole world, that which is in the moon, and that which is in fire—know that light to be Mine.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That light which resides in the sun, illuminating the whole world; that which is in the moon and in the fire—know that light to be Mine.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_12.mp3]
gita_verse:15.13	<center><big>गामाविश्य च भूतानि धारयाम्यहमोजसा।पुष्णामि चौषधीः सर्वाः सोमो भूत्वा रसात्मकः।।15.13।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>gām āviśhya cha bhūtāni dhārayāmy aham ojasā<br>puṣhṇāmi chauṣhadhīḥ sarvāḥ somo bhūtvā rasātmakaḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>And entering the Earth, I sustain the beings through My power; and nourish all the plants by becoming Soma, which is of the nature of sap.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Permeating the earth, I support all beings with My energy; and having become the watery moon, I nourish all herbs.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_13.mp3]
gita_verse:15.14	<center><big>अहं वैश्वानरो भूत्वा प्राणिनां देहमाश्रितः।प्राणापानसमायुक्तः पचाम्यन्नं चतुर्विधम्।।15.14।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ahaṁ vaiśhvānaro bhūtvā prāṇināṁ deham āśhritaḥ<br>prāṇāpāna-samāyuktaḥ pachāmy annaṁ chatur-vidham<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Taking the form of Vaisvanara, and residing in the bodies of creatures, I, in association with Prana and Apana, digest the four kinds of food.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Having become the fire Vaisvanara, I abide in the bodies of living beings and, associated with the Prana and the Apana, digest the fourfold food.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_14.mp3]
gita_verse:15.15	<center><big>सर्वस्य चाहं हृदि सन्निविष्टो    मत्तः स्मृतिर्ज्ञानमपोहनं च।वेदैश्च सर्वैरहमेव वेद्यो    वेदान्तकृद्वेदविदेव चाहम्।।15.15।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sarvasya chāhaṁ hṛidi sanniviṣhṭo<br>mattaḥ smṛitir jñānam apohanaṁ cha<br>vedaiśh cha sarvair aham eva vedyo<br>vedānta-kṛid veda-vid eva chāham<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>And I am seated in the hearts of all. From Me come memory, knowledge, and their loss. I am verily That which has to be known by all the Vedas; I am indeed the author of the Vedanta and the knower of the Vedas.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_15.mp3]
gita_verse:15.16	<center><big>द्वाविमौ पुरुषौ लोके क्षरश्चाक्षर एव च।क्षरः सर्वाणि भूतानि कूटस्थोऽक्षर उच्यते।।15.16।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dvāv imau puruṣhau loke kṣharaśh chākṣhara eva cha<br>kṣharaḥ sarvāṇi bhūtāni kūṭa-stho ’kṣhara uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>There are two kinds of people in the world: the mutable and the immutable. All beings are perishable, and the Kutastha—the unchanging—is called the imperishable.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_16.mp3]
gita_verse:15.17	<center><big>उत्तमः पुरुषस्त्वन्यः परमात्मेत्युदाहृतः।यो लोकत्रयमाविश्य बिभर्त्यव्यय ईश्वरः।।15.17।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>uttamaḥ puruṣhas tv anyaḥ paramātmety udāhṛitaḥ<br>yo loka-trayam āviśhya bibharty avyaya īśhvaraḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But the Supreme Person is different; He is spoken of as the transcendental Self, permeating the three worlds and upholding them, and He is the imperishable God.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But distinct is the Supreme Purusha, called the highest Self, indestructible and Lord, who pervades the three worlds and sustains them.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_17.mp3]
gita_verse:15.18	<center><big>यस्मात्क्षरमतीतोऽहमक्षरादपि चोत्तमः।अतोऽस्मि लोके वेदे च प्रथितः पुरुषोत्तमः।।15.18।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yasmāt kṣharam atīto ’ham akṣharād api chottamaḥ<br>ato ’smi loke vede cha prathitaḥ puruṣhottamaḥ<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Since I am transcendental to the mutable and above even the immutable, therefore I am well known in the world and in the Vedas as the supreme Person.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>As I transcend the perishable and am even higher than the imperishable, I am declared to be the highest Purusha in the world and in the Vedas.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_18.mp3]
gita_verse:15.19	<center><big>यो मामेवमसम्मूढो जानाति पुरुषोत्तमम्।स सर्वविद्भजति मां सर्वभावेन भारत।।15.19।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yo mām evam asammūḍho jānāti puruṣhottamam<br>sa sarva-vid bhajati māṁ sarva-bhāvena bhārata<br><br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O scion of the Bharata dynasty, he who, being free from delusion, knows Me, the supreme Person, thus, is all-knowing and adores Me with his whole being.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who, undeluded, knows Me as the highest Purusha, he, knowing all, worships Me with his whole being (heart), O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_15_19.mp3]
gita_verse:15.20	<center><big>इति गुह्यतमं शास्त्रमिदमुक्तं मयाऽनघ।एतद्बुद्ध्वा बुद्धिमान्स्यात्कृतकृत्यश्च भारत।।15.20।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>iti guhyatamaṁ śhāstram idam uktaṁ mayānagha<br>etad buddhvā buddhimān syāt kṛita-kṛityaśh cha bhārata<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O sinless one, I have thus uttered this most secret scripture. gita_verse:16.1-3	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाच<br><br>अभयं सत्त्वसंशुद्धिः ज्ञानयोगव्यवस्थितिः।<br><br>दानं दमश्च यज्ञश्च स्वाध्यायस्तप आर्जवम्।।16.1।।<br> <br><br>अहिंसा सत्यमक्रोधस्त्यागः शान्तिरपैशुनम्।दया भूतेष्वलोलुप्त्वं मार्दवं ह्रीरचापलम्।।16.2।।<br><br>तेजः क्षमा धृतिः शौचमद्रोहो नातिमानिता।<br><br>भवन्ति सम्पदं दैवीमभिजातस्य भारत।।16.3।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī-bhagavān uvācha<br>abhayaṁ sattva-sanśhuddhir jñāna-yoga-vyavasthitiḥ<br>dānaṁ damaśh cha yajñaśh cha svādhyāyas tapa ārjavam<br><br>ahinsā satyam akrodhas tyāgaḥ śhāntir apaiśhunam<br>dayā bhūteṣhv aloluptvaṁ mārdavaṁ hrīr achāpalam<br><br>tejaḥ kṣhamā dhṛitiḥ śhaucham adroho nāti-mānitā<br>bhavanti sampadaṁ daivīm abhijātasya bhārata<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said: Fearlessness, purity of mind, persistence in knowledge and yoga, charity, control of the external organs, sacrifice, scriptural study, austerity, and rectitude. Non-injury, truthfulness, absence of anger, renunciation, control of the inner self, absence of vilification, kindness to creatures, non-covetousness, gentleness, modesty, and freedom from restlessness; Vigour, forgiveness, fortitude, purity, freedom from malice, absence of haughtiness—these, O scion of the Bharata dynasty, are the qualities of one born destined to have the divine nature.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said: Fearlessness, purity of heart, steadfastness in knowledge and yoga, almsgiving, control of the senses, sacrifice, study of scriptures, austerity, and straightforwardness. Harmlessness, truth, absence of anger, renunciation, peacefulness, absence of crookedness, compassion for beings, non-covetousness, gentleness, modesty, and absence of fickleness. Vigor, forgiveness, fortitude, purity, absence of hatred, absence of pride—these belong to one born for a divine state, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_16_1-3.mp3]
gita_verse:16.4	<center><big>दम्भो दर्पोऽभिमानश्च क्रोधः पारुष्यमेव च।अज्ञानं चाभिजातस्य पार्थ सम्पदमासुरीम्।।16.4।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dambho darpo ’bhimānaśh cha krodhaḥ pāruṣhyam eva cha<br>ajñānaṁ chābhijātasya pārtha sampadam āsurīm<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O son of Prtha, the attributes of one destined to have the demoniacal nature are religious ostentation, pride, haughtiness, self-conceit, anger, rudeness, and ignorance.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Hypocrisy, arrogance, and self-conceit, anger, harshness, and ignorance—these belong to one who is born for a demoniacal state, O Partha.<br><br>[sound:gita_16_4.mp3]
gita_verse:16.5	<center><big>दैवी सम्पद्विमोक्षाय निबन्धायासुरी मता।मा शुचः सम्पदं दैवीमभिजातोऽसि पाण्डव।।16.5।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>daivī sampad vimokṣhāya nibandhāyāsurī matā<br>mā śhuchaḥ sampadaṁ daivīm abhijāto ’si pāṇḍava<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The divine nature is Liberation, while the demoniacal is considered to be an inevitable bondage. Do not grieve, O son of Pandu! You are destined to possess the divine nature.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The divine nature is deemed conducive to liberation, and the demonic to bondage. Grieve not, O Arjuna, for you are born with divine endowments.<br><br>[sound:gita_16_5.mp3]
gita_verse:16.6	<center><big>द्वौ भूतसर्गौ लोकेऽस्मिन् दैव आसुर एव च।दैवो विस्तरशः प्रोक्त आसुरं पार्थ मे श्रृणु।।16.6।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dvau bhūta-sargau loke ’smin daiva āsura eva cha<br>daivo vistaraśhaḥ prokta āsuraṁ pārtha me śhṛiṇu<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>In this world, there are two kinds of creation of beings: the divine and the demoniacal. gita_verse:16.7	<center><big>प्रवृत्तिं च निवृत्तिं च जना न विदुरासुराः।न शौचं नापि चाचारो न सत्यं तेषु विद्यते।।16.7।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>pravṛittiṁ cha nivṛittiṁ cha janā na vidur āsurāḥ<br>na śhauchaṁ nāpi chāchāro na satyaṁ teṣhu vidyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Neither do the demoniacal persons understand what should be done and what should not be done; nor do they possess purity, good conduct, or truthfulness.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The demoniacal do not know what to do and what to refrain from; they have neither purity, nor right conduct, nor truth.<br><br>[sound:gita_16_7.mp3]

gita_verse:17.1	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाचये शास्त्रविधिमुत्सृज्य यजन्ते श्रद्धयाऽन्विताः।तेषां निष्ठा तु का कृष्ण सत्त्वमाहो रजस्तमः।।17.1।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>ye śhāstra-vidhim utsṛijya yajante śhraddhayānvitāḥ<br>teṣhāṁ niṣhṭhā tu kā kṛiṣhṇa sattvam āho rajas tamaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, But, O Krsna, what is the state of those who, endued with faith, perform sacrifices, distribute wealth, etc. in honour of gods and others, while ignoring the injunctions of the scriptures? gita_verse:17.2	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाचत्रिविधा भवति श्रद्धा देहिनां सा स्वभावजा।सात्त्विकी राजसी चैव तामसी चेति तां श्रृणु।।17.2।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī-bhagavān uvācha<br>tri-vidhā bhavati śhraddhā dehināṁ sā svabhāva-jā<br>sāttvikī rājasī chaiva tāmasī cheti tāṁ śhṛiṇu<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "That faith of the embodied beings, born of their own nature, is threefold—born of sattva, rajas, and tamas. gita_verse:17.3	<center><big>सत्त्वानुरूपा सर्वस्य श्रद्धा भवति भारत।श्रद्धामयोऽयं पुरुषो यो यच्छ्रद्धः स एव सः।।17.3।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sattvānurūpā sarvasya śhraddhā bhavati bhārata<br>śhraddhā-mayo ‘yaṁ puruṣho yo yach-chhraddhaḥ sa eva saḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O scion of the Bharata dynasty, the faith of all beings is in accordance with their minds. gita_verse:17.4	<center><big>यजन्ते सात्त्विका देवान्यक्षरक्षांसि राजसाः।प्रेतान्भूतगणांश्चान्ये यजन्ते तामसा जनाः।।17.4।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yajante sāttvikā devān yakṣha-rakṣhānsi rājasāḥ<br>pretān bhūta-gaṇānśh chānye yajante tāmasā janāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Those with sattva quality worship the gods; those with rajas, the demigods and demons; and those with tamas, ghosts and hosts of spirits.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The sattvic, or pure, men worship the gods; the rajasic, or passionate, worship the yakshas and rakshasas; the others, the tamasic or deluded people, worship ghosts and hosts of nature-spirits.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_4.mp3]
gita_verse:17.5-6	<center><big>अशास्त्रविहितं घोरं तप्यन्ते ये तपो जनाः।दम्भाहङ्कारसंयुक्ताः कामरागबलान्विताः।।17.5।।<br><br>कर्षयन्तः शरीरस्थं भूतग्राममचेतसः।मां चैवान्तःशरीरस्थं तान्विद्ध्यासुरनिश्चयान्।।17.6।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>aśhāstra-vihitaṁ ghoraṁ tapyante ye tapo janāḥ<br>dambhāhankāra-sanyuktāḥ kāma-rāga-balānvitāḥ<br><br>karṣhayantaḥ śharīra-sthaṁ bhūta-grāmam achetasaḥ<br>māṁ chaivāntaḥ śharīra-sthaṁ tān viddhy āsura-niśhchayān<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Those persons who, given to ostentation and pride, and possessed of passion, attachment, and strength, undertake severe austerities not sanctioned by the scriptures; (And those who,) being non-discriminating, torture all the organs in the body as well as even Me who reside in the body—know them to be possessed of demoniacal conviction.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Those men who practice terrific austerities not prescribed by the scriptures, given to hypocrisy and egoism, driven by the force of lust and attachment.
