gita_verse:17.7	<center><big>आहारस्त्वपि सर्वस्य त्रिविधो भवति प्रियः।यज्ञस्तपस्तथा दानं तेषां भेदमिमं श्रृणु।।17.7।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>āhāras tv api sarvasya tri-vidho bhavati priyaḥ<br>yajñas tapas tathā dānaṁ teṣhāṁ bhedam imaṁ śhṛiṇu<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Food, which is dear to all, is of three kinds; likewise, sacrifices, austerity, and charity are also of three kinds. Listen to this classification of them.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The food that is dear to each is threefold, as well as sacrifice, austerity, and almsgiving. Hear the distinction of these.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_7.mp3]
gita_verse:17.8	<center><big>आयुःसत्त्वबलारोग्यसुखप्रीतिविवर्धनाः।रस्याः स्निग्धाः स्थिरा हृद्या आहाराः सात्त्विकप्रियाः।।17.8।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>āyuḥ-sattva-balārogya-sukha-prīti-vivardhanāḥ<br>rasyāḥ snigdhāḥ sthirā hṛidyā āhārāḥ sāttvika-priyāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Foods that augment life, firmness of mind, strength, health, happiness, and delight, and which are succulent, oleaginous, substantial, and agreeable, are dear to one endowed with sattva.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The foods that increase life, purity, strength, health, joy, and cheerfulness (good appetite), which are savory, oily, substantial, and agreeable, are dear to the Sattvic (pure) people.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_8.mp3]
gita_verse:17.9	<center><big>कट्वम्ललवणात्युष्णतीक्ष्णरूक्षविदाहिनः।आहारा राजसस्येष्टा दुःखशोकामयप्रदाः।।17.9।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kaṭv-amla-lavaṇāty-uṣhṇa- tīkṣhṇa-rūkṣha-vidāhinaḥ<br>āhārā rājasasyeṣhṭā duḥkha-śhokāmaya-pradāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Foods that are bitter, sour, salty, very hot, pungent, dry, and burning, producing pain, sorrow, and disease, are dear to one who has rajas.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The foods that are bitter, sour, salty, overly hot, pungent, dry, and burning are liked by the Rajasic and are productive of pain, grief, and disease.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_9.mp3]
gita_verse:17.10	<center><big>यातयामं गतरसं पूति पर्युषितं च यत्।उच्छिष्टमपि चामेध्यं भोजनं तामसप्रियम्।।17.10।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yāta-yāmaṁ gata-rasaṁ pūti paryuṣhitaṁ cha yat<br>uchchhiṣhṭam api chāmedhyaṁ bhojanaṁ tāmasa-priyam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Food that is not properly cooked, lacking in essence, putrid and stale, as well as that which is unfit for sacrifice, is dear to one possessed of tamas.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That which is stale, tasteless, putrid, rotten, rejected, and impure is the food liked by the Tamasic.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_10.mp3]
gita_verse:17.11	<center><big>अफलाकाङ्क्षिभिर्यज्ञो विधिदृष्टो य इज्यते।यष्टव्यमेवेति मनः समाधाय स सात्त्विकः।।17.11।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>aphalākāṅkṣhibhir yajño vidhi-driṣhṭo ya ijyate<br>yaṣhṭavyam eveti manaḥ samādhāya sa sāttvikaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That sacrifice which is in accordance with the injunctions, performed by persons who do not hanker after results, and with the mental conviction that it is surely obligatory, is done through sattva.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That sacrifice which is offered by men without desire for reward, as enjoined by the ordinance (scripture), with a firm faith that doing so is their duty, is Sattvic or pure.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_11.mp3]
gita_verse:17.12	<center><big>अभिसंधाय तु फलं दम्भार्थमपि चैव यत्।इज्यते भरतश्रेष्ठ तं यज्ञं विद्धि राजसम्।।17.12।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>abhisandhāya tu phalaṁ dambhārtham api chaiva yat<br>ijyate bharata-śhreṣhṭha taṁ yajñaṁ viddhi rājasam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But that sacrifice which is performed with an aim for a result, as well as for show—know that sacrifice to be done through rajas, O greatest among the descendants of Bharata.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The sacrifice that is offered, O Arjuna, seeking a reward and for show, know that to be a Rajasic Yajna.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_12.mp3]
gita_verse:17.13	<center><big>विधिहीनमसृष्टान्नं मन्त्रहीनमदक्षिणम्।श्रद्धाविरहितं यज्ञं तामसं परिचक्षते।।17.13।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>vidhi-hīnam asṛiṣhṭānnaṁ mantra-hīnam adakṣhiṇam<br>śhraddhā-virahitaṁ yajñaṁ tāmasaṁ parichakṣhate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>They declare that sacrifice as 'done through tamas' which is contrary to injunction, in which no food is distributed, in which no mantras are used, in which no offerings are made to priests, and which is devoid of faith.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>They declare that sacrifice to be Tamasic which is contrary to the ordinances of the scriptures, in which no food is distributed, and which is devoid of mantras, gifts, and faith.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_13.mp3]
gita_verse:17.14	<center><big>देवद्विजगुरुप्राज्ञपूजनं शौचमार्जवम्।ब्रह्मचर्यमहिंसा च शारीरं तप उच्यते।।17.14।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>deva-dwija-guru-prājña- pūjanaṁ śhaucham ārjavam<br>brahmacharyam ahinsā cha śhārīraṁ tapa uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The worship of gods, twice-borns, venerable persons, and the wise; purity, straightforwardness, celibacy, and non-injury—these are said to be bodily austerities.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Worship of the gods, the twice-born, the teachers, and the wise; purity, straightforwardness, celibacy, and non-injury are all called the austerities of the body.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_14.mp3]
gita_verse:17.15	<center><big>अनुद्वेगकरं वाक्यं सत्यं प्रियहितं च यत्।स्वाध्यायाभ्यसनं चैव वाङ्मयं तप उच्यते।।17.15।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>anudvega-karaṁ vākyaṁ satyaṁ priya-hitaṁ cha yat<br>svādhyāyābhyasanaṁ chaiva vāṅ-mayaṁ tapa uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That speech which causes no pain, which is true, agreeable, and beneficial; as well as the practice of studying the scriptures—is said to be the austerity of speech.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Speech that causes no excitement, is truthful, pleasant, and beneficial; the practice of studying the Vedas is called austerity of speech.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_15.mp3]
gita_verse:17.16	<center><big>मनःप्रसादः सौम्यत्वं मौनमात्मविनिग्रहः।भावसंशुद्धिरित्येतत्तपो मानसमुच्यते।।17.16।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>manaḥ-prasādaḥ saumyatvaṁ maunam ātma-vinigrahaḥ<br>bhāva-sanśhuddhir ity etat tapo mānasam uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Tranquility of mind, gentleness, reticence, withdrawal of the mind, purity of heart—these are what are called mental austerities.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Serenity of mind, good-heartedness, self-control, and purity of nature—this is called mental austerity.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_16.mp3]
gita_verse:17.17	<center><big>श्रद्धया परया तप्तं तपस्तत्ित्रविधं नरैः।अफलाकाङ्क्षिभिर्युक्तैः सात्त्विकं परिचक्षते।।17.17।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhraddhayā parayā taptaṁ tapas tat tri-vidhaṁ naraiḥ<br>aphalākāṅkṣhibhir yuktaiḥ sāttvikaṁ parichakṣhate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>When that threefold austerity is undertaken with supreme faith by people who do not hanker after results and are self-controlled, they speak of it as being born of sattva.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>This threefold austerity, practiced by steadfast men, with the utmost faith, desiring no reward, is called Sattvic.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_17.mp3]
gita_verse:17.18	<center><big>सत्कारमानपूजार्थं तपो दम्भेन चैव यत्।क्रियते तदिह प्रोक्तं राजसं चलमध्रुवम्।।17.18।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>satkāra-māna-pūjārthaṁ tapo dambhena chaiva yat<br>kriyate tad iha proktaṁ rājasaṁ chalam adhruvam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That austerity which is undertaken for earning a name, being honored and worshipped, and also ostentatiously—that is spoken of as born of rajas, belonging to this world, uncertain, and transitory.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The austerity that is practiced with the aim of gaining good reception, honor, and worship, and with hypocrisy, is said to be Rajasic, unstable, and transient.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_18.mp3]
gita_verse:17.19	<center><big>मूढग्राहेणात्मनो यत्पीडया क्रियते तपः।परस्योत्सादनार्थं वा तत्तामसमुदाहृतम्।।17.19।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>mūḍha-grāheṇātmano yat pīḍayā kriyate tapaḥ<br>parasyotsādanārthaṁ vā tat tāmasam udāhṛitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That austerity which is undertaken with a foolish intent, causing pain to oneself or for the destruction of others, is said to be born of tamas.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That austerity which is practised out of a foolish notion, with self-torture, or for the purpose of destroying another, is declared to be of the Tamasic nature.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_19.mp3]
gita_verse:17.20	<center><big>दातव्यमिति यद्दानं दीयतेऽनुपकारिणे।देशे काले च पात्रे च तद्दानं सात्त्विकं स्मृतम्।।17.20।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dātavyam iti yad dānaṁ dīyate ‘nupakāriṇe<br>deśhe kāle cha pātre cha tad dānaṁ sāttvikaṁ smṛitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That gift is referred to as born of sattva which is given with the idea that it should be given, to one who will not serve in return, at the right place, right time, and to the right person.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That gift which is given to one who does nothing in return, knowing it to be a duty to give in a suitable place and time to a worthy person, is held to be Sattvic.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_20.mp3]
gita_verse:17.21	<center><big>यत्तु प्रत्युपकारार्थं फलमुद्दिश्य वा पुनः।दीयते च परिक्लिष्टं तद्दानं राजसं स्मृतम्।।17.21।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yat tu pratyupakārārthaṁ phalam uddiśhya vā punaḥ<br>dīyate cha parikliṣhṭaṁ tad dānaṁ rājasaṁ smṛitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But the gift which is given expecting reciprocation, or with a desire for its result, and grudgingly, is considered to be born of rajas.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>And, that gift which is given with the intention of receiving something in return, or expecting a reward, or begrudgingly, is considered to be Rajasic.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_21.mp3]
gita_verse:17.22	<center><big>अदेशकाले यद्दानमपात्रेभ्यश्च दीयते।असत्कृतमवज्ञातं तत्तामसमुदाहृतम्।।17.22।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>adeśha-kāle yad dānam apātrebhyaśh cha dīyate<br>asat-kṛitam avajñātaṁ tat tāmasam udāhṛitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The gift which is made at an inappropriate place and time, and to undeserving persons, without proper respect and with disdain, is declared to be born of tamas.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The gift that is given in the wrong place and at the wrong time, to unworthy persons, without respect or with insult, is declared to be of a Tamasic nature.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_22.mp3]
gita_verse:17.23	<center><big> तत्सदिति निर्देशो ब्रह्मणस्त्रिविधः स्मृतः।ब्राह्मणास्तेन वेदाश्च यज्ञाश्च विहिताः पुरा।।17.23।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>oṁ tat sad iti nirdeśho brahmaṇas tri-vidhaḥ smṛitaḥ<br>brāhmaṇās tena vedāśh cha yajñāśh cha vihitāḥ purā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>"Om-tat-sat" - this is considered to be the threefold designation of Brahman. gita_verse:17.24	<center><big>तस्मादोमित्युदाहृत्य यज्ञदानतपःक्रियाः।प्रवर्तन्ते विधानोक्ताः सततं ब्रह्मवादिनाम्।।17.24।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tasmād oṁ ity udāhṛitya yajña-dāna-tapaḥ-kriyāḥ<br>pravartante vidhānoktāḥ satataṁ brahma-vādinām<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Therefore, acts of sacrifice, charity, and austerity, as prescribed through injunctions, of those who study and expound the Vedas, always commence after uttering the syllable ‘Om’.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Therefore, with the utterance of "Om," the acts of sacrifice, gift, and austerity, as enjoined in the scriptures, are always begun by the students of Brahman.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_24.mp3]
gita_verse:17.25	<center><big>तदित्यनभिसन्धाय फलं यज्ञतपःक्रियाः।दानक्रियाश्च विविधाः क्रियन्ते मोक्षकाङ्क्षि।।17.25।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tad ity anabhisandhāya phalaṁ yajña-tapaḥ-kriyāḥ<br>dāna-kriyāśh cha vividhāḥ kriyante mokṣha-kāṅkṣhibhiḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>After uttering the word "tat," acts of sacrifice and austerity, as well as various acts of charity, are performed without regard for results by persons aspiring for liberation.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Uttering "Tat," without aiming for the fruits, are the acts of sacrifice, austerity, and the various acts of gifts performed by those seeking liberation.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_25.mp3]
gita_verse:17.26-27	<center><big>सद्भावे साधुभावे च सदित्येतत्प्रयुज्यते।प्रशस्ते कर्मणि तथा सच्छब्दः पार्थ युज्यते।।17.26।।<br><br>यज्ञे तपसि दाने च स्थितिः सदिति चोच्यते।कर्म चैव तदर्थीयं सदित्येवाभिधीयते।।17.27।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sad-bhāve sādhu-bhāve cha sad ity etat prayujyate<br>praśhaste karmaṇi tathā sach-chhabdaḥ pārtha yujyate<br><br>yajñe tapasi dāne cha sthitiḥ sad iti chochyate<br>karma chaiva tad-arthīyaṁ sad ity evābhidhīyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>This word "sat" is used with regard to something coming into being and someone becoming good. Likewise, O son of Prtha, the word "sat" is used with regard to an auspicious rite. And the steadfastness in sacrifice, austerity, and charity is spoken of as sat (good). And even the action meant for these is, indeed, called as sat.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The word "Sat" is used to refer to reality and goodness; likewise, O Arjuna, the word "Sat" is used to refer to an auspicious act. Steadfastness in sacrifice, austerity, and gift is also called 'Sat', and action in connection with these, or for the sake of the Supreme, is also called 'Sat'.<br><br>[sound:gita_17_26-27.mp3]
gita_verse:17.28	<center><big>अश्रद्धया हुतं दत्तं तपस्तप्तं कृतं च यत्।असदित्युच्यते पार्थ न च तत्प्रेत्य नो इह।।17.28।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>aśhraddhayā hutaṁ dattaṁ tapas taptaṁ kṛitaṁ cha yat<br>asad ity uchyate pārtha na cha tat pretya no iha<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O son of Prtha, whatever is offered in sacrifice and given in charity, as also whatever austerity is undertaken or whatever is done without faith, is said to be of no avail. gita_verse:18.1	<center><big>अर्जुन उवाच<br><br>संन्यासस्य महाबाहो तत्त्वमिच्छामि वेदितुम्।<br><br>त्यागस्य च हृषीकेश पृथक्केशिनिषूदन।।18.1।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>arjuna uvācha<br>sannyāsasya mahā-bāho tattvam ichchhāmi veditum<br>tyāgasya cha hṛiṣhīkeśha pṛithak keśhi-niṣhūdana<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, O mighty-armed Hrsikesa, O slayer of Kesi, I want to know separately the truth about sannyasa as well as about tyaga.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Arjuna said, "O mighty-armed Hrishikesa, I desire to know the essence or truth of renunciation and abandonment severally, O slayer of Kesi."<br><br>[sound:gita_18_1.mp3]
gita_verse:18.2	<center><big>श्री भगवानुवाच<br><br>काम्यानां कर्मणां न्यासं संन्यासं कवयो विदुः।<br><br>सर्वकर्मफलत्यागं प्राहुस्त्यागं विचक्षणाः।।18.2।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhrī-bhagavān uvācha<br>kāmyānāṁ karmaṇāṁ nyāsaṁ sannyāsaṁ kavayo viduḥ<br>sarva-karma-phala-tyāgaṁ prāhus tyāgaṁ vichakṣhaṇāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The Blessed Lord said, "The learned ones know sannyasa to be the giving up of actions done with a desire for reward. gita_verse:18.3	<center><big>त्याज्यं दोषवदित्येके कर्म प्राहुर्मनीषिणः।<br><br>यज्ञदानतपःकर्म न त्याज्यमिति चापरे।।18.3।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tyājyaṁ doṣha-vad ity eke karma prāhur manīṣhiṇaḥ<br>yajña-dāna-tapaḥ-karma na tyājyam iti chāpare<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Some learned persons say that action, beset with evil as it is, should be abandoned, and others say that the practice of sacrifice, charity, and austerity should not be abandoned.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Some philosophers declare that actions should be abandoned as evil; while others declare that acts of sacrifice, gift, and austerity should not be relinquished.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_3.mp3]
gita_verse:18.4	<center><big>निश्चयं श्रृणु मे तत्र त्यागे भरतसत्तम।त्यागो हि पुरुषव्याघ्र त्रिविधः संप्रकीर्तितः।।18.4।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>niśhchayaṁ śhṛiṇu me tatra tyāge bharata-sattama<br>tyāgo hi puruṣha-vyāghra tri-vidhaḥ samprakīrtitaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O the most excellent among the descendants of Bharata, hear from Me the firm conclusion regarding that tyaga. For, O greatest among men, tyaga has been clearly declared to be of three kinds.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Hear from Me the conclusion or the final truth about this abandonment, O best of the Bharatas; abandonment, indeed, O best of men, has been declared to be of three kinds.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_4.mp3]
gita_verse:18.5	<center><big>यज्ञदानतपःकर्म न त्याज्यं कार्यमेव तत्।यज्ञो दानं तपश्चैव पावनानि मनीषिणाम्।।18.5।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yajña-dāna-tapaḥ-karma na tyājyaṁ kāryam eva tat<br>yajño dānaṁ tapaśh chaiva pāvanāni manīṣhiṇām<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The practice of sacrifice, charity, and austerity should not be abandoned; it should certainly be undertaken. Sacrifice, charity, and austerity are indeed the purifiers of the wise.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Acts of sacrifice, gift, and austerity should not be abandoned, but should be performed; for sacrifice, gift, and austerity are the purifiers of the wise.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_5.mp3]
gita_verse:18.6	<center><big>एतान्यपि तु कर्माणि सङ्गं त्यक्त्वा फलानि च।कर्तव्यानीति मे पार्थ निश्िचतं मतमुत्तमम्।।18.6।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>etāny api tu karmāṇi saṅgaṁ tyaktvā phalāni cha<br>kartavyānīti me pārtha niśhchitaṁ matam uttamam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But even these actions must be undertaken by renouncing attachment and hankering for results. This is My firm and definitive conclusion, O Partha.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But even these actions should be performed, leaving aside attachment and the desire for rewards, O Arjuna; this is my certain and most assured conviction.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_6.mp3]
gita_verse:18.7	<center><big>नियतस्य तु संन्यासः कर्मणो नोपपद्यते।मोहात्तस्य परित्यागस्तामसः परिकीर्तितः।।18.7।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>niyatasya tu sannyāsaḥ karmaṇo nopapadyate<br>mohāt tasya parityāgas tāmasaḥ parikīrtitaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Abandoning one's daily obligatory acts is not justifiable; giving up those through delusion is said to be rooted in tamas.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Verily, the renunciation of obligatory action is not proper; the abandonment of the same out of delusion is declared to be Tamasic.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_7.mp3]
gita_verse:18.8	<center><big>दुःखमित्येव यत्कर्म कायक्लेशभयात्त्यजेत्।स कृत्वा राजसं त्यागं नैव त्यागफलं लभेत्।।18.8।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>duḥkham ity eva yat karma kāya-kleśha-bhayāt tyajet<br>sa kṛitvā rājasaṁ tyāgaṁ naiva tyāga-phalaṁ labhet<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Whatever action one may relinquish merely as being painful, out of fear of physical suffering, he, having resorted to renunciation based on rajas, will surely not acquire the fruits of renunciation.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who abandons action out of fear of bodily trouble (because it is painful), does not obtain the merit of renunciation by performing such Rajasic renunciation.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_8.mp3]
gita_verse:18.9	<center><big>कार्यमित्येव यत्कर्म नियतं क्रियतेऽर्जुन।सङ्गं त्यक्त्वा फलं चैव स त्यागः सात्त्विको मतः।।18.9।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kāryam ity eva yat karma niyataṁ kriyate ‘rjuna<br>saṅgaṁ tyaktvā phalaṁ chaiva sa tyāgaḥ sāttviko mataḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Whatever obligatory duty is performed just because it is a bounden duty, O Arjuna, by giving up attachment and the results as well—that renunciation is considered to be based on sattva.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Whatever obligatory action is done, O Arjuna, merely because it ought to be done, abandoning attachment and also the desire for reward, that renunciation is regarded as sattvic (pure).<br><br>[sound:gita_18_9.mp3]
gita_verse:18.10	<center><big>न द्वेष्ट्यकुशलं कर्म कुशले नानुषज्जते।त्यागी सत्त्वसमाविष्टो मेधावी छिन्नसंशयः।।18.10।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na dveṣhṭy akuśhalaṁ karma kuśhale nānuṣhajjate<br>tyāgī sattva-samāviṣhṭo medhāvī chhinna-sanśhayaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The man of renunciation, imbued with sattva, wise and free from doubts, does not hate unbecoming action, nor does he become attached to becoming activity.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The man of renunciation, pervaded by purity, intelligent, and with his doubts cut asunder, does not hate an unpleasant task nor is he attached to a pleasant one.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_10.mp3]
gita_verse:18.11	<center><big>न हि देहभृता शक्यं त्यक्तुं कर्माण्यशेषतः।यस्तु कर्मफलत्यागी स त्यागीत्यभिधीयते।।18.11।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na hi deha-bhṛitā śhakyaṁ tyaktuṁ karmāṇy aśheṣhataḥ<br>yas tu karma-phala-tyāgī sa tyāgīty abhidhīyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Since it is not possible for one who holds onto a body to give up actions entirely, therefore he who renounces the results of his actions is called a man of renunciation.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Indeed, it is not possible for an embodied being to completely abandon actions; however, he who relinquishes the rewards of actions is truly called a man of renunciation.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_11.mp3]
gita_verse:18.12	<center><big>अनिष्टमिष्टं मिश्रं च त्रिविधं कर्मणः फलम्।भवत्यत्यागिनां प्रेत्य न तु संन्यासिनां क्वचित्।।18.12।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>aniṣhṭam iṣhṭaṁ miśhraṁ cha tri-vidhaṁ karmaṇaḥ phalam<br>bhavaty atyāgināṁ pretya na tu sannyāsināṁ kvachit<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The threefold results of actions—the undesirable, the desirable, and the mixed—accrue after death to those who do not resort to renunciation, but never to those who resort to renunciation.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The threefold fruit of action (evil, good, and mixed) accrues after death to those who do not abandon it, but never to those who do.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_12.mp3]
gita_verse:18.13	<center><big>पञ्चैतानि महाबाहो कारणानि निबोध मे।सांख्ये कृतान्ते प्रोक्तानि सिद्धये सर्वकर्मणाम्।।18.13।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>pañchaitāni mahā-bāho kāraṇāni nibodha me<br>sānkhye kṛitānte proktāni siddhaye sarva-karmaṇām<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O mighty-armed one, learn from Me these five factors for the accomplishment of all actions, which have been spoken of in the Vedanta, in which actions terminate.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Learn from Me, O mighty-armed Arjuna, these five causes, as declared in the Sankhya system, for the accomplishment of all actions.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_13.mp3]
gita_verse:18.14	<center><big>अधिष्ठानं तथा कर्ता करणं च पृथग्विधम्।विविधाश्च पृथक्चेष्टा दैवं चैवात्र पञ्चमम्।।18.14।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>adhiṣhṭhānaṁ tathā kartā karaṇaṁ cha pṛithag-vidham<br>vividhāśh cha pṛithak cheṣhṭā daivaṁ chaivātra pañchamam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The locus, the agent, the different kinds of organs, the many and varied activities, and the divine are the fifth here.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The body, the doer, the various senses, the different functions of various kinds, and the presiding deity—the fifth.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_14.mp3]
gita_verse:18.15-16	<center><big>शरीरवाङ्मनोभिर्यत्कर्म प्रारभते नरः।न्याय्यं वा विपरीतं वा पञ्चैते तस्य हेतवः।।18.15।।<br><br>तत्रैवं सति कर्तारमात्मानं केवलं तु यः।पश्यत्यकृतबुद्धित्वान्न स पश्यति दुर्मतिः।।18.16।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śharīra-vāṅ-manobhir yat karma prārabhate naraḥ<br>nyāyyaṁ vā viparītaṁ vā pañchaite tasya hetavaḥ<br><br>tatraivaṁ sati kartāram ātmānaṁ kevalaṁ tu yaḥ<br>paśhyaty akṛita-buddhitvān na sa paśhyati durmatiḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Whatever action a person performs with their body, speech, and mind, whether it be just or its opposite, these five are the causes of it. Therefore, anyone whose intellect is imperfect and perceives the Absolute Self as the agent, does not perceive properly and has a distorted intellect.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Whatever action a person performs with their body, speech, and mind, whether right or wrong, these five are its causes. Now, such being the case, verily he who, owing to an untrained understanding, looks upon his Self, which is isolated, as the agent, he of perverted intelligence does not see.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_15-16.mp3]
gita_verse:18.17	<center><big>यस्य नाहंकृतो भावो बुद्धिर्यस्य न लिप्यते।हत्वापि स इमाँल्लोकान्न हन्ति न निबध्यते।।18.17।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yasya nāhankṛito bhāvo buddhir yasya na lipyate<br>hatvā ‘pi sa imāl lokān na hanti na nibadhyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He who has no feeling of egoism, whose intellect is untainted, he does not kill, nor does he become bound—even by killing these creatures!<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He who is free from the egoistic notion, whose intelligence is not tainted by good or evil, though he slays these people, he does not slay, nor is he bound by the action.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_17.mp3]
gita_verse:18.18	<center><big>ज्ञानं ज्ञेयं परिज्ञाता त्रिविधा कर्मचोदना।करणं कर्म कर्तेति त्रिविधः कर्मसंग्रहः।।18.18।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>jñānaṁ jñeyaṁ parijñātā tri-vidhā karma-chodanā<br>karaṇaṁ karma karteti tri-vidhaḥ karma-saṅgrahaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Knowledge, the object of knowledge, and the knower—these are the threefold inducements to action. The comprehension of actions comes under three heads: the instruments, the object, and the subject.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Knowledge, the knowable, and the knower form the threefold impulse for action; the organ, the action, and the agent form the threefold basis of action.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_18.mp3]
gita_verse:18.19	<center><big>ज्ञानं कर्म च कर्ता च त्रिधैव गुणभेदतः।प्रोच्यते गुणसंख्याने यथावच्छृणु तान्यपि।।18.19।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>jñānaṁ karma cha kartā cha tridhaiva guṇa-bhedataḥ<br>prochyate guṇa-saṅkhyāne yathāvach chhṛiṇu tāny api<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Knowledge, action, and agent are stated in the teaching about the gunas to be only of three kinds, according to the differences of the gunas. Hear about them also as they are.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Knowledge, action, and actor are declared in the science of the Gunas (Sankhya philosophy) to be of three kinds only, according to the distinction of the Gunas. Of these, hear duly.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_19.mp3]
gita_verse:18.20	<center><big>सर्वभूतेषु येनैकं भावमव्ययमीक्षते।अविभक्तं विभक्तेषु तज्ज्ञानं विद्धि सात्त्विकम्।।18.20।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sarva-bhūteṣhu yenaikaṁ bhāvam avyayam īkṣhate<br>avibhaktaṁ vibhakteṣhu taj jñānaṁ viddhi sāttvikam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Know that knowledge to originate from sattva, through which one sees a single, undecaying, undivided entity in all the diversified things.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That by which one sees the indestructible Reality in all beings, not separate in any of them—know that knowledge to be Sattvic.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_20.mp3]
gita_verse:18.21	<center><big>पृथक्त्वेन तु यज्ज्ञानं नानाभावान्पृथग्विधान्।वेत्ति सर्वेषु भूतेषु तज्ज्ञानं विद्धि राजसम्।।18.21।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>pṛithaktvena tu yaj jñānaṁ nānā-bhāvān pṛithag-vidhān<br>vetti sarveṣhu bhūteṣhu taj jñānaṁ viddhi rājasam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But know that knowledge to originate from rajas, which amidst all things apprehends the different entities of various kinds as distinct [as possessing distinct selves].<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But that knowledge which sees in all beings various entities of distinct kinds as being distinct from one another, know thou that knowledge to be Rajasic.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_21.mp3]
gita_verse:18.22	<center><big>यत्तु कृत्स्नवदेकस्मिन्कार्ये सक्तमहैतुकम्।अतत्त्वार्थवदल्पं च तत्तामसमुदाहृतम्।।18.22।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yat tu kṛitsna-vad ekasmin kārye saktam ahaitukam<br>atattvārtha-vad alpaṁ cha tat tāmasam udāhṛitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But that (knowledge) is said to be born of tamas which is confined to one form as if it were all, which is irrational, unconcerned with truth, and trivial.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But that which clings to one single effect as if it were the whole, without reason, without any foundation in Truth, and is trivial—that is declared to be Tamasic.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_22.mp3]
gita_verse:18.23	<center><big>नियतं सङ्गरहितमरागद्वेषतः कृतम्।अफलप्रेप्सुना कर्म यत्तत्सात्त्विकमुच्यते।।18.23।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>niyataṁ saṅga-rahitam arāga-dveṣhataḥ kṛitam<br>aphala-prepsunā karma yat tat sāttvikam uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The daily obligatory action which is performed without attachment and without likes or dislikes, by one who does not hanker for rewards, is said to be born of sattva.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>An action that is ordained, free from attachment, done without love or hatred, and without desire for reward is declared to be Sattvic.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_23.mp3]
gita_verse:18.24	<center><big>यत्तु कामेप्सुना कर्म साहङ्कारेण वा पुनः।क्रियते बहुलायासं तद्राजसमुदाहृतम्।।18.24।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yat tu kāmepsunā karma sāhankāreṇa vā punaḥ<br>kriyate bahulāyāsaṁ tad rājasam udāhṛitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But that action is said to be born of rajas which is done by one desirous of results or by one who is egotistical, and which is highly strenuous.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But that action which is done by one longing for the fulfillment of desires or gain with egotism or with much effort is declared to be Rajasic (passionate).<br><br>[sound:gita_18_24.mp3]
gita_verse:18.25	<center><big>अनुबन्धं क्षयं हिंसामनपेक्ष्य च पौरुषम्।मोहादारभ्यते कर्म यत्तत्तामसमुच्यते।।18.25।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>anubandhaṁ kṣhayaṁ hinsām anapekṣhya cha pauruṣham<br>mohād ārabhyate karma yat tat tāmasam uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That action is said to be born of tamas which is undertaken out of delusion, without consideration of its consequences, loss, harm, and ability.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That action which is undertaken from delusion, without regard for the consequences, loss, injury, and one's own ability, is declared to be Tamasic (dark).<br><br>[sound:gita_18_25.mp3]
gita_verse:18.26	<center><big>मुक्तसङ्गोऽनहंवादी धृत्युत्साहसमन्वितः।सिद्ध्यसिद्ध्योर्निर्विकारः कर्ता सात्त्विक उच्यते।।18.26।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>mukta-saṅgo ‘nahaṁ-vādī dhṛity-utsāha-samanvitaḥ<br>siddhy-asiddhyor nirvikāraḥ kartā sāttvika uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>[Ast. introduces this verse with 'Idanim kartrbhedah ucyate, Now is being stated the distinctions among the agents.'-Tr.] The agent who is free from attachment [Attachment to results or the idea of agentship.], not egotistical, endowed with fortitude and diligence, and unperturbed by success and failure is said to be possessed of sattva.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>An agent who is free from attachment, non-egoistic, endowed with firmness and enthusiasm, and unaffected by success or failure, is considered to be of a Sattvic (pure) nature.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_26.mp3]
gita_verse:18.27	<center><big>रागी कर्मफलप्रेप्सुर्लुब्धो हिंसात्मकोऽशुचिः।हर्षशोकान्वितः कर्ता राजसः परिकीर्तितः।।18.27।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>rāgī karma-phala-prepsur lubdho hinsātmako ‘śhuchiḥ<br>harṣha-śhokānvitaḥ kartā rājasaḥ parikīrtitaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The agent who has attachment, who is desirous of the results of actions, covetous, cruel by nature, unclean, and subject to joy and sorrow, is declared to be possessed of rajas.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Passionate, desiring to obtain the reward of their actions, greedy, cruel, impure, moved by joy and sorrow, such an agent is said to be Rajasic.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_27.mp3]
gita_verse:18.28	<center><big>अयुक्तः प्राकृतः स्तब्धः शठो नैष्कृतिकोऽलसः।विषादी दीर्घसूत्री च कर्ता तामस उच्यते।।18.28।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>ayuktaḥ prākṛitaḥ stabdhaḥ śhaṭho naiṣhkṛitiko ‘lasaḥ<br>viṣhādī dīrgha-sūtrī cha kartā tāmasa uchyate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The agent who is unsteady, naive, inflexible, deceitful, wicked, lazy, sullen, and procrastinating is said to be possessed of tamas.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Unsteady, vulgar, inflexible, deceitful, malicious, lazy, despondent, and procrastinating—such an agent is called Tamasic.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_28.mp3]
gita_verse:18.29	<center><big>बुद्धेर्भेदं धृतेश्चैव गुणतस्त्रिविधं श्रृणु।प्रोच्यमानमशेषेण पृथक्त्वेन धनञ्जय।।18.29।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>buddher bhedaṁ dhṛiteśh chaiva guṇatas tri-vidhaṁ śhṛiṇu<br>prochyamānam aśheṣheṇa pṛithaktvena dhanañjaya<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Dhananjaya, listen to the classification of the intellect and fortitude, which is threefold according to the gunas, while it is being stated in detail and separately.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Hear thou the threefold division of intellect and firmness, according to the Gunas, as I declare them fully and distinctly, O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_29.mp3]
gita_verse:18.30	<center><big>प्रवृत्तिं च निवृत्तिं च कार्याकार्ये भयाभये।बन्धं मोक्षं च या वेत्ति बुद्धिः सा पार्थ सात्त्विकी।।18.30।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>pravṛittiṁ cha nivṛittiṁ cha kāryākārye bhayābhaye<br>bandhaṁ mokṣhaṁ cha yā vetti buddhiḥ sā pārtha sāttvikī<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Partha, that intellect is born of sattva which understands action and withdrawal, duty and what is not duty, the sources of fear and fearlessness, as well as bondage and freedom.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The intellect which knows the path of work and renunciation, what should be done and what should not be done, fear and fearlessness, bondage and liberation—that intellect is Sattvic (pure), O Arjuna.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_30.mp3]
gita_verse:18.31	<center><big>यया धर्ममधर्मं च कार्यं चाकार्यमेव च।अयथावत्प्रजानाति बुद्धिः सा पार्थ राजसी।।18.31।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yayā dharmam adharmaṁ cha kāryaṁ chākāryam eva cha<br>ayathāvat prajānāti buddhiḥ sā pārtha rājasī<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Partha, that intellect is born of rajas with which one wrongly understands virtue and vice, as well as what ought to be done and ought not to be done.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That by which one wrongly understands dharma and adharma, and also what ought to be done and what ought not to be done—that intellect, O Arjuna, is rajasic (passionate).<br><br>[sound:gita_18_31.mp3]
gita_verse:18.32	<center><big>अधर्मं धर्ममिति या मन्यते तमसाऽऽवृता।सर्वार्थान्विपरीतांश्च बुद्धिः सा पार्थ तामसी।।18.32।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>adharmaṁ dharmam iti yā manyate tamasāvṛitā<br>sarvārthān viparītānśh cha buddhiḥ sā pārtha tāmasī<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Partha, that intellect is born of tamas which, being covered by darkness, considers vice as virtue, and indeed perceives all things contrary to what they are.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That intellect, O Arjuna, which is enveloped in darkness and sees Adharma as Dharma and all things perverted, is Tamasic (dark).<br><br>[sound:gita_18_32.mp3]
gita_verse:18.33	<center><big>धृत्या यया धारयते मनःप्राणेन्द्रियक्रियाः।योगेनाव्यभिचारिण्या धृतिः सा पार्थ सात्त्विकी।।18.33।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>dhṛityā yayā dhārayate manaḥ-prāṇendriya-kriyāḥ<br>yogenāvyabhichāriṇyā dhṛitiḥ sā pārtha sāttvikī<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O Partha, the firmness that is unfailing through concentration, with which one restrains the functions of the mind, vital forces, and the organs—that firmness is born of sattva.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>The unwavering firmness, through which Yoga restrains the functions of the mind, life-force, and senses—that firmness, O Arjuna, is Sattvic (pure).<br><br>[sound:gita_18_33.mp3]
gita_verse:18.34	<center><big>यया तु धर्मकामार्थान् धृत्या धारयतेऽर्जुन।प्रसङ्गेन फलाकाङ्क्षी धृतिः सा पार्थ राजसी।।18.34।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yayā tu dharma-kāmārthān dhṛityā dhārayate ‘rjuna<br>prasaṅgena phalākāṅkṣhī dhṛitiḥ sā pārtha rājasī<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>But, O Partha, the steadfastness with which one holds on to righteousness, covetable things, and wealth, desiring their fruits as the occasion for each arises, that steadfastness is born of rajas.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>But that, O Arjuna, by which one holds fast to Dharma (duty), enjoyment of pleasures, and earning of wealth, on account of attachment and desire for reward—that firmness, O Arjuna, is Rajasic (passionate).<br><br>[sound:gita_18_34.mp3]
gita_verse:18.35	<center><big>यया स्वप्नं भयं शोकं विषादं मदमेव च।न विमुञ्चति दुर्मेधा धृतिः सा पार्थ तामसी।।18.35।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yayā svapnaṁ bhayaṁ śhokaṁ viṣhādaṁ madam eva cha<br>na vimuñchati durmedhā dhṛitiḥ sā pārtha tāmasī<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That firmness is considered to be born of tamas, due to which a person with a corrupt intellect does not give up sleep, fear, sorrow, despondency, as well as sensuality.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That firmness, O Arjuna, by which a stupid man does not abandon sleep, fear, grief, despair, and conceit, is Tamasic.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_35.mp3]
gita_verse:18.36	<center><big>सुखं त्विदानीं त्रिविधं श्रृणु मे भरतर्षभ।अभ्यासाद्रमते यत्र दुःखान्तं च निगच्छति।।18.36।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sukhaṁ tv idānīṁ tri-vidhaṁ śhṛiṇu me bharatarṣhabha<br>abhyāsād ramate yatra duḥkhāntaṁ cha nigachchhati<br> yat tad agre viṣham iva pariṇāme ‘mṛitopamam<br>tat sukhaṁ sāttvikaṁ proktam ātma-buddhi-prasāda-jam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Now hear from Me, O scion of the Bharata dynasty, as regards the three kinds of joy: That in which one delights due to habit, and certainly attains the cessation of sorrows; [S. and S.S. take the second line of this verse along with the next verse referring to sattvika happiness.-Tr.]<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>And now, O Arjuna, hear from Me of the threefold pleasure, in which one rejoices through practice and surely comes to the end of pain.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_36.mp3]
gita_verse:18.37	<center><big>यत्तदग्रे विषमिव परिणामेऽमृतोपमम्।तत्सुखं सात्त्विकं प्रोक्तमात्मबुद्धिप्रसादजम्।।18.37।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yat  tad agre    viṣam   iva pariṇāme    'mṛtopamam  tat sukhaṁ  sāttvikaṁ   proktam ātma-buddhi-prasāda-jam<br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That which is like poison in the beginning, but is likened to nectar in the end, and which arises from the purity of one's intellect—that joy is spoken of as born of sattva.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That which is like poison at first but in the end like nectar—that happiness is declared to be sattvic, born of the purity of one's own mind due to self-realization.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_37.mp3]
gita_verse:18.38	<center><big>विषयेन्द्रियसंयोगाद्यत्तदग्रेऽमृतोपमम्।परिणामे विषमिव तत्सुखं राजसं स्मृतम्।।18.38।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>viṣhayendriya-sanyogād yat tad agre ’mṛitopamam<br>pariṇāme viṣham iva tat sukhaṁ rājasaṁ smṛitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That joy is referred to as born of rajas, which, arising from the contact of the organs and their objects, is like nectar in the beginning but like poison in the end.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That happiness which arises from the contact of the senses with the objects, which is initially like nectar but eventually like poison, is said to be Rajasic.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_38.mp3]
gita_verse:18.39	<center><big>यदग्रे चानुबन्धे च सुखं मोहनमात्मनः।निद्रालस्यप्रमादोत्थं तत्तामसमुदाहृतम्।।18.39।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yad agre chānubandhe cha sukhaṁ mohanam ātmanaḥ<br>nidrālasya-pramādotthaṁ tat tāmasam udāhṛitam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>That joy is said to be born of tamas, which, both in the beginning and in the end, is delusive to oneself and arises from sleep, laziness, and inadvertence.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>That happiness which at first, as well as in the end, deludes the self, and which arises from sleep, indolence, and heedlessness—that is declared to be Tamasic.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_39.mp3]
gita_verse:18.40	<center><big>न तदस्ति पृथिव्यां वा दिवि देवेषु वा पुनः।सत्त्वं प्रकृतिजैर्मुक्तं यदेभिः स्यात्ित्रभिर्गुणैः।।18.40।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>na tad asti pṛithivyāṁ vā divi deveṣhu vā punaḥ<br>sattvaṁ prakṛiti-jair muktaṁ yad ebhiḥ syāt tribhir guṇaiḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>There is no entity in the world, nor among the gods in heaven, that can be free from these three gunas born of Nature.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>There is no being on earth or in heaven among the gods that is liberated from the three qualities born of Nature.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_40.mp3]
gita_verse:18.41	<center><big>ब्राह्मणक्षत्रियविशां शूद्राणां च परंतप।कर्माणि प्रविभक्तानि स्वभावप्रभवैर्गुणैः।।18.41।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>brāhmaṇa-kṣhatriya-viśhāṁ śhūdrāṇāṁ cha parantapa<br>karmāṇi pravibhaktāni svabhāva-prabhavair guṇaiḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O scorcher of enemies, the duties of the Brahmanas, Ksatriyas, Vaisyas, and Sudras have been fully classified according to the gunas born from Nature.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Of Brahmanas, Kshatriyas, Vaisyas, and Sudras, O Arjuna, the duties are distributed according to the qualities born of their own nature.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_41.mp3]
gita_verse:18.42	<center><big>शमो दमस्तपः शौचं क्षान्तिरार्जवमेव च।ज्ञानं विज्ञानमास्तिक्यं ब्रह्मकर्म स्वभावजम्।।18.42।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhamo damas tapaḥ śhauchaṁ kṣhāntir ārjavam eva cha<br>jñānaṁ vijñānam āstikyaṁ brahma-karma svabhāva-jam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The natural duties of the Brahmanas are the control of the internal and external organs, austerity, purity, forgiveness, straightforwardness, knowledge, as well as wisdom [Knowledge refers to the understanding of subjects presented by the scriptures; wisdom means making them matters of one's own experience.], and faith.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Serenity, self-restraint, austerity, purity, forgiveness, and uprightness, as well as knowledge, realization, and belief in God, are the duties of Brahmanas, born of their own nature.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_42.mp3]
gita_verse:18.43	<center><big>शौर्यं तेजो धृतिर्दाक्ष्यं युद्धे चाप्यपलायनम्।दानमीश्वरभावश्च क्षात्रं कर्म स्वभावजम्।।18.43।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhauryaṁ tejo dhṛitir dākṣhyaṁ yuddhe chāpy apalāyanam<br>dānam īśhvara-bhāvaśh cha kṣhātraṁ karma svabhāva-jam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The natural duties of the Ksatriyas are heroism, boldness, fortitude, capability, and not retreating from battle, generosity, and lordliness.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Prowess, splendor, firmness, dexterity, and not fleeing from battle, generosity, and lordliness are the duties of the Kshatriyas, born of their own nature.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_43.mp3]
gita_verse:18.44	<center><big>कृषिगौरक्ष्यवाणिज्यं वैश्यकर्म स्वभावजम्।परिचर्यात्मकं कर्म शूद्रस्यापि स्वभावजम्।।18.44।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>kṛiṣhi-gau-rakṣhya-vāṇijyaṁ vaiśhya-karma svabhāva-jam<br>paricharyātmakaṁ karma śhūdrasyāpi svabhāva-jam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>The natural duties of the Vaisyas are agriculture, cattle-rearing, and trading. gita_verse:18.45	<center><big>स्वे स्वे कर्मण्यभिरतः संसिद्धिं लभते नरः।स्वकर्मनिरतः सिद्धिं यथा विन्दति तच्छृणु।।18.45।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sve sve karmaṇy abhirataḥ sansiddhiṁ labhate naraḥ<br>sva-karma-nirataḥ siddhiṁ yathā vindati tach chhṛiṇu<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Being devoted to his own duty, one attains complete success. gita_verse:18.46	<center><big>यतः प्रवृत्तिर्भूतानां येन सर्वमिदं ततम्।स्वकर्मणा तमभ्यर्च्य सिद्धिं विन्दति मानवः।।18.46।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yataḥ pravṛittir bhūtānāṁ yena sarvam idaṁ tatam<br>sva-karmaṇā tam abhyarchya siddhiṁ vindati mānavaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>A human being achieves success by adoring, through his own duties, Him from whom is the origin of creatures and by whom all this is pervaded.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He from whom all the beings have evolved and by whom all this is pervaded, worshipping Him with his own duty, one attains perfection.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_46.mp3]
gita_verse:18.47	<center><big>श्रेयान्स्वधर्मो विगुणः परधर्मात्स्वनुष्ठितात्।स्वभावनियतं कर्म कुर्वन्नाप्नोति किल्बिषम्।।18.47।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>śhreyān swa-dharmo viguṇaḥ para-dharmāt sv-anuṣhṭhitāt<br>svabhāva-niyataṁ karma kurvan nāpnoti kilbiṣham<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One's own duty, though defective, is superior to another's duty well performed. gita_verse:18.48	<center><big>सहजं कर्म कौन्तेय सदोषमपि न त्यजेत्।सर्वारम्भा हि दोषेण धूमेनाग्निरिवावृताः।।18.48।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>saha-jaṁ karma kaunteya sa-doṣham api na tyajet<br>sarvārambhā hi doṣheṇa dhūmenāgnir ivāvṛitāḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O son of Kunti, one should not give up the duty to which one is born, even though it be imperfect. gita_verse:18.49	<center><big>असक्तबुद्धिः सर्वत्र जितात्मा विगतस्पृहः।नैष्कर्म्यसिद्धिं परमां संन्यासेनाधिगच्छति।।18.49।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>asakta-buddhiḥ sarvatra jitātmā vigata-spṛihaḥ<br>naiṣhkarmya-siddhiṁ paramāṁ sannyāsenādhigachchhati<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>He whose intellect remains unattached to everything, who has conquered his internal organs and is desireless, attains through monasticism the supreme perfection consisting of the state of one free from duties.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>He whose intellect is unattached everywhere, who has subdued his self, from whom desire has fled, he attains the supreme state of freedom from action through renunciation.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_49.mp3]
gita_verse:18.50	<center><big>सिद्धिं प्राप्तो यथा ब्रह्म तथाप्नोति निबोध मे।समासेनैव कौन्तेय निष्ठा ज्ञानस्य या परा।।18.50।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>siddhiṁ prāpto yathā brahma tathāpnoti nibodha me<br>samāsenaiva kaunteya niṣhṭhā jñānasya yā parā<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Understand for certain from Me, in brief indeed, O son of Kunti, that process by which one who has achieved success attains Brahman, which is the supreme consummation of knowledge.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Learn from Me, O Arjuna, in brief how one who has attained perfection reaches Brahman—the Eternal, that supreme state of knowledge.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_50.mp3]
gita_verse:18.51-53	<center><big>बुद्ध्या विशुद्धया युक्तो धृत्याऽऽत्मानं नियम्य च।शब्दादीन् विषयांस्त्यक्त्वा रागद्वेषौ व्युदस्य च।।18.51।।<br><br>विविक्तसेवी लघ्वाशी यतवाक्कायमानसः।ध्यानयोगपरो नित्यं वैराग्यं समुपाश्रितः।।18.52।।<br><br>अहङ्कारं बलं दर्पं कामं क्रोधं परिग्रहम्।विमुच्य निर्ममः शान्तो ब्रह्मभूयाय कल्पते।।18.53।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>buddhyā viśhuddhayā yukto dhṛityātmānaṁ niyamya cha<br>śhabdādīn viṣhayāns tyaktvā rāga-dveṣhau vyudasya cha<br><br>vivikta-sevī laghv-āśhī yata-vāk-kāya-mānasaḥ<br>dhyāna-yoga-paro nityaṁ vairāgyaṁ samupāśhritaḥ<br><br>ahankāraṁ balaṁ darpaṁ kāmaṁ krodhaṁ parigraham<br>vimuchya nirmamaḥ śhānto brahma-bhūyāya kalpate<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Endowed with a pure intellect and controlling oneself with fortitude, one should reject the objects beginning from sound [sound, touch, form, color, taste, and smell - Tr.] and eliminate attachment and hatred. One who resorts to solitude, eats sparingly, has control over their speech, body, and mind, for whom meditation and concentration are ever the highest duty, and who is possessed of dispassion; Having discarded egotism, force, pride, desire, anger, and superfluous possessions, and being free from the idea of possession and serene, that person is fit for becoming Brahman.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Endowed with a pure intellect, controlling the self through firmness, relinquishing sound and other objects and abandoning attraction and hatred. Dwelling in solitude, eating sparingly, with speech, body, and mind subdued, always engaged in meditation and concentration, and resorting to dispassion. Having abandoned egoism, strength, arrogance, desire, anger, and covetousness, and being free from the notion of 'mine' and peaceful, he is fit for becoming Brahman.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_51-53.mp3]
gita_verse:18.54	<center><big>ब्रह्मभूतः प्रसन्नात्मा न शोचति न काङ्क्षति।समः सर्वेषु भूतेषु मद्भक्तिं लभते पराम्।।18.54।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>brahma-bhūtaḥ prasannātmā na śhochati na kāṅkṣhati<br>samaḥ sarveṣhu bhūteṣhu mad-bhaktiṁ labhate parām<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>One who has become Brahman and has attained the blissful Self does not grieve nor desire. gita_verse:18.55	<center><big>भक्त्या मामभिजानाति यावान्यश्चास्मि तत्त्वतः।ततो मां तत्त्वतो ज्ञात्वा विशते तदनन्तरम्।।18.55।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>bhaktyā mām abhijānāti yāvān yaśh chāsmi tattvataḥ<br>tato māṁ tattvato jñātvā viśhate tad-anantaram<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Through devotion, he knows Me in reality, as to what and who I am. gita_verse:18.74	<center><big>सञ्जय उवाचइत्यहं वासुदेवस्य पार्थस्य च महात्मनः।संवादमिममश्रौषमद्भुतं रोमहर्षणम्।।18.74।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>sañjaya uvācha<br>ity ahaṁ vāsudevasya pārthasya cha mahātmanaḥ<br>saṁvādam imam aśhrauṣham adbhutaṁ roma-harṣhaṇam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Sanjaya said, "I thus heard this conversation between Vasudeva and the great-souled Partha, which is unique and makes one's hair stand on end."<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Sanjaya said, Thus, I have heard this wonderful dialogue between Krishna and the high-souled Arjuna, which causes one's hair to stand on end.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_74.mp3]
gita_verse:18.75	<center><big>व्यासप्रसादाच्छ्रुतवानेतद्गुह्यमहं परम्।योगं योगेश्वरात्कृष्णात्साक्षात्कथयतः स्वयम्।।18.75।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>vyāsa-prasādāch chhrutavān etad guhyam ahaṁ param<br>yogaṁ yogeśhvarāt kṛiṣhṇāt sākṣhāt kathayataḥ svayam<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Through the favor of Vyasa, I heard this secret concerning the supreme Yoga from Krishna, the Lord of Yogas, while He Himself was speaking!<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Through the grace of Vyasa, I have heard this supreme and most secret Yoga, directly from Krishna, the Lord of Yoga, Himself declaring it.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_75.mp3]
gita_verse:18.76	<center><big>राजन्संस्मृत्य संस्मृत्य संवादमिममद्भुतम्।केशवार्जुनयोः पुण्यं हृष्यामि च मुहुर्मुहुः।।18.76।।</big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>rājan sansmṛitya sansmṛitya saṁvādam imam adbhutam<br>keśhavārjunayoḥ puṇyaṁ hṛiṣhyāmi cha muhur muhuḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>And, O King, while repeatedly remembering this unique, sacred dialogue between Kesava and Arjuna, I rejoice every moment.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>O King, remembering this wonderful and holy dialogue between Krishna and Arjuna, I continually rejoice.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_76.mp3]
gita_verse:18.77	<center><big>तच्च संस्मृत्य संस्मृत्य रूपमत्यद्भुतं हरेः।<br><br>विस्मयो मे महान् राजन् हृष्यामि च पुनः पुनः।।18.77।।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>tach cha sansmṛitya saṁsmṛitya rūpam aty-adbhutaṁ hareḥ<br>vismayo ye mahān rājan hṛiṣhyāmi cha punaḥ punaḥ<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>O King, repeatedly recollecting that greatly extraordinary form of Hari, I am struck with wonder and rejoice again and again.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>And, remembering again and again that most wonderful form of Hari, I am filled with great wonder, O King; and I rejoice again and again.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_77.mp3]
gita_verse:18.78	<center><big>यत्र योगेश्वरः कृष्णो यत्र पार्थो धनुर्धरः।<br><br>तत्र श्रीर्विजयो भूतिर्ध्रुवा नीतिर्मतिर्मम।।18.78।<br> </big></center>	<b>IAST:</b><br>yatra yogeśhvaraḥ kṛiṣhṇo yatra pārtho dhanur-dharaḥ<br>tatra śhrīr vijayo bhūtir dhruvā nītir matir mama<br><br><br><b>Literal — Gambirananda:</b><br>Where there is Krishna, the Lord of yogas, and where there is Partha, the wielder of the bow, there is fortune, victory, prosperity, and unfailing prudence. Such is my conviction.<br><br><b>Devotional — Sivananda:</b><br>Wherever Krishna, the Lord of Yoga, is; and wherever Arjuna, the wielder of the bow, is; there is prosperity, victory, happiness, and a firm policy; this is my conviction.<br><br>[sound:gita_18_78.mp3]
